Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Who Bears the Ghurrah for Miscarriage: The 'Aqilah or the Offender?
Dispute on whether ghurrah is paid by 'aqilah or offender

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on who bears the ghurrah for miscarriage and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the relevant proofs.

Core Idea
Ghurrah is upon the 'aqilah because it is compensation for a life (nafs), not a part.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a key ikhtilaf in the chapter of diyat: who is liable to pay the ghurrah when a woman miscarries due to an assault? The Hanafi school holds that the 'aqilah (paternal relatives) must pay when the amount is five hundred dirhams, while Imam Malik places the liability on the offender individually. The disagreement hinges on whether the fetus is considered a distinct life or a part of the mother, and on the interpretation of the prophetic ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling of the Hanafi school: the ghurrah is wajib on the 'aqilah when it amounts to five hundred dirhams. Note the condition of the amount.
The text specifies 'indana' (according to us) and adds the condition 'idha kanat khams mi'at dirham'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that the ghurrah is paid from the offender's own wealth, not by the 'aqilah. Understand his reasoning: the fetus is a part (juz') of the mother, so compensation is for a part, analogous to a wound less than five hundred dirhams.
Maliki view is stated as 'fi malihi' (in his wealth).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Maliki dalil: the fetus is a part, so the ghurrah is a substitute for a part (badal al-juz'), and the rule for wounds (jarh) less than five hundred dirhams is that they are on the offender. Therefore, ghurrah should also be on the offender.
The text says 'li'annahu badal al-juz'' (because it is a substitute for a part).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: (1) the prophetic judgment (qada) explicitly placed the ghurrah on the 'aqilah; (2) the ghurrah is a substitute for a life (nafs), not a part, because the fetus is considered a distinct life (nafs). Hence it is called diyah, and diyah is upon the 'aqilah.
The text cites the hadith 'qada bil-ghurrah 'ala al-'aqilah' and the term 'diyah' used by the Prophet.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, the 'aqilah pays; in the Maliki school, the offender pays personally. This affects who bears the financial burden.
The tarjih (preferred view) in the Hanafi school is the Hanafi position.

غرہ کس پر لازم ہے عاقلہ پر یا اس کے اپنے مال میں
وهو على العاقلة عندنا اذا كانت خمس مائة درهم و قال مالک فی ماله لانه بدل الجزء ولنا انه عليه السلام قضى بالغرة على العاقلة ولانه بدل النفس ولهذا سماه عليه السلام دية حيث قال دوه و قالوا اندی لا صاح ولا استهل الحديث الا ان العواقل لا تحقل ما دون خمس مائة
ترجمہ اور یہ ( غرہ) ہمارے نزدیک عاقلہ پر ہے جب کہ پانچو درہم ہو اور مالک نے فرمایا کہ اس کے مال میں ہے، اس لئے کہ یہ جز کا بدل ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نبی علیہ السّلام نے غرہ کا فیصلہ عاقلہ پر فرمایا اور اس لئے کہ یہ ( غرہ) نفس ( جنین ) کا بدل ہے اسی وجدت نبی علیہ السلام نے اس کا نام دیت رکھا اس حیثیت سے کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس کی دیت ادا کرو اور انہوں نے کہا کہ کیا ہم دیت ادا کریں اس کی جو نہ چلایا اور نہ روی ( الحدیث ) مگر عواقل پانچسو درہم سے کم کی دیت نہیں دیتے۔ تشریح . اب سوال یہ پیدا ہوا کہ غرہ کون ادا کرے خود ضارب یا عاقلہ تو فرمایا کہ ہمارے نزدیک غرہ عاقلہ پر واجب ہے اور امام مالک کے نزدیک ضارب پر انہوں نے یہ دلیل دی ہے کہ جنین تو ماں کا جز ہے تو یہ غرہ ماں کا جزء فوت کرنے کی وجہ سے اجب کیا گیا ہے۔ اور جوارش مادون النفس میں ہوتا ہے وہ عاقلہ پر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ خود مجرم پر واجب ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں کا غرہ بھی مجرم پر واجب ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل ... ایک تو حدیث ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے غرہ عاقلہ پر واجب فرمایا ہے اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غرو نفس کا بدل ہے اور نفس کے بدل کو دیت کہتے ہیں اور حدیث میں اس کو دیت کہا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ ایسا واقعہ پیش آنے پر نبی علیہ السلام نے فرمایا تھا کہ اس کی دیت ادا کرو، انہوں نے کہا تھا کہ اس کی دیت کیسے ادا کریں یہ تو نہ بولا نہ رویا (الحدیث) بہر حال حدیث میں اس کو دیت کہا جا رہا ہے تو اس کا وجوب حسب دستور عاقلہ پر ہی ہوگا۔ اور یہ اصول پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ جوارش پانچسو درہم سے کم ہو اس کا وجوب خود مجرم پر ہو گا عاقلہ پر نہ ہوگا اور یہاں جوغرہ واجب ہوا ہے وہ پانچسو درہم ہی ہے۔ تنبیہ یہاں جوغرہ واجب ہوا ہے وہ پانچ سو درہم ہیں جیسے ماقبل میں گزرا اس لئے یہاں عندنا کے بعد اذا كانت خمس مائة درہم کی قید بر حمل نہیں ہے۔ یاممکن ہے کہ یہ اذا کے بجائے از ہو اس وقت اس میں گنجائش ہے کہ وجوب علی العاقلہ کی دلیل ہو کہ عاقلہ پر وجوب کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ یہ پانچ سو درہم ہیں جس کا وجوب عاقلہ پر ہوتا ہے۔ تنبیہودگی ، یدی ، ودیا ، ددینڈ ، خون بہانا امر کے صیغے یہ ہیں، یہ دیا ، دوا، دی، دیا دین تو یہاں دُوه : مفعول به
Book of Diyat. For detailed discussion on these two hadith, see Nasb al-Rayah vol. 4 p. 381. Upon whom is the ghurrah obligatory, upon the 'aqilah or in his own wealth? It is upon the 'aqilah according to us when it is five hundred dirhams. Malik said: In his wealth, because it is a substitute for a part. Our proof: The Prophet (peace be upon him) judged the ghurrah upon the 'aqilah, and because it is a substitute for the life (nafs), thus the Prophet called it diyah when he said: 'Pay its diyah.' They said: 'Shall we pay diyah for one who neither cried nor screamed?' (The hadith) except that the 'aqilah do not bear what is less than five hundred dirhams. Translation: And this (ghurrah) according to us is upon the 'aqilah when it is five hundred dirhams, and Malik ruled that it is in his wealth, because it is a substitute for a part. Our proof: One is the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged the ghurrah upon the 'aqilah, and the second proof is that it is a substitute for the life (nafs), and the substitute for life is called diyah, and in the hadith it was called diyah. Because when such an incident occurred, the Prophet said: 'Pay its diyah.' They said: 'How can we pay diyah for one who neither spoke nor cried?' (The hadith). In any case, in the hadith it is called diyah, so its obligation according to the practice is upon the 'aqilah. And the principle has passed before that when the jarh (wound) is less than five hundred dirhams, its obligation is upon the criminal himself, not upon the 'aqilah. And here the ghurrah that is obligatory is five hundred dirhams. Note: The ghurrah that is obligatory here is five hundred dirhams as passed before, so here after 'indana' the condition 'idha kanat khams mi'at dirham' is not superfluous. Or it may be that it is 'idh' instead of 'idha', in which case there is room that it is proof of obligation upon the 'aqilah: why is it obligatory upon the 'aqilah? Because it is five hundred dirhams, which is what is obligatory upon the 'aqilah. Note: Wudghi, yadi, wadiya, dand, khun bahana – these are imperative forms: diya, dawa, di, diya din, so here 'duhu' is maf'ul bihi.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the obligation of ghurrah (compensation for causing a miscarriage), specifically who is liable to pay it. The text opens with a definition and a statement of the Hanafi position: the ghurrah is upon the 'aqilah (the paternal relatives responsible for blood money) when it amounts to five hundred dirhams. This is based on a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged the ghurrah to be on the 'aqilah. The passage then contrasts the view of Imam Malik, who holds that it is upon the offender himself, reasoning that the fetus is a part of the mother, so the compensation is for a part (juz'), not for a whole life, and thus follows the rule of wounds (jurh) which are paid by the offender if less than five hundred dirhams. The Hanafi response counters that the ghurrah is a substitute for a life (nafs), as the fetus is considered a distinct life, and thus it is called diyah (blood money) in the hadith. Since diyah is upon the 'aqilah, so is ghurrah. The text further notes a principle: wounds (jarh) that are less than five hundred dirhams are obligatory on the offender, not the 'aqilah. Since ghurrah is exactly five hundred dirhams, it falls within the scope of the 'aqilah. A linguistic note at the end clarifies the imperative forms of the word 'diyah' used in the hadith.

Key Terms
غرہ (ghurrah): Compensation paid for causing a miscarriage; specifically 500 dirhams.
عاقلہ ('aqilah): The paternal relatives of the offender who bear responsibility for paying diyah or ghurrah.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid for taking a life; ghurrah is considered a type of diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is liable to pay the ghurrah for miscarriage?
A) The offender himself
B) The 'aqilah (paternal relatives) when the amount is 500 dirhams
C) The mother's family
D) The state treasury

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah for miscarriage is wajib on the 'aqilah in the Hanafi school because the prophetic judgment and analogy to diyah place it on the paternal relatives.

Payment Period for Ghurrah: One Year vs Three Years
Dispute on ghurrah payment period between Hanafi and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the ghurrah payment period and explain the dual-resemblance argument (shabahayn) that distinguishes it from full diyah.

Core Idea
The ghurrah is paid in one year because it resembles both life and limb; payment follows limb, inheritance follows life.

The ghurrah is a fixed compensation for causing a miscarriage. A key practical question is over how many years this amount must be paid. The Hanafi school holds one year, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues for three years, equating it to full diyah. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning, which uses a dual-resemblance analogy: the ghurrah is inherited like a life-substitute, but its payment period follows the rules for limb compensation because the fetus is connected to the mother.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and the opposing view
Identify that the Hanafi school rules ghurrah is wajib in one year on the 'aqilah. Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds it should be in three years, like diyah.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in payment schedule.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Understand the Shafi'i dalil: ghurrah is a substitute for life (badal al-nafs) because it is inherited by the fetus's heirs, unlike limb compensation (arsh) which goes to the victim. Therefore, it should follow diyah rules of three-year installments.
The key indicator is tawrith (inheritance).
3
Analyze the Hanafi naqli proof
The Hanafis cite a report from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan that the Prophet (ﷺ) placed the ghurrah on the 'aqilah in one year. This is a direct textual evidence (dalil naqli) for the one-year period.
Though the report is ahad and zanni, it is relied upon in the absence of stronger proof.
4
Trace the Hanafi qiyas argument
The Hanafis argue that the ghurrah has a dual nature: from one perspective it is a substitute for a separate life (hence inherited), but from another it is a substitute for a limb because the fetus is physically connected to the mother. They apply the resemblance of life for inheritance (tawrith), and the resemblance of limb for the payment period (one year). The rule for limb compensation: when the amount is between half of a tenth (1/20) and one-third of diyah, it is paid in one year. The ghurrah (500 dirhams or equivalent) falls within that range.
This is a sophisticated application of shabah (resemblance) to resolve conflicting analogies.
5
Address the objection about diyah parts
The text raises an objection: if multiple killers each pay a share of diyah that is half of a tenth, why isn't that paid in one year? The Hanafi answer: the principle of one year applies to substitutes for limbs, not for life. In collective killing, each pays a part of diyah which is still a life-substitute, so three years applies.
This clarifies the scope of the analogy: it is specific to ghurrah's unique dual nature.

و تجب في سنة و قال الشافعى فى ثلث سنين لانه بدل النفس ولهذا يكون موروثا بين ورثته و لنا ماروی عن محمد بن الحسن انه قال بلغنا ان رسول الله عليه السلام جعل على العاقلة في سنة ولانه ان كان بدل النفس من حيث انه نفس على حدة فهو بدل العضو من حيث الاتصال بالام فعملنا بالشبه الأول في حق التوريث وبالثاني في حق التاجيل الى سنة لان بدل العضو اذا كان ثلث الدية او اقل اكثر من نصف العشر يجب في سنة بخلاف اجزاء الدية لان كل جزء منها على من وجب يجب في ثلث سنين
ترجمہ اور غزہ ایک سال میں واجب ہوگا اور شافعی نے فرمایا تین سالوں میں اس لئے کہ یہ نفس کا بدل ہے اسی وجہ سے یہ جنین کے ورثا کے درمیان میراث میں تقسیم ہوتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل وہ ہے جو محمد بن حسن سے مروی ہے انہوں نے کہا کہ ہم کو یہ بات پہنچی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے غرہ کو عاقلہ پر ایک سال میں قرار دیا ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ (غرہ) علیحدہ نفس ہونے کی وجہ سے اگر چہ بدل نفس ہے پس وہ ماں کے ساتھ اتصال کی وجہ سے عضو کا بدل ہے تو ہم نے توریث کے حق میں پہلی مشابہت پر عمل کیا اور سال بھر مہلت دینے کے حق میں دوسری مشابہت پر عمل کیا اس لئے کہ عضو کا بدل جب کہ وہ تہائی دیت یا کم ہو یعنی نصف عشر سے زیادہ تو وہ بدل ایک سال میں واجب ہوتا ہے بخلاف دیت کے اجزاء کے اس لئے کہ دیت کا ہر جز جس پر واجب ہوتا ہے وہ تین سال میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح اب یہ سوال پیدا ہوا کہ مر کی ادائیگی کا طریقہ ہوگا؟ تو اس میں اختلاف ہے امام شافعی کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ اس کی ادائیگی دبیت کے مثل تین سال میں ہوگی۔ اور حنیفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ ایک سال میں ادا ئیگی کرنی ہوگی۔
دلیل شافی یہ ہے کہ غر نفس کا بدل ہے اور اصول یہ ہے کہ جو مال نفس کا بدل ہو اس کی ادائیگی قسطوار تین سال میں واجب ہوتی ہے لہذا یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہئے ۔ اور اس کہ دلیل کہ غرہ نفس کا بدل ہے یہ بھی ہے کہ غرہ توجنین کے ورثا کے درمیان تقسیم جاتا ہے اور اطراف کے ارش کو ورثا کے درمیان تقسیم نہیں کیا جا تا بلکہ وہ مظلوم کو دیا جاتا ہے۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ غرہ نفس کا بدل نفس ہے اور جب یہ بدل نفس ہے تو حسب قانون دیت اس کی ادائی کی تین سال میں ہوگی۔ ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل اولا تو یہ ہے کہ امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ ہم تک یہ بات پہنچی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے غرہ کو عا قلہ پر ایک سال میں ادا کرنے کا فیصلہ فرمایا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جنین ایک اعتبار سے علیحدہ نفس ہے اور دوسرے اعتبار سے ماں کے ساتھ متصل ہونے کی وجہ سے عضو ہے لہذا غرہ کے اندر بھی دو احتمال ہو گئے۔

سوال ایک شخص کو میں آدمیوں نے حطاقتل کر دیا تو ان کے حصہ میں جو ریت آرہی ہے وہ بھی نصف عشر ہے لہذا اس کی ادائیگی بھی آپ کے اصول کے مطابق ایک سال میں ہونی چاہئے حالانکہ بالا تفاق اس کی ادائیگی تین سالوں میں واجب ہوتی ہے؟ جواب ... ہم نے جو اصول پیش کیا ہے یہ بدل عضو کا ہے اور یہاں بدل نفس ے لیکن شرکاء کے تکثر کی وجہ سے دیت کے اجزاء
Method of payment of ghurrah, statements of jurists. And it is obligatory in one year, and al-Shafi'i said in three years, because it is a substitute for life, and therefore it is inherited among his heirs. Our proof: what is narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan that he said: It has reached us that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) placed the ghurrah upon the 'aqilah in one year. And because, although it is a substitute for life in that it is a separate life, it is a substitute for a limb in terms of its connection with the mother. So we acted upon the first resemblance in the matter of inheritance, and upon the second in the matter of deferment to one year. Because a substitute for a limb, when it is one-third of the diyah or less but more than half of a tenth, is obligatory in one year, unlike the parts of diyah, because each part of it, upon whomever it is obligatory, is obligatory in three years. Translation: And the ghurrah is obligatory in one year, and al-Shafi'i said in three years, because it is a substitute for life, and therefore it is inherited among the heirs of the fetus. Our proof is what is narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan that he said: It has reached us that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) placed the ghurrah upon the 'aqilah in one year. And because, although it is a substitute for life in that it is a separate life, it is a substitute for a limb in terms of its connection with the mother. So we acted upon the first resemblance in the matter of inheritance, and upon the second in the matter of deferment to one year. Because a substitute for a limb, when it is one-third of the diyah or less but more than half of a tenth, is obligatory in one year, unlike the parts of diyah, because each part of it, upon whomever it is obligatory, is obligatory in three years. Explanation: Now the question arose as to the method of payment of the ghurrah. There is a difference of opinion: Imam al-Shafi'i's position is that its payment, like diyah, will be in three years. Abu Hanifa's position is that it must be paid in one year. Al-Shafi'i's proof: the ghurrah is a substitute for life, and the principle is that wealth which is a substitute for life is obligatory to be paid in installments over three years, so here also it should be the same. And another proof that ghurrah is a substitute for life is that ghurrah is distributed among the heirs of the fetus, whereas arsh (compensation for limbs) is not distributed among heirs but is given to the victim. Therefore, it is known that ghurrah is a substitute for life. And when it is a substitute for life, according to the law of diyah, its payment will be in three years. Abu Hanifa's proof: first, it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that we have received that the Prophet (peace be upon him) decided that the ghurrah be paid by the 'aqilah in one year. Second, the fetus from one perspective is a separate life, and from another perspective, due to its connection with the mother, it is a limb. So in the ghurrah, there are two possibilities: (1) substitute for a limb, (2) substitute for life. We acted upon both resemblances: we declared ghurrah inheritable due to its being a substitute for life, and we granted a deferment of one year due to its being a substitute for a limb. What does this mean? It means that a substitute for a limb, provided it is not less than half of a tenth, has a deferment of one year. And this (ghurrah) is also not less than half of a tenth, and it is a substitute from one aspect, so a one-year deferment should be given. Objection: If one person is killed by multiple people, the share of each in the diyah is also half of a tenth, so according to your principle, it should be paid in one year, whereas by consensus it is obligatory in three years. Answer: The principle we presented is for a substitute for a limb, and here it is a substitute for life, but due to the multiplicity of participants, the parts of diyah...
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage addresses the method of payment for the ghurrah, specifically the time period over which it must be paid. The Hanafi ruling is that the ghurrah is obligatory in one year, not three. The text presents the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues for three years on the basis that the ghurrah is a substitute for life (nafs), and substitutes for life (like full diyah) are paid over three years. He supports this by noting that ghurrah is inherited by the heirs of the fetus, whereas compensation for limbs (arsh) is not inherited. The Hanafi response uses two proofs. First, a report from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) set the ghurrah on the 'aqilah to be paid in one year. Second, an analogical reasoning: although the ghurrah is a substitute for life (as a separate life), it also has characteristics of a substitute for a limb because the fetus is connected to the mother. Therefore, the Hanafi school applies one resemblance for inheritance (it is inherited because it is like a life) and another resemblance for payment period (one year, because limb compensation for amounts between half of a tenth and one-third of diyah is paid in one year). The ghurrah falls within this range. The passage also addresses an objection: if multiple persons kill one person, each pays a share of diyah that is also half of a tenth, yet the payment period is three years by consensus. The answer is that the principle of one year applies to substitutes for limbs, not for life; in the case of collective killing, the diyah is still a substitute for life, so the three-year period applies.

Key Terms
غرہ (ghurrah): Compensation for miscarriage, here discussed regarding payment period.
توریث (tawrith): Inheritance; the ghurrah is inherited by the fetus's heirs, indicating it is a substitute for life.
بدل العضو (badal al-'udw): Substitute for a limb; here used to determine the payment period of one year for amounts between half of tenth and one-third of diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which proof is cited for the one-year payment period of ghurrah?
A) A Quranic verse on diyah
B) A report from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan that the Prophet set it in one year
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to full diyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that ghurrah is paid in one year, using a dual-resemblance analogy: inheritance follows life, payment period follows limb.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate

Dispute on Payment Period of Ghurrah
Dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on payment period of ghurrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that ghurrah is paid in one year and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the dual-analogy reasoning.

Core Idea
The ghurrah is paid in one year, not three, because the Prophet explicitly decreed it and the fetus is both a life and a limb.

This passage presents the classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the time period for paying ghurrah—the compensation for a miscarried fetus. The Shafi'i school argues that ghurrah, being a substitute for a life, should follow the full diyah rule of three-year installments. The Hanafi school counters with a prophetic decree (hadith) and a nuanced dual-analogy that treats the fetus as both a separate life and a part of the mother's body.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and both positions
Identify the contested ruling: the payment period for ghurrah. Hanafi: one year. Shafi'i: three years.
2
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i proof: ghurrah is a substitute for a life (badal nafs). Evidence: it is inherited by the fetus's heirs, unlike limb compensation. Full diyah for a life is paid in three years, so ghurrah should be as well.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response – explicit hadith
First, the Hanafi cite a hadith narrated by Muhammad al-Shaybani: the Prophet decreed ghurrah to be paid in one year. This explicit text takes precedence over analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response – dual analogy
Second, the dual-analogy: the fetus from one perspective is a separate life (so inheritable), but from another perspective it is a limb of the mother (so payment period follows limb compensation rules). Under Hanafi law, compensation for a limb that is at least half of one-tenth (nisf 'ushr) of the full diyah is due in one year. Since ghurrah equals nisf 'ushr (500 dirhams), it falls under this rule.
5
Apply to a potential objection
Consider the objection: if several men accidentally kill a person, each paying a share equal to nisf 'ushr, that share would not be paid in one year but in three by consensus. The Hanafi respond: the principle of one-year applies to limb substitutes; here the payment is for life, but because of multiple participants it becomes parts of diyah (ajza al-diyah), which are always in three years. This is a distinction (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Translation: And ghurrah is obligatory to be paid in one year, and al-Shafi'i said in three years because it is a substitute for life, and for that reason it is distributed among the heirs of the fetus. And our proof is what is narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan: he said that it reached us that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) decreed the ghurrah to be paid by the 'aqila in one year. And because this (ghurrah), due to being a separate life, even though it is a substitute for life, but due to its connection with the mother it is a substitute for a limb. So we acted upon the first similarity regarding inheritance and upon the second similarity regarding postponement to one year, because the substitute for a limb, when it is one-third of the diyah or less, meaning more than nisf 'ushr, then that substitute is obligatory in one year, unlike the parts of the diyah because each part of the diyah on whom it is obligatory is obligatory in three years. Explanation: Now a question arises about the method of payment of ghurrah? There is a dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i's position is that its payment is similar to diyah, in three years. And Abu Hanifa's position is that payment must be made in one year. The proof of al-Shafi'i is that ghurrah is a substitute for life, and the principle is that wealth which is a substitute for life is paid in installments over three years, so here also it should be similarly. And another proof that ghurrah is a substitute for life is that ghurrah is divided among the heirs of the fetus, whereas compensation for limbs is not divided among heirs but is given to the victim. Therefore, it is known that ghurrah is a substitute for life, and when it is a substitute for life, then according to the law of diyah, its payment should be in three years. Abu Hanifa's proof: first, it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that it reached us that the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed that the ghurrah be paid by the 'aqila in one year. Second proof: the fetus is from one aspect a separate life and from another aspect, due to connection with the mother, a limb. Hence, regarding ghurrah, two probabilities exist: (1) substitute for a limb, (2) substitute for life. So we acted upon both similarities: we declared ghurrah to be inherited due to being a substitute for life, and we gave a postponement of one year due to it being a substitute for a limb. What is meant? The meaning is that if something is a substitute for a limb, provided it is not less than nisf 'ushr, then it is given a postponement of one year, and this ghurrah is also not less than nisf 'ushr, and from one perspective it is a substitute for a limb, so it deserves a postponement of one year. Question: If a person is killed by mistake by several men, and the share of each in the diyah is also nisf 'ushr, then according to your principle its payment should be in one year, whereas by consensus its payment is obligatory in three years? Answer: The principle we presented is for substitute of a limb, and here it is substitute for life, but due to multiplicity of participants, the diyah becomes parts, so this analogy is invalid. Note: 'Or less, more than nisf 'ushr' means the substitute for less is more; the commentators have objected that the condition 'more' is not needed because even in the case of nisf 'ushr the obligation is in one year, so the qualification 'more' is useless. But it can be said that the author says: one-third and less, the amount that is more than nisf 'ushr, in that the obligation is in one year, so in the case of nisf 'ushr also the obligation will be in one year.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the payment period of ghurrah (compensation for a miscarried fetus). The Shafi'i school argues that ghurrah, being a substitute for a human life, should be paid in three years like full diyah. They support this by noting that ghurrah is inherited by the fetus's heirs, unlike limb compensation which goes only to the victim. The Hanafi school counters with two proofs. First, an actual hadith narrated by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically decreed ghurrah to be paid in one year. Second, a dual-analogy reasoning: the fetus from one angle is a separate life (so the payment is inheritable as a life-substitute), but from another angle it is a part of the mother's body (so the payment period follows the rules for limb compensation). Under Hanafi rules, compensation for a limb that is at least half of one-tenth of full diyah is due in one year. Since ghurrah (500 dirhams) equals nisf 'ushr, it falls under this rule. The Hanafi position is considered mufta bihi because it is based on an explicit prophetic decree and the nuanced legal reasoning that gives effect to both aspects of the fetus's nature.

Key Terms
غرہ (ghurrah): Compensation for a miscarried fetus; consists of a slave or five hundred dirhams.
نصف عشر (nisf 'ushr): Half of one-tenth of the full diyah, i.e., 50 dinars or 500 dirhams.
عاقلہ ('aqila): The male paternal relatives of the perpetrator who are jointly responsible for paying diyah in cases of accidental homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Qiyas on limb compensation
C) An explicit hadith from Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) The Quranic verse on diyat

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah is wajib in one year because the Prophet explicitly decreed it, and the fetus's dual nature allows simultaneous application of inheritance rules (life-substitute) and payment rules (limb-substitute).

Diyat — Blood Money

Equality of Male and Female in Ghurrah
Ruling that ghurrah is equal for male and female fetuses with two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the amount of ghurrah for a miscarried fetus and explain the Hanafi proof that it is the same for male and female.

Core Idea
The ghurrah for a fetus is 500 dirhams regardless of sex, because the hadith is absolute and the fetal stage lacks differentiation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the question of whether the compensation (ghurrah) for a miscarried fetus differs if the fetus is male or female. It firmly establishes that the ghurrah is equal, and provides two proofs: first, the absolute wording of the prophetic hadith, and second, a rational argument that the distinctions between men and women that affect legal rulings only appear after birth, not in the fetal stage. Understanding this ruling clarifies a key principle in Hanafi diyat law: the fetal stage is treated as a single category with a fixed compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
What is the act that triggers ghurrah? For what kind of fetus? The ruling applies to any miscarriage caused by another, irrespective of the fetus's sex.
The ghurrah is a type of diyat (blood money) for a fetus, fixed at a slave or slave-girl or 500 dirhams.
2
Locate the Primary Proof
The author cites the hadith: 'Fi al-janin ghurrah, 'abdun aw amatun aw khamsu mi'atin.' This is the textual evidence (dalil naqli).
The hadith is narrated in the famous collections and is considered sahih (sound).
3
Analyze the Nature of the Dalil
The hadith is absolute ('amm) in its wording—it does not specify male or female. According to Hanafi usul, an 'amm text applies to all its instances unless there is a specific exclusion (takhsis). Here, no exclusion exists.
The Hanafi principle 'al-amm yufidu al-wujub' means a general command indicates obligation and generality remains binding.
4
Understand the Secondary Rationale
The author adds a rational argument: the differences that produce unequal diyah between men and women (e.g., in marriage guardianship) only arise after birth when the full 'meanings of humanity' manifest. In the fetal stage, no such differentiation exists. Therefore, a single amount suffices.
This is a supplementary proof (istiqlali), reinforcing the law's wisdom.
5
Conclude the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the ghurrah for both male and female fetuses is 500 dirhams (or equivalent value). No distinction is made.
This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school, and there is no significant intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جنین مذکر اور مؤنث برابر ہیں و يستوى فيه الذكر والانثى لا طلاق ما روينا ولان فى الحيين انما ظهر التفات لتفاوت معانى الأدمية ولا تفاوت في الجنين فيقدر بمقدار واحد وهو خمس مائة ترجمہ اور اس میں ( وجوب مقدار غرہ میں ) لڑکا اور لڑکی برابر ہیں اس حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں اور اس لئے کہ دو زندوں میں تفاوت ظاہر ہو گا۔ آدمیت کے معنی کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے اور جنین میں کوئی تفاوت نہیں تو جنین کی دیت ایک ہی مقدار کے ساتھ مقدر ہوگی اور وہ پانچسو درہم ہے۔ تشریح یہ غرہ لڑکا اور لڑکی میں برابر ہے یعنی بہر دو صورت پانچسو درہم ہے اس لئے کہ حدیث مذكوره ( في الجنين غرة عبداوامة او خمس مائة) مطلق ہے جس میں لڑکا اور لڑکی کی کوئی تخصیص نہیں ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ لڑکے اور لڑکی میں تفاوت ہے لیکن وہ درجہ اور ہے جہاں تفاوت ہے اور جس میں یہ اب ہیں اس میں کوئی تفاوت نہیں ہے، بالفاظ دیگر ترتیب آثار کے درجہ میں تفاوت ہے اور درجہ تحقیق میں کوئی تفاوت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ دوسرے درجہ میں جو تفاوت ہے وہ آدمیت کے معنی کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے پیدا ہوا ہے مثلا مال کا مالک مرد و عورت دونوں ہو سکتے ہیں لیکن مالک نکاح صرف مرد ہوتا ہے نہ عورت بہر حال یہ تفاوت تو ہوتا ہے مگر وہ دوسرے درجہ میں ہے جنین میں کوئی تفاوت نہیں ہے لہذا دونوں کی ثیت ایک ہی مقر کی جائے گی یعنی پانچ سو درہم ۔
The male and female fetus are equal. And it is equal in it (the obligation of amount of ghurrah) for male and female due to the absoluteness of the hadith that we narrated, and because among the living, difference appears due to the difference of the meanings of humanity, but in the fetus there is no difference, so its diyah is determined by a single amount, which is five hundred dirhams. Explanation: This ghurrah is equal for male and female, i.e., in both cases it is five hundred dirhams, because the mentioned hadith ('for a fetus, a slave or a slave-girl or five hundred') is absolute with no specification for male or female. A second reason is that difference between male and female exists but in another stage where there is difference, and in the stage they are now (as fetuses) there is no difference. In other words, there is difference in the stage of manifestation of effects, but not in the stage of reality. Because the difference in the second stage arises from the difference in the meaning of humanity; for example, both men and women can own property, but the guardian in marriage is only the man, not the woman. Anyway, this difference exists but in the second stage; in the fetus there is no difference, so the diyah for both is fixed as the same amount, i.e., five hundred dirhams.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the ghurrah for a miscarried fetus is the same whether the fetus is male or female. Two proofs are given. First, the hadith reported earlier ('for a fetus, a slave or a slave-girl or five hundred dirhams') is absolute ('amm) and does not distinguish between male and female. Second, a rational argument: the differences that exist between men and women in legal rulings (such as marriage guardianship) arise after birth at a stage where the full meanings of humanity manifest. In the fetal stage, no such differentiation exists. Therefore the diyah for a fetus is fixed at five hundred dirhams for both sexes. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
غرہ (ghurrah): Compensation for a miscarried fetus; a slave or five hundred dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the amount of ghurrah for a female fetus according to the Hanafi school?
A) 250 dirhams
B) 500 dirhams
C) 1,000 dirhams
D) Half of the male's ghurrah

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah for any miscarried fetus is fixed at 500 dirhams, irrespective of gender.

Full Diyah When Fetus Born Alive Then Dies
Ruling that full diyah is due if fetus born alive then dies from prior injury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why full diyah (100 camels) is due when a fetus is born alive and then dies from a prenatal injury, and distinguish this case from stillbirth where only ghurrah is due.

Core Idea
A fetus born alive becomes a separate legal person; killing it demands full diyah.

This lesson addresses a key distinction in diyah (blood money) cases involving prenatal injuries. When a pregnant woman is struck, causing miscarriage, the compensation varies depending on whether the fetus was stillborn or born alive and later died. The source passage clarifies that if the child is born alive and then dies from the injury, full diyah is wajib because a living human was killed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the death of a fetus that was born alive, caused by a prior strike. The ruling is that full diyah (100 camels or equivalent) is wajib.
2
Understand the key condition
The ruling depends on the condition that the fetus is born alive (zindah bahar aya) and then dies from the injury. If stillborn, different rules apply.
Stillbirth triggers ghurrah (1/20 of diyah).
3
Analyze the reasoning
The striker destroyed a living being (atlafta hayyan). At birth, the child is an independent human. The cause of death is the prenatal strike, so it is killing a living person.
Rational proof: qiyas on killing any living human.
4
Contrast with alternative scenarios
If the fetus is stillborn, only ghurrah is due because it never lived separately. This distinction is critical for correct application.

Source Text

If the woman delivers the fetus alive and then it dies, then full diyah is due because the striker destroyed a living being by the prior strike. Translation: So if the woman delivers a living fetus and then it dies, then full diyah is due because the striker destroyed a living being due to the prior strike. Explanation: That is, if the fetus comes out alive and then dies, in that case full diyah will be obligatory. Because the child's death is from the effect of the first blow, and since its death is after the appearance of life, full diyah is due.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a pregnant woman is struck, causing labor. The fetus is born alive but subsequently dies from the injury sustained in the womb. The ruling is that full diyah (complete blood money) is wajib. The reasoning: at birth, the child is a separate living human being. The prior strike caused the death of a living person after the appearance of life. Therefore, it is treated as the killing of a living person, not merely as a miscarriage (which would require only ghurrah). This is a straightforward application of the principle that killing a living human demands full diyah.

Key Terms
دية كاملة (diyah kamilah): Full blood money, i.e., 100 camels or equivalent for killing a free Muslim.
غرة (ghurrah): Compensation for miscarriage/stillbirth: one-twentieth of diyah (e.g., 5 camels or equivalent).

Male and Female Fetus Equal in Ghurrah
Establishes equality of male and female fetus in diyat amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the ghurrah for a male and female fetus is equal and justify it using the Hanafi mutlaq principle and the reasoning from the absence of functional differences in fetal life.

Core Idea
The ghurrah for a fetus is 500 dirhams regardless of gender, because the hadith is absolute and the fetus has no functional differences.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a key Hanafi ruling on diyat for fetal loss. While some schools differentiate compensation based on the fetus's gender, the Hanafi school holds that the ghurrah is a fixed amount for both. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi treatment of absolute (mutlaq) texts and the reasoning behind the equality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the legal amount for ghurrah for a fetus? Does it vary by gender according to the Hanafi school?
The answer: 500 dirhams for both male and female.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Which hadith is cited as evidence? Quote the key phrase that establishes ghurrah.
The hadith: 'Fi al-janin ghurratun: 'abdun aw amatun aw khamsu mi'atin.'
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Why does the mutlaq hadith preclude gender distinction? Explain the Hanafi rule that mutlaq remains upon its absoluteness.
The hadith does not specify male or female, so it applies equally to both.
4
Understand the secondary reasoning
What is the talil based on the difference between living humans and fetuses?
Living males and females differ in legal capacities (e.g., guardianship), but a fetus has no such differences, so compensation should be uniform.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
How does the Shafi'i position differ? Why do they differentiate?
Shafi'is use qiyas on full diyat where male is double, but Hanafis reject this because the hadith is specific.

Commentary
This passage establishes that the ghurrah (compensation) for a fetus is the same whether male or female: 500 dirhams. Additionally, the reasoning (talil) is that the differences between living males and females arise from their distinct social roles (e.g., guardianship in marriage), which do not exist in a fetus. Therefore, the diyat is set at a single value for both.

Mother dies after delivering dead fetus: diyah and ghurrah
Ruling on double liability when mother dies after miscarriage due to injury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that both diyah and ghurrah are wajib when a mother dies after delivering a dead fetus due to injury, and cite the hadith from Tabarani as proof.

Core Idea
Two lives lost deserve two compensations: diyah for the mother, ghurrah for the fetus.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a single blow causes two deaths — a mother and her unborn fetus — the aggressor does not escape full liability. This lesson examines the ruling that both diyah (full blood money) and ghurrah (compensation for fetal loss) must be paid. The proof is a prophetic judgment recorded by Tabarani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The passage describes a pregnant woman who is struck, delivers a dead fetus, and then dies from the injury. Recognize that two independent deaths have occurred: the mother (a free human) and the fetus (a life with potential).
The fetus was already dead at delivery (stillborn) — this matters.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The text explicitly states that the aggressor owes both diyah for the mother and ghurrah for the fetus. Note that diyah is the full blood money for a free adult, while ghurrah is a fixed compensation of 500 dirhams for the loss of a fetus.
Diyah for the mother wajib; ghurrah for the fetus wajib.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Tabarani: the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) judged in such a case with both diyah and ghurrah. Identify that this is a Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut) but still binding as a proof in Hanafi usul.
The hadith: 'انه عليه السلام قضى في هذا بالدية والغرة'.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actual judgment is the proof — his action demonstrates the rule. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's actions (fi'l) can indicate obligation (wujub) when they are done to explain a general command or in a judicial context.
No other method of istinbat needed; the hadith directly prescribes the rule.
5
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school is unanimous on this ruling. There is no dispute among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. The ruling is also not contested by other schools — it is muttafaq alayh.
Cross-madhhab: all four schools agree on this point.

The proof is a hadith from Tabarani that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) decided in such a case to give diyah for the mother and ghurrah for the fetus. This shows that the liability for two separate harms (mother's death and fetal loss) are independent.

Two Full Diyahs for Mother and Living Child
Ruling on two full diyahs when mother and then living child die sequentially

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah liability when a pregnant woman and her subsequently born child die from the same injury and apply it to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Two separate lives mean two full diyahs—the child's independent life after birth establishes separate liability.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in diyat: when a perpetrator strikes a pregnant woman, causing her death, and then the fetus is born alive but later succumbs to the same injury. The Hanafi ruling requires two full diyahs, one for each victim. Understanding this case clarifies how diyat treats the death of a fetus that achieves independent life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the event sequence
First, the mother dies from the blow. Then the fetus is delivered alive. Finally, the child dies from the effects of the blow.
The order matters: the child must be born alive for a full diyah.
2
Determine the child's legal status
Since the child was born alive, he is a separate human being under Islamic law, not merely a part of the mother.
A stillborn child only merits ghurrah, not full diyah.
3
Apply the rule of diyah for each victim
The perpetrator killed two distinct persons, so he owes a full diyah for the mother and a full diyah for the child.
No reduction: the diyah is full in both cases.
4
Confirm the absence of dispute
There is no intra-Hanafi disagreement; the ruling is consistent across the school and is mutually agreed upon by other madhahib.
This case is straightforward in its application.

Fetal Liability When Mother Dies: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on fetal liability after mother's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not impose ghurrah when the mother dies before delivering a dead fetus, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
When causation is uncertain due to an intervening death, liability is not established.

This lesson tackles a subtle inter-madhhab dispute: a pregnant woman is struck, dies before delivery, and the fetus is later expelled dead. The Hanafi school holds that only diyah for the mother is wajib, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues that ghurrah is also due for the fetus. The difference hinges on whether the mother's death creates doubt about the cause of the fetal death. By the end, you will be able to trace the reasoning and apply it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: only diyah for the mother, nothing for the fetus. Note the hukm level (wajib for mother's diyah).
The ruling is clear from the text: 'لا شيء في الجنين'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ghurrah is wajib for the fetus. His reasoning: the apparent cause of fetal death is the blow, just as when the mother survives and delivers a dead fetus.
The Shafi'i view is described in the text: 'وقال الشافعى تجب الغرة في الجنين'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i uses qiyas: this case is analogized to the situation where the mother survives but delivers a dead fetus. In that case, ghurrah is wajib because the blow is clearly the cause.
The text says: 'فصار كما اذا القته ميتا وهي حية'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the mother's death is an intervening cause—the fetus suffocates because its breathing depends on hers. Thus there is doubt (shakk) about whether the blow or the mother's death caused the fetal death. The principle 'al-wajib la yathbutu bi al-shakk' applies.
The text: 'فلا يجب الضمان بالشك'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi judge orders only diyah for the mother; a Shafi'i judge would also order ghurrah for the fetus. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the Hanafi position.
The difference is a real variation in compensation amounts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت مرگئی پھر مردہ بچہ ڈال دیا تو ضارب پر ماں کی دیت ہے بچہ کے بدلے غرہ ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
وان ماتت ثم القت ميتا فعليه دية فى الام ولا شيء فى الجنين و قال الشافعى تجب الغرة في الجنين لان الظاهر موا بالضرب فصار كما اذا القته ميتا وهي حية ولنا ان موت الام احد سببى موته لانه يختنق بموتها اذ تنفسه بتنفسها فلا يجب الضمان بالشك
ترجمه .... اور اگر عوت مرگئی پھر اس نے مردہ بچہ ڈالا تو ضارب پر ماں کی دیت ہے اور جنین میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جنین میں غرہ واجب ہے اس لئے کہ مرنا ضرب کی وجہ سے ہے تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جب کہ اس کو مردہ کو ڈالا ہو اور عورت زندہ ہو اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماں کی موت بچہ کی موت کے دوسیوں میں سے ایک ہے اسلئے کہ ماں کے مرنے کی وجہ سے اس کا دم گھٹ جائے گا اس لئے کہ اس کا سانس لینا ماں کے سانس لینے کی وجہ سے ہے تو شک کی وجہ سے ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح اور اگر یہ صورت پیش آئی کہ عورت مرگئی پھر مرا ہوا بچہ نکلا تو یہ صورت اختلافی ہے، ہمارے نزدیک صورت مذکورہ میں صرف ماں کی دیت واجب ہوگی اور بچہ کا کچھ راجب نہ ہوگا۔
And if she dies, then delivers a dead fetus, then upon him is diyah for the mother and nothing for the fetus. Al-Shafi'i said: the ghurrah is wajib for the fetus because it is apparent that the death was from the blow, so it becomes like when she delivers it dead while she is alive. Our proof is that the mother's death is one of the two causes of its death, because it suffocates with her death since its breathing is from her breathing, so liability is not wajib due to doubt.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-madhhab dispute? Actually inter-madhhab with Shafi'i. The scenario: a woman is struck, she dies before delivering, and then the dead fetus is expelled. The Hanafi ruling is that only diyah for the mother is wajib, and no ghurrah for the fetus. The reason is that the mother's death itself could have caused the fetal death (e.g., by suffocation as the fetus breathes through her). Since there is doubt about whether the blow or the mother's death killed the fetus, liability is not established (the principle: al-wajib la yathbutu bi al-shakk). Al-Shafi'i argues that since the blow caused the mother's death and presumably also caused the fetal death, ghurrah is wajib, just like when a woman is struck and delivers a dead fetus while alive. The Hanafi response distinguishes: when the mother survives, the causal link is clear; when she dies, there is an intervening factor (the mother's own death) that could have killed the fetus, creating doubt. Hence no liability for the fetus.

Key Terms
غرہ (ghurrah): Compensation for fetal loss (usually a slave or equivalent value).
شک (shakk): Doubt regarding causation; here, doubt prevents liability as per Hanafi principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a woman is struck, dies, and then a dead fetus is delivered, what is the liability?
A) Full diyah for the mother and ghurrah for the fetus
B) Only full diyah for the mother
C) Only ghurrah for the fetus
D) No liability at all

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when the mother's death precedes the fetal delivery, the uncertainty in causation negates any separate liability for the fetus.

Diyat — Blood Money

Ruling on Diyah and Ghurrah When a Woman Miscarries and Dies
Ruling with hadith proof for diyah and ghurrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two obligatory compensations when a woman is struck, miscarries a dead fetus, and dies, and cite the prophetic proof.

Core Idea
When a pregnant woman is killed and her fetus is miscarried dead, the striker owes both diyah for the mother and ghurrah for the fetus.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Book of Diyat (Blood Money). The matn declares that if a woman is struck, delivers a dead fetus, and then dies, the striker must pay both the diyah (full blood money) for the mother and a ghurrah (one-fifth of diyah) for the fetus. The proof is an authentic hadith in which the Prophet ﷺ judged accordingly. Understanding this ruling clarifies that a single act causing the death of two persons results in two separate compensations, each with its own basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two liabilities
Read the matn: 'upon the striker is the diyah for killing the mother and a ghurrah for the casting.' List the two obligations.
Diyah is the blood money for a free person; ghurrah is specifically for a miscarried fetus.
2
Understand the ghurrah amount
The ghurrah is one-fifth of the full diyah. In Hanafi fiqh, this is 20 camels or 500 dirhams.
This is fixed regardless of the sex of the fetus.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'the Prophet ﷺ judged in this case with diyah and ghurrah.' Identify the source (Tabarani).
The hadith is ahad (single transmission) but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalalah).
4
Analyze the proof's strength
Determine thubut (transmission) and dalala (indication). The hadith is zanni al-thubut (ahad) but qat'i al-dalalah (explicit ruling).
Hanafi usul: a hadith ahad can establish a wajib ruling when its meaning is unequivocal.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Example: Zaid kicks a pregnant woman. She miscarries a dead fetus and then dies. What must Zaid pay?
He pays the full diyah to the mother's heirs and the ghurrah to the fetus's heirs (the father).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات عورت نے جنین مردہ ڈالا پھر عورت بھی مرگئی تو ضارب پر ماں کے قتل کی دیت واجب ہے وان القت ميتا ثم ماتت الام فعليه دية بقتل الام وغرة بالقائها و قد صح انه عليه السلام قضى في هذا بالدية والغرة ترجمہ اور اگر عورت نے مردہ بچہ ڈالا ہو پھر مرگئی تو ضارب پر ماں کے قتل کی وجہ سے دیت ہے اور ماں کے بچہ ڈالنے کی وجہ سے غرہ ہے اور درجہ صحت کو پہنچی ہے یہ بات کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے اس صورت میں دیت اور غرہ کا فیصلہ فرمایا ہے۔ تشریح اگر زید کے لات مارنے کی وجہ سے ( مثلا ) جنین میت باہر آ گیا اور پھر عورت بھی مرگئی تو یہاں زید پر دو ضمان ہیں عورت کی دیت واجب ہے اور جنین کی وجہ سے غرہ واجب ہے۔ اور بموجب روایت طبرانی صورت مذکورہ میں حضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہی فیصلہ فرمایا ہے۔
Book of Diyat. A woman cast a dead fetus, then the mother died. So upon the striker is the diyah for killing the mother and a ghurrah for the casting. And it has been authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged in this case with diyah and ghurrah. Translation: And if the woman cast a dead child, then she died, then upon the striker is diyah for the mother's killing and ghurrah for the mother's casting. And it has reached the level of authenticity that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged in this situation with diyah and ghurrah. Explanation: For example, if due to Zaid's kicking the fetus came out dead, and then the woman also died, then here two compensations are obligatory upon Zaid: the diyah of the woman is obligatory and the ghurrah due to the fetus is obligatory. And according to Tabarani's narration, the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave this same judgment in the mentioned situation.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the chapter of Diyat. The matn declares that if a woman is struck and she delivers a dead fetus and then dies, the striker must pay the diyah (blood money) for the mother and the ghurrah (compensation, one-fifth of full diyah) for the fetus. The proof is the authentic hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged accordingly. The Urdu commentary clarifies the scenario: the injury causes first the miscarriage of a dead fetus and then the mother's death, leading to two separate obligations. The commentary also cites Tabarani's corroborating narration.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money paid for wrongful killing or injury; in this context, full diyah for the mother.
غرة (ghurrah): Compensation for a fetus; set at one-fifth of the full diyah (20 camels or equivalent), payable when a fetus is miscarried due to assault.
جنين (janeen): Unborn child in the womb; in diyat rulings, a miscarried fetus whose life is compensated with ghurrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Diyah for mother only
B) Diyah for mother and ghurrah for fetus
C) Ghurrah for mother and diyah for fetus
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's judgment establishes that when a pregnant woman is killed and her fetus dies, the killer owes both diyah (for the mother) and ghurrah (for the fetus).

Diyat — Blood Money

Two Full Diyah When Mother Dies and Fetus Born Alive Then Dies
Ruling requiring two full diyah for killing mother and live-born child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pregnant woman is fatally struck and her child is born alive but subsequently dies, and explain why two full diyah are required.

Core Idea
Born alive means a separate life — full diyah for both mother and child.

In Hanafi law, the blood money (diyah) for a fetus depends on whether it was born alive. This passage clarifies a scenario where the mother dies from an assault, then the fetus is delivered alive but later dies. The ruling is straightforward but hinges on the critical distinction between a fetus (compensated with ghurrah) and a living person (full diyah). Understanding this distinction is essential for correct application in cases of prenatal injury.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and sequence of death
The scenario: mother dies from the assault first, then the child is born alive, then the child dies from the same injury.
The order matters: the child was alive after birth, so it became a separate human being.
2
Determine liability for the mother
Since the mother was killed directly by the strike, the assailant owes full diyah for her life.
No dispute among Hanafis that a direct killing (mubasharah) requires full diyah.
3
Determine liability for the child
Because the child was born alive, it became a separate person. Therefore, the assailant owes full diyah for the child, not ghurrah.
Had the child died in the womb, only ghurrah (one-twentieth of diyah) would be due.
4
Combine the obligations
The assailant is the direct killer of two persons, so two full diyah are wajib.
The reasoning: 'because he is the killer of two persons' (talil).
5
Contrast with the stillborn scenario
If the child had been stillborn, only one full diyah (for the mother) plus ghurrah would be due. This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical difference.
This highlights the importance of the 'born alive' condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضرب سے عورت فوت ہو گئی بچہ زندہ پیدا ہوا پھر مرا تو ضارب پر دو دیتیں واجب ہیں و ان ماتت الام من الضربة ثم خرج الجنين بعد ذالك حيا ثم مات فعليه دية في الام ودية في الجنين لانه قاتل شخصين ترجمہ اور اگر مارنے کی وجہ سے ماں مرگئی پھر اس کے بعد زندہ جنین نکلا پھر وہ مر گیا تو اس کے اوپر ماں میں دیت ہے اور ایک دیست جنین کی ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ( ضارب ) دو شخصوں کا قاتل ہے۔ تشریح اور اگر یہ صورت ہوئی ہو کہ مار کی وجہ سے پہلے ماں مرگئی پھر بچہ زندہ نکلا اور پھر وہ بھی مر گیا تو یہاں دودیت واجب ہوں گی۔ بچہ کی پوری دیت اور عورت کی پوری دیت کیونکہ ضارب نے دو کو قتل کیا ہے۔
And if the mother dies from the blow, then the fetus comes out after that alive, then dies, then upon him is diyah for the mother and diyah for the fetus, because he is the killer of two persons. Translation: And if due to the blow the mother died, then after that a live fetus came out, then he died, then upon him is diyah for the mother and one diyah for the fetus, because he (the striker) is the killer of two persons. Explanation: And if this situation occurs, that due to the blow first the mother died, then the child came out alive and then he also died, then here two diyah will be obligatory: the full diyah of the child and the full diyah of the woman, because the striker has killed two.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents another scenario: the mother is struck and dies immediately, then the fetus is born alive but subsequently dies. In this case, the assailant owes two full diyah payments—one for the mother and one for the child. The reasoning is straightforward: the striker is directly responsible for the deaths of two human beings (the mother and the child, who was born alive and thus a separate person). The Urdu commentary reinforces that both are full diyah, not ghurrah, because the child was born alive and thus constitutes a complete human life.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Full blood money for a complete human life; in this case, full diyah for the child because it was born alive.
قاتل (qatil): Killer; here, the striker is considered a direct killer of two persons.
غرّة (ghurrah): One-twentieth of full diyah, paid for a fetus that dies in the womb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only diyah for the mother
B) Diyah for mother and ghurrah for child
C) Two full diyah for mother and child
D) No liability for child

Key Takeaway
When a fetus is born alive before death, full diyah is due for both mother and child because the striker has killed two separate individuals.

Dispute on Ghurrah When Mother Dies Before Fetus
Inter-madhhab dispute on causation and liability for fetal death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on ghurrah when the mother dies first and identify the role of certainty of causation in imposing liability.

Core Idea
When causation is uncertain, liability cannot be imposed.

This lesson examines a classical dispute in diyat (blood money) concerning a fetus. The scenario: a pregnant woman is struck, dies, and then delivers a dead fetus. Both schools agree on the mother's diyah, but differ on whether ghurrah (compensation for the fetus) is due. Understanding this dispute reveals a foundational Hanafi principle: liability requires certainty of cause.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and agreed ruling
Identify the factual scenario: mother dies first, then delivers dead fetus. Note that both schools agree the mother's diyah is wajib.
This is the starting point: full diyah for mother is uncontested.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds ghurrah wajib for the fetus. His proof: the apparent cause of fetal death is the blow, analogizing to the case where the fetus is delivered dead first and then the mother dies.
Shafi'i relies on qiyas: both scenarios share the apparent cause (the blow).
3
Identify the Hanafi position and its proof
State that the Hanafi school holds no ghurrah wajib. Their proof: the mother's death is an independent alternative cause (suffocation of the fetus), creating uncertainty about the actual cause.
Hanafi uses the principle: doubt (shakk) in causation prevents liability.
4
Analyze the Hanafi principle of doubt
Examine why the Hanafi school considers the mother's death a valid alternative cause. The fetus depends on the mother's breathing; when she dies, it suffocates. Thus, two possible causes exist: the blow or the asphyxiation.
This is a rational (aqli) argument, not based on a text.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi fiqh, the responsible party pays only the mother's diyah. In Shafi'i fiqh, they pay both mother's diyah and fetus's ghurrah. Identify which position is mufta bihi in Hanafi practice.
The Hanafi position is relied upon according to the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت مرگئی پھر مردہ بچہ ڈال دیا تو ضارب پر ماں کی دیت ہے بچہ کے بدلے غرہ ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء وان ماتت ثم القت ميتا فعليه دية فى الام ولا شيء فى الجنين و قال الشافعى تجب الغرة في الجنين لان الظاهر موا بالضرب فصار كما اذا القته ميتا وهي حية ولنا ان موت الام احد سببى موته لانه يختنق بموتها اذ تنفسه بتنفسها فلا يجب الضمان بالشک ترجمه .... اور اگر عوت مرگئی پھر اس نے مردہ بچہ ڈالا تو ضارب پر ماں کی دیت ہے اور جنین میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جنین میں غرہ واجب ہے اس لئے کہ مرنا ضرب کی وجہ سے ہے تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جب کہ اس کو مردہ کو ڈالا ہو اور عورت زندہ ہو اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماں کی موت بچہ کی موت کے دوسیوں میں سے ایک ہے اسلئے کہ ماں کے مرنے کی وجہ سے اس کا دم گھٹ جائے گا اس لئے کہ اس کا سانس لینا ماں کے سانس لینے کی وجہ سے ہے تو شک کی وجہ سے ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح اور اگر یہ صورت پیش آئی کہ عورت مرگئی پھر مرا ہوا بچہ نکلا تو یہ صورت اختلافی ہے، ہمارے نزدیک صورت مذکورہ میں صرف ماں کی دیت واجب ہوگی اور بچہ کا کچھ راجب نہ ہوگا۔ كتاب الديات 19- اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ماں کی دیت اور بچہ میں غرہ واجب ہوگا امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں بچہ کا مرنا ضرب کی وجہ سے ہے۔ ظاہر یہی ہے تو یہ پہلی صورت کے مثل ہو گیا یعنی جہ کہ پہلے مرا ہوا بچہ نکل جائے اور پھر ماں مر جائے تو جیسے اس میں دیت ام اور بچہ کا غرہ واجب ہے یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہیئے ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ کے مرنے کے یہاں دو سبب ہیں 1- ضرب کی وجہ سے مرجائے -۲- ماں کے مرنے کی وجہ سے دم گھٹ کر مر جائے کیونکہ بچہ ماں کے سانس کے ذریعہ سانس لیتا ہے۔ بہر حال یہاں شک پیدا ہو گیا کہ موت اول کی وجہ سے ہے یا ثانی کی شک کی وجہ سے ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
And if she dies then casts a dead [fetus], then upon him is diyah for the mother and nothing for the fetus. And al-Shafi'i said: The ghurrah is obligatory for the fetus because the apparent [cause] is death by the blow, so it becomes like when she casts it dead while she is alive. And our evidence is that the mother's death is one of the two causes of his death, because he suffocates with her death since his breathing is due to her breathing, so liability is not obligated due to doubt. Translation: ... And if this situation occurs that the woman died and then a dead child came out, then this situation is disputed. According to us, in the mentioned situation only the diyah of the mother is obligatory and nothing for the child. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the diyah of the mother and ghurrah for the child are obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that in the mentioned situation, the child's death is due to the blow. This is apparent, so it becomes similar to the first situation, i.e., when a dead child comes out first and then the mother dies, just as in that case the diyah of the mother and ghurrah of the child are obligatory, similarly here. Our evidence is that the child's death has two causes: 1. He may die due to the blow; 2. He may die due to the mother's death by suffocation because the child breathes through the mother's breathing. In any case, doubt arises whether the death is due to the first cause or the second. Due to doubt, liability is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This is a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The scenario: the woman is struck and dies first, and then the fetus is delivered dead. Both schools agree that the mother's diyah is due. The disagreement is over the ghurrah for the fetus. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the apparent cause is the blow, so ghurrah is due, analogizing to the case where the fetus is delivered dead and then the mother dies. The Hanafi school holds that the mother's death is an independent cause of the fetus's death: since the fetus's oxygen supply depends on the mother, once she dies, the fetus suffocates. Thus, there is uncertainty (shakk) about the actual cause of death, and liability cannot be imposed based on doubt.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurrah): Compensation for a miscarried fetus; in this dispute, whether it is due when mother dies first.
سبب (sabab): Cause; here, the two possible causes of the fetus's death: the blow and the mother's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is ghurrah not obligatory when the mother dies and then delivers a dead fetus?
A) Because the fetus was never alive
B) Because the mother's death may have caused the fetus's death, creating doubt
C) Because the blow did not affect the fetus
D) Because the fetus was already dead

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, certainty of causation is required for liability; doubt (shakk) from alternative causes precludes imposing ghurrah.

Inheritance of Ghurrah: Killer Cannot Inherit
Ruling that the ghurrah for a fetus is inherited by the fetus's heirs, and the killer is excluded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the inheritance of the ghurrah for a fetus and identify the killer's exclusion.

Core Idea
The ghurrah is the fetus's property, inherited by its heirs; the killer is always barred.

This lesson addresses a specific case in the law of diyat: the disposition of the ghurrah payment when a fetus is killed. Understanding that the ghurrah is treated as the fetus's estate reveals why the killer, even if the father, cannot inherit from it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the payment and its legal nature
Recognize that the ghurrah is wajib and defined as badal al-nafs (substitute for the person). This makes it part of the fetus's estate.
The term badal al-nafs is key: the ghurrah is not a fine but compensation for the life lost.
2
Determine the proper disposition
Since the ghurrah belongs to the fetus's estate, it is inherited by the fetus's legal heirs according to faraid rules.
The heirs are determined as if the fetus had died naturally after birth.
3
Apply the killer's exclusion
The rule 'a killer does not inherit' applies. Even if the killer is a potential heir (like the father), he is barred from the ghurrah.
This rule is unconditional in Hanafi law: any unjust killing, direct or indirect, bars inheritance.
4
Analyze the provided example
The text gives the case of a father striking his wife's belly, causing fetal death. The father is the killer and thus excluded; the 'aqila pays the ghurrah to other heirs.
This illustrates the practical application of the principle in a commonly-asked scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وما يجب في الجنين موروث عنه لانه بدل نفسه فيرثه ورثته ولا يرثه الضارب حتى لو ضرب بطن امرأته فالقت ابنه ميتا فعلى عاقلة الاب غرة ولايرث منها لانه قاتل بغير حق مباشرة ولا ميراث للقاتل ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جنین میں جو غرہ واجب ہو گاوہ اس کی جانب سے میراث میں تقسیم کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے نفس کا بدل ہے تو جنین کے ورثا سکے وارث ہوں گے اور ضارب اس کا وارث نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر اس نے اپنی بیوی کے پیٹ پر مارا پس عورت نے ضارب کے بچہ کو ڈالا۔ حالانکہ وہ مردہ ہے تو باپ کی برادری پر غرہ ہے اور باپ اس غرہ میں وارث نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ ناحق مباشرت کے طریقہ پر قتل کرنے والا ہے حالانکہ قاتل کو میراث نہیں ملتی ۔ تشریح جنین کی جملہ صورت مذکورہ میں ضارب پر جو مال واجب کیا گیا ہے چونکہ یہ حسب تصریح سابق نفس کا بدل ہے لہذا اس کو جنین کے ورثا کے درمیان تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اگر ضارب بھی اس کا وارث ہو تو وہ میراث سے محروم رہے گا مثلاً کسی نے اپنی بیوی کے پیٹ پر لات ماری جس سے مردہ جنین باہر نکل پڑا تو یہاں ضارب کی برادری پر دیت واجب ہوگی اور ضارب اس غرہ میں میراث کا مستحق نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قاتل کو میراث نہیں ملا کرتی اور یہ قاتل ہے اور یہ قتل بھی قتل سبب نہیں بلکہ قتل مباشرت ہے اور قتل ناحق ہے فیہ مافیہ۔
He said: And what is obligatory for the fetus is inherited from him, because it is the substitute of his person, so his heirs inherit it, and the striker does not inherit it. Even if he struck his wife's belly and she cast his son dead, then upon the father's 'aqila is a ghurrah, and he does not inherit from it, because he is a killer unjustly directly, and there is no inheritance for the killer. Translation: Quduri said: And the ghurrah that is obligatory for the fetus is divided as inheritance from its side, because it is the substitute of his person, so the fetus's heirs inherit it, and the striker does not inherit it. To the extent that if he struck his wife's belly and she cast his child, while it is dead, then upon the father's 'aqila is a ghurrah, and the father does not inherit from it, because he is a killer unjustly by direct causation, and there is no inheritance for the killer. Explanation: In all the mentioned situations of the fetus, the wealth that is made obligatory upon the striker, since as per the previous clarification it is the substitute of the person, therefore it is distributed among the fetus's heirs. But if the striker is also his heir, then he will be deprived of inheritance. For example, someone kicked his wife's belly from which a dead fetus came out. So here, diyah is obligatory upon the striker's 'aqila, and the striker is not entitled to inheritance in this ghurrah, because the killer does not get inheritance, and he is a killer, and this killing is not killing by cause but direct killing, and it is unjust killing.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage explains the disposition of the ghurrah payment. Since the ghurrah is compensation for the fetus's life (badal al-nafs), it is treated as the fetus's property and thus distributed among its legal heirs according to the law of inheritance. Crucially, the person who caused the fetal death (the striker) is excluded from inheriting any part of the ghurrah, even if he would normally be an heir (e.g., the father). The rule is that a killer does not inherit from the victim. This applies whether the killing is direct (mubasharah) or by cause (sabab), but here it is direct and unjust.

Key Terms
بدل النفس (badal al-nafs): Substitute for the person; compensation for the life of the fetus, making it part of the estate.
قاتل (qatil): Killer; here, the striker is a direct killer and thus barred from inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the inheritance of the ghurrah for a fetus?
A) The killer inherits if he is the father
B) The ghurrah is not inherited, it goes to the state
C) The ghurrah is inherited by the fetus's heirs, excluding the killer
D) The ghurrah is divided equally among all relatives

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah is inherited by the fetus's heirs, and the killer is always excluded from this inheritance.

Amount of Ghurrah for the Fetus of a Slave Woman
Ruling and dispute on the amount of ghurrah for the fetus of a slave woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the amount of ghurrah for a slave woman's fetus and evaluate the differing proofs.

Core Idea
The ghurrah for a slave woman's fetus is based on its hypothetical value, not the mother's.

This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses a crucial difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding compensation (ghurrah) for the fetus of a slave woman. The Hanafi school calculates the amount based on the fetus's hypothetical value, varying by sex, while the Shafi'i school uses a fixed fraction of the mother's value. Understanding the reasoning behind each position is key to mastering the Hanafi approach to diyat (blood money).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact amounts: for a male fetus, half a tenth of its value if alive; for a female, one tenth of its value.
The Hanafi school treats the fetus as a potential separate person.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the ghurrah is a tenth of the mother's value regardless of the fetus's sex.
The opposing school is the Shafi'i madhhab.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Shafi'i reasoning: the fetus is considered a part (juz') of the mother, and compensation for parts is derived from the original's value.
This is a qiyas on compensation for limbs.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school implicitly rejects this by treating the fetus as a distinct entity, deserving its own valuation.
The response is based on the potential independence of the fetus.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the amount of ghurrah: Hanafi gives different amounts based on the fetus's hypothetical value; Shafi'i gives a fixed fraction of the mother's value.
This affects monetary compensation in cases of miscarriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و في جنين الامة اذا كان ذكراً نصف عشر قيمته لو كان حيا و عشر قيمته لو كان انثى و قال الشافعي فيه عشر قيمة الام لانه جزء من وجه وضمان الاجزاء يوخذ مقدارها من الاصل ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور باندی کے جنین میں جب کہ وہ لڑکا ہو اس کی قیمت کا نصف عشر ہے اگر وہ زندہ ہوتا اور اس کی قیمت کا عشر ہے اگر وہ لڑکی ہو اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس میں ماں کی قیمت کا عشر ہے اس لئے کہ یہ من وجہ جزء ہے اور اجزاء کا ضمان اس کی مقدار اصل کے حامہ ،ا سے لی جاتی ہے۔
He said: And regarding the fetus of a slave woman, if it is a male, then half of a tenth of its value if it were alive, and a tenth of its value if it were female. And al-Shafi'i said: In it is a tenth of the mother's value, because it is a part from one aspect, and the liability for parts takes its amount from the original. Translation: Quduri said: And regarding the fetus of a slave woman, when it is a male, half a tenth of its price if it were alive, and a tenth of its price if it were female. And al-Shafi'i said: In it is a tenth of the mother's price, because it is a part from one aspect, and liability for parts takes its amount from the original.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage discusses the quantum of ghurrah for the fetus of a slave woman (umm al-walad or ordinary slave). The Hanafi school differentiates based on the sex of the fetus: for a male, half a tenth of the value the fetus would have if born alive; for a female, a tenth of that value. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the ghurrah is a tenth of the mother's value, reasoning that the fetus is a part (juz') of the mother and compensation for parts is taken from the original's value. The Hanafi school, however, treats the fetus as potentially a separate entity and calculates based on its hypothetical value.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurrah): Compensation for a slave woman's fetus; amount varies according to school.
جنين الأمة (janeen al-ammah): Fetus of a slave woman; its ghurrah amount is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the amount of ghurrah for a male fetus of a slave woman?
A) A tenth of the mother's value
B) Half a tenth of the fetus's value if alive
C) A tenth of the fetus's value if alive
D) Full diyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school values the fetus independently, while the Shafi'i school ties it to the mother's value.
