Diyat for Fetus When Mother Dies After Miscarriage
Presents the intra-madhhab dispute and Hanafi proof based on doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on diyat when a pregnant woman dies after a miscarriage and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of shakk.

Core Idea
Uncertainty (shakk) about the cause of death prevents imposing liability — Hanafi limits ghurrah when the mother's death may have caused fetal death.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding blood money (diyat) when a pregnant woman is struck, causing miscarriage, and she then dies. The central question is whether the assailant must pay both a full diyah for the mother and a ghurrah for the fetus, or only the mother's diyah. The Hanafi position rests on the legal principle that damages cannot be imposed based on uncertainty (shakk), while the Shafi'i position relies on apparent causation and analogy (qiyas). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply usul al-fiqh principles in criminal liability cases.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the disputed ruling
Identify the scenario: a pregnant woman is struck, the fetus is delivered dead, and then the mother dies. The dispute is whether the assailant must pay both a full diyah for the mother and a ghurrah for the fetus, or only the mother's diyah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam Shafi'i argues that both compensations are due, analogizing to the case where the dead fetus is expelled first and then the mother dies—there, both are due. The apparent cause of the fetus's death is the blow.
Shafi'i uses qiyas based on the similar outcome.
3
Identify the Hanafi position and its proof
Hanafis hold that only the mother's diyah is due because the cause of the fetus's death is uncertain: it could be from the blow or from suffocation due to the mother's death. The fetus breathes through the mother, so her death can cause fetal death. This doubt (shakk) prevents imposing liability for the fetus.
Hanafis invoke the principle that damages are not imposed based on probability.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i analogy
The Hanafi rebuttal is that the analogy fails because in the scenario where the mother dies after, the link between the blow and the fetus's death is weakened by the intervening death of the mother. The doubt is real and legally significant.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis would not order the additional ghurrah for the fetus; Shafi'is would. The outcome depends on which school's ruling is applied.
This difference has real financial and legal consequences for the liable party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ماں کی دیت اور بچہ میں غرہ واجب ہوگا امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں بچہ کا مرنا ضرب کی وجہ سے ہے۔ ظاہر یہی ہے تو یہ پہلی صورت کے مثل ہو گیا یعنی جب کہ پہلے مرا ہوا بچہ نکل جائے اور پھر ماں مر جائے تو جیسے اس میں دیت ام اور بچہ کا غرہ واجب ہے یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہیئے ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ کے مرنے کے یہاں دو سبب ہیں 1- ضرب کی وجہ سے مرجائے -۲- ماں کے مرنے کی وجہ سے دم گھٹ کر مر جائے کیونکہ بچہ ماں کے سانس کے ذریعہ سانس لیتا ہے۔ بہر حال یہاں شک پیدا ہو گیا کہ موت اول کی وجہ سے ہے یا ثانی کی شک کی وجہ سے ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
And according to Imam Shafi'i, the full diyah for the mother and a ghurrah for the child are obligatory. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that in the mentioned case, the child's death is caused by the blow. This is apparent, so it becomes like the first case: when the dead child comes out first and then the mother dies, just as in that case the mother's diyah and the child's ghurrah are obligatory, here too it should be similar. Our proof is that for the child's death, there are two causes here: 1. It dies due to the blow. 2. It dies due to suffocation from the mother's death, because the child breathes through the mother's breath. In any case, doubt arises whether the death is due to the first or the second. Due to doubt, compensation is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the case where a pregnant woman is struck, causing a miscarriage (the fetus comes out dead), and then the mother subsequently dies. Imam Shafi'i argues that if both are dead, full diyah is due for the mother and a ghurrah for the fetus, analogizing to the case where the dead fetus is expelled first. The Hanafi response is that the cause of the fetus's death is uncertain: it could have died from the blow or from suffocation due to the mother's death. Since the fetus depends on the mother's breathing, if she dies before delivery, the fetus may die from asphyxiation. This uncertainty (shakk) prevents the imposition of compensation (daman) for the fetus's death because the causal link is not established. Thus, only the ghurrah is due if the fetus is born dead, but if the mother dies later, the fetal death is attributed to her death, so no additional ghurrah.

Key Terms
غرہ (ghurrah): Compensation for a miscarried fetus, fixed at one-twentieth of the mother's diyah (i.e., 5 camels or equivalent).
شک (shakk): Doubt or uncertainty about the cause of death; according to Hanafi usul, it prevents the imposition of liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, why is no separate ghurrah due for the fetus when the mother dies after a miscarriage caused by a blow?
A) Because the fetus is considered a part of the mother
B) Because the cause of the fetus's death is uncertain (doubt) between the blow and suffocation from the mother's death
C) Because the fetus is not a human being until born alive
D) Because the assailant cannot be liable for two deaths from one act

Key Takeaway
When the cause of death is uncertain (shakk), Hanafis do not impose compensation; thus, if a mother dies after a miscarriage, only her diyah is due, not a separate ghurrah for the fetus.

Inheritance of Ghurrah for a Miscarried Fetus
States and explains inheritance of ghurrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who inherits the ghurrah paid for a miscarried fetus and explain why the assailant is excluded.

Core Idea
The ghurrah belongs to the fetus's estate; the assailant is barred as a direct murderer.

This passage from Al-Quduri establishes a clear principle: compensation for the fetus itself (ghurrah) is inherited by the fetus's heirs. Even if the assailant is the father, he cannot inherit because he is classified as a direct murderer. Let's unpack the reasoning and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first sentence: 'Whatever is obligatory in the case of a fetus is inherited from him.' This states the main rule: the ghurrah is treated as the deceased fetus's property and passes to its heirs.
2
Identify the exception
The text immediately adds: 'the assailant does not inherit it.' This is the key exception: even if the assailant is an heir, he is excluded.
3
Understand the reason (talil)
The reason given: 'because it is compensation for his self.' The ghurrah is badal nafs (compensation for the person), not a mere fine. Therefore it is part of the fetus's estate.
4
Apply to the example
The example: a man strikes his wife's belly, causing stillbirth. The father's 'aqilah pays ghurrah, but the father (who is the killer) does not inherit. This confirms the rule: direct wrongful murder bars inheritance.
Note the distinction: direct murder (mubashir) vs. indirect (sabab); only direct bars inheritance.
5
Check the cross-madhhab status
The hanafi_position_box shows this is mukhtalaf fih (disputed) among schools. Some schools may allow the father to inherit if he did not intend the miscarriage. Hanafis maintain the strict bar.
This disagreement stems from different definitions of 'qatil' and its effect on inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وما يجب في الجنين موروث عنه لانه بدل نفسه فيرثه ورثته ولا يرثه الضارب حتى لو ضرب بطن امرأته فالقت ابنه ميتا فعلى عاقلة الاب غرة ولايرث منها لانه قاتل بغير حق مباشرة ولا ميراث للقاتل ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جنین میں جو غرہ واجب ہو گاوہ اس کی جانب سے میراث میں تقسیم کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے نفس کا بدل ہے تو جنین کے ورثا سکے وارث ہوں گے اور ضارب اس کا وارث نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر اس نے اپنی بیوی کے پیٹ پر مارا پس عورت نے ضارب کے بچہ کو ڈالا۔ حالانکہ وہ مردہ ہے تو باپ کی برادری پر غرہ ہے اور باپ اس غرہ میں وارث نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ ناحق مباشرت کے طریقہ پر قتل کرنے والا ہے حالانکہ قاتل کو میراث نہیں ملتی ۔ تشریح جنین کی جملہ صورت مذکورہ میں ضارب پر جو مال واجب کیا گیا ہے چونکہ یہ حسب تصریح سابق نفس کا بدل ہے لہذا اس کو جنین کے ورثا کے درمیان تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اگر ضارب بھی اس کا وارث ہو تو وہ میراث سے محروم رہے گا مثلاً کسی نے اپنی بیوی کے پیٹ پر لات ماری جس سے مردہ جنین باہر نکل پڑا تو یہاں ضارب کی برادری پر دیت واجب ہوگی اور ضارب اس غرہ میں میراث کا مستحق نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قاتل کو میراث نہیں ملا کرتی اور یہ قاتل ہے اور یہ قتل بھی قتل سبب نہیں بلکہ قتل مباشرت ہے اور قتل ناحق ہے فیہ مافیہ۔
He said: And whatever is obligatory in the case of a fetus is inherited from him, because it is compensation for his self. So his heirs inherit it, and the assailant does not inherit it. Even if he struck his wife's belly and she miscarried his son dead, then the father's 'aqilah owes a ghurrah, and the father does not inherit from it, because he is a direct murderer without right, and there is no inheritance for a killer. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the ghurrah that becomes obligatory for the fetus is distributed as inheritance from him, because it is the compensation for his self. So the fetus's heirs inherit it, and the assailant does not inherit it. For example, if a man struck his wife's belly and she miscarried his son, while it is dead, then the father's 'aqilah owes a ghurrah, and the father does not inherit from it, because he is a direct murderer without right, and a murderer does not inherit. Explanation: In all the mentioned cases of the fetus, the wealth made obligatory upon the assailant, since it is, as previously stated, compensation for the self, it will be distributed among the fetus's heirs. But if the assailant is also an heir, he will be deprived of inheritance. For example, someone kicked his wife's belly, causing a dead fetus to come out; here the assailant's 'aqilah owes the diyah, and the assailant is not entitled to inherit from this ghurrah because a murderer does not inherit, and he is a murderer, and this murder is not indirect but direct murder, and it is wrongful murder.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Quduri, explained by the commentator. It establishes that the ghurrah (compensation) for a miscarried fetus is the property of the fetus itself, considered as its 'self-compensation' (badal nafsihi). Therefore, it is inherited by the fetus's heirs according to the law of inheritance. The assailant (the one who caused the miscarriage) is specifically excluded from inheriting this ghurrah, even if he is a legal heir (e.g., the father). The reason is that the assailant is a direct (mubashir) and wrongful murderer, and a murderer is barred from inheriting from the victim. The commentary provides an example: if a man strikes his wife's belly, causing her to miscarry his own son stillborn, the father's 'aqilah (paternal male relatives) must pay the ghurrah, but the father himself does not inherit any part of it because he is the killer. This ruling is based on the general principle that a killer does not inherit from the victim.

Key Terms
غرہ (ghurrah): Fixed compensation for a miscarried fetus, payable by the assailant's 'aqilah.
قاتل مباشر (qatil mubashir): A direct killer who personally causes death, as opposed to an indirect cause (sabab).
بدل نفس (badal nafs): Compensation for the person himself, as opposed to compensation for a part or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, who inherits the ghurrah paid for a miscarried fetus?
A) The mother
B) The assailant if he is an heir
C) The fetus's heirs, not the assailant
D) The 'aqilah of the assailant

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah for a fetus is treated as the fetus's own property and is inherited by its heirs; the assailant is always excluded as a direct murderer.

Diyah for Fetus of Slave Woman: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presents ruling on diyah for male/female fetus of a slave woman and the Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the diyah of a male and female fetus of a slave woman, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The fetus is compensated for its own hypothetical value, not as a part of the mother.

This lesson examines a key dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the diyah for a miscarried fetus of a slave woman. The matn from Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi ruling, which assesses the fetus's own hypothetical value. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the fetus is a part of the mother and thus compensation should be based on the mother's value. We will explore the proofs, the Hanafi response, and the intra-Hanafi difference of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Learn the exact fractions for male and female fetuses of a slave woman as per the matn.
Male: half of one-tenth (1/20); Female: one-tenth (1/10) of the fetus's hypothetical value if born alive.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Identify why Imam al-Shafi'i holds that compensation should be one-tenth of the mother's value.
He considers the fetus a part (juz') of the mother.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi proof that the fetus is compensated for its own self (badal nafs), not as a limb (daman taraf).
No deficiency in the mother is required; a fixed amount is due.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Learn Imam Abu Yusuf's view that compensation should be based on the actual deficiency in the mother, analogizing to animal fetuses.
This is a minority view within the Hanafi school.

He said: And for the fetus of a slave woman, if it is male, half of one-tenth of its value if it were alive, and one-tenth of its value if it were female. And al-Shafi'i said: One-tenth of the mother's value, because it is a part from one perspective, and compensation for parts is taken in proportion to the origin. Translation: Al-Quduri said: For the fetus of a slave woman, if it is a boy, half of one-tenth of its value if it were alive, and one-tenth of its value if it is a girl. And al-Shafi'i said: One-tenth of the mother's value, because it is a part in a way, and compensation for parts is taken from the origin. Explanation: This was the detail for the fetus of a free woman. If it is a slave, then it is the slave of the owner of the slave woman, so its ruling is different. Therefore, if the fetus of a slave woman were alive, it would have a value. Then it is seen whether the fetus is male or female. If male, one-twentieth of its value is due; if female, one-tenth is due. This is the Hanafi school. Imam Shafi'i said: In any case, the mother's value is assessed, and one-tenth of the mother's value is due, because the fetus is a part of the mother (from one aspect, as mentioned). And where compensation for parts is obligatory, the amount is calculated from the origin, and the origin is the mother, so we have calculated from that and made one-tenth of her value due. The Hanafi proof: And our proof is that it is compensation for the self, because compensation for a limb is not obligatory except upon the appearance of deficiency in the origin, and that is not considered in compensation for the fetus. So it is compensation for the self, and thus it is assessed by the fetus's own self. Explanation: The consideration is of the fetus's value, not the mother's, because this compensation is for the fetus's self, not for the mother's limb. For where compensation for a limb is obligatory, it is considered how much deficiency occurred in the origin, then that much compensation is made obligatory. But here that is not considered; rather it is absolutely stated that one-tenth of the mother's value is due. Therefore, if no deficiency to the woman occurs from it, then no compensation should be due. Thus it is clear that this is compensation for the self, not for a limb. And when it is compensation for the self, its assessment will be according to the value of the self. The school of Imam Abu Yusuf: And Abu Yusuf said: Compensation for the deficiency is obligatory if the mother is deficient, analogizing to the fetus of animals. This is because, according to him, in the killing of a slave, the compensation is for the property, as we will mention, God willing. So the analogy is sound according to his principle. Explanation: This is the school of Imam Abu Yusuf, the gist of which is that the case of a slave woman and animals are equal. Thus, if someone killed someone's buffalo...
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage deals with the diyah for a fetus of a slave woman (umm al-walad or regular slave). The matn from Al-Quduri states the Hanafi ruling: if the fetus is male, half of one-tenth of its value if it were alive; if female, one-tenth of its value. This means that if a slave woman's fetus is miscarried, the assailant must pay a fraction of the value the fetus would have had if born alive, with a 2:1 ratio for male to female. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, holding that the compensation should be one-tenth of the mother's (slave woman's) value because the fetus is considered a part of the mother, and compensation for a part is based on the deficiency caused to the whole. The Hanafi response is that compensation for a fetus is not for a limb (part) but for the fetus's own self (badal nafs). They argue that if it were a limb, compensation would only be due if the mother's value decreased, which is not the case here; the ruling is fixed regardless of deficiency. Therefore, it must be compensation for the fetus's self, so it is based on the fetus's own value, not the mother's. The passage then mentions a third position from Imam Abu Yusuf, who analogizes to animal fetuses and requires compensation for the actual deficiency suffered by the mother (i.e., the decrease in her value). This is an intra-Hanafi difference. The text ends abruptly, but the gist is given.

Key Terms
نصف عشر (nisf 'ushr): Half of one-tenth, i.e., one-twentieth (1/20).
عشر ('ushr): One-tenth (1/10), applicable for a female fetus of a slave woman.
ضمان طرف (daman taraf): Compensation for injury to a limb or part, measured by the deficiency caused to the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the diyah for a male fetus of a slave woman?
A) One-tenth of the mother's value
B) One-twentieth of the fetus's hypothetical value if alive
C) Full diyah of a free male
D) One-tenth of the fetus's value

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school compensates a slave woman's fetus based on its own hypothetical value, with a 2:1 male-female ratio, rejecting the part-based analogy.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Compensation for the Fetus of a Slave Woman: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on compensation for slave woman's fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on compensation for a slave woman's fetus, explain the Hanafi proof distinguishing daman al-nafs from daman al-taraf, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the schools.

Core Idea
The compensation for a slave woman's fetus is based on the fetus's own value (Hanafi), not the mother's (Shafi'i), because it is compensation for the self, not a limb.

In this lesson, we examine a key dispute in diyat: how to determine blood money for a miscarried fetus when the mother is a slave woman. The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ fundamentally on whether the compensation is for the fetus's own life or as a part of the mother. You will learn the rationale behind each view and the practical difference it makes. Additionally, we will touch on Imam Abu Yusuf's unique position within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling context
Recognize that the ruling for a slave woman's fetus differs from a free woman's fetus. The fetus becomes property of the master, so its compensation is based on value.
2
State the Hanafi position
Recall that Hanafi school says: if male, 1/20 of the fetus's value; if female, 1/10. This is because the compensation is for the fetus's self (badal al-nafs).
3
State the Shafi'i position
Recall that Imam al-Shafi'i says: in all cases, 1/10 of the mother's value. This is because the fetus is considered a part (juz') of the mother.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Understand the distinction between daman al-taraf (limb) and daman al-nafs (self). Compensation for a limb requires a reduction in the principal (mother's value), but no such reduction is considered in fetus compensation; therefore, it must be for the self.
The key phrase is 'wa la mu'tabar bihi fi daman al-janeen' – no consideration of reduction.
5
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf and Abu Yusuf's view
The practical difference is the amount. Hanafi uses fetus's value, Shafi'i uses mother's value. Abu Yusuf adds: if the mother's value decreases, compensation for that decrease is due, analogizing to animals.
Abu Yusuf's view is intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

احناف کی دلیل
ولنا انه بدل نفسه لان ضمان الطرف لا يجب الا عند ظهور النقصان من الأصل ولا معتبر به في ضمان الجنين فكان بدل نفسه فيقدر بها ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ اس کے نفس کا بدل ہے اس لئے کہ طرف کا ضمان نہیں واجب ہوتا مگر اصول کا نقصان ظاہر ہونے کے وقت اور جنین کے ضمان میں نقصان اصل کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے تو ہو جائے گا یہ (ضمان جنین ) جنین کے نفس کا بدل تو ضمان کو مقدر کیا جائے گا نفس جنین کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح اصل لحاظ جنین کی قیمت کا ہوگا نہ کہ ماں کی کیونکہ یہ ضمان ، ضمان نفس جنین ہے ماں کے عضو کا ضمان نہیں ہے کیونکہ جہاں ضمانِ طرف واجب ہوتا ہے تو وہاں اس پر غور کیا جاتا ہے کہ اصل میں کتنا نقصان پیدا ہوا ہے پھر اتنا ہی ضمان واجب کیا جاتا ہے حالانکہ یہاں اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ مطلق فرما دیا گیا کہ ماں کی قیمت کا عشر واجب ہوگا۔ لہذا اگر عورت کا کوئی نقصان اس کی وجہ سے نہ ہوا تو پھر کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہونا چاہیئے ۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ یہ ضمان نفس ہے ضمان طرف نہیں اور جب یہ ضمان نفس ہے تو اس کی تقدیر نفس کی قیمت کے لحاظ سے ہوگی۔
امام ابو یوسف کا مسلک
و قال ابو يوسف يجب ضمان النقصان لو اتنقصت الام اعتبارا بجنين البهائم هذا لان الضامن في قتل الرقيق ضمان مال عنده ما نذكره انشاء الله تعالى فصح الاعتبار على اصله ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ ضمان نقصان واجب ہو گا اگر ماں کے اندر نقصان ہو چو پاؤں کے جنین پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ غلام کے قتل میں ضمان ماں کا ضمان ہوتا ہے ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم انشا اللہ ذکر کریں گے تو ابو یوسف کی اصل کے مطابق ( باندی کے جنین پر ) پر قیاس کرنا درست ہو گیا۔
Book of Diyat. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 15. Explanation: This was the detail of the fetus that falls from a free woman. If it was a slave woman, then it becomes a slave of the slave woman's master. So its ruling is different. Therefore, for a slave woman's fetus, if it were born alive, its value would be considered. Then it is seen whether the fetus is male or female. If male, one-twentieth of its value is obligatory; if female, one-tenth is obligatory. This is the Hanafi position. Imam al-Shafi'i said: In any case, the mother's value is assessed, and one-tenth of the mother's value is made obligatory because this is a part of the mother (in one respect as mentioned). And where compensation for parts is obligatory, the calculation of amount is based on the original, and the original is the mother. Therefore, we calculate from it and make one-tenth of the value obligatory.
Hanafi proof: 'And for us, it is a substitute for its self because compensation for a limb is not obligatory except when there is a reduction from the original, and this is not considered in the compensation for the fetus. So it is a substitute for its self, and it is estimated accordingly.' Translation: Our proof is that this is a substitute for its self because compensation for a limb is not obligatory except at the time of the appearance of deficiency in the original, and in the compensation for the fetus, no consideration is given to the deficiency of the original. So this (compensation for fetus) becomes a substitute for the self of the fetus, so the compensation will be estimated according to the self of the fetus. Explanation: The consideration will be of the fetus's value, not the mother's, because this compensation is compensation for the self of the fetus, not compensation for a limb of the mother. Because where compensation for a limb is obligatory, there it is considered how much deficiency has occurred in the original, then that much compensation is made obligatory, whereas here no such consideration is given, rather it is absolutely decreed that one-tenth of the mother's value is obligatory. Therefore, if the woman suffers no loss because of it, then no compensation should be obligatory. Hence it is known that this is compensation for the self, not compensation for a limb. And when it is compensation for the self, its estimation will be according to the value of the self.
Imam Abu Yusuf's position: 'And Abu Yusuf said: Compensation for the reduction is obligatory if the mother is reduced, by analogy with the fetus of animals. This is because the guarantor in killing a slave is compensation of property according to him, as we will mention, Allah willing, so the analogy upon his principle is sound.' Translation: And Abu Yusuf said that compensation for reduction is obligatory if there is a reduction in the mother, by analogy with the fetus of quadrupeds. And this is because the compensation in killing a slave is property compensation according to him, according to the detail we will mention, Allah willing. So the analogy upon his principle (on the slave woman's fetus) becomes valid.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the diyah (blood money) for the fetus of a slave woman. It begins by summarizing the earlier discussion on a free woman's fetus, then moves to the slave woman's case. The Hanafi school holds that the compensation is based on the fetus's own value: if the fetus were male, one-twentieth of that value; if female, one-tenth. This is because the compensation is for the self (nafs) of the fetus, not a limb (taraf) of the mother. The Shafi'i school, however, argues that the fetus is a part of the mother, so one-tenth of the mother's value is due in all cases, regardless of the fetus's gender. The Hanafi proof is that compensation for a limb is only payable when there is a reduction in the principal (the mother's value), but here no such condition is considered; thus, the compensation is for the fetus's own life, and its amount is determined by the fetus's value. Imam Abu Yusuf offers a third opinion, analogizing to animals: if the mother's value decreases, compensation for that decrease is due. This is based on his principle that the guarantee in killing a slave is property compensation. The passage presents these views and their rationales, with the Hanafi position being the relied-upon view of the school.

Key Terms
ضمان الطرف (daman al-taraf): Compensation for injuring a limb, which is only due when there is a reduction in the value of the principal (the whole body).
جنین (janeen): The unborn offspring, a fetus.
بدل نفسه (badal nafsihi): A substitute or compensation for the self (life) of the fetus, as opposed to compensation for a limb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the compensation for a male fetus of a slave woman?
A) One-tenth of the mother's value.
B) One-twentieth of the fetus's value.
C) One-tenth of the fetus's value.
D) Full diyah of a free person.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, compensation for a slave woman's fetus is based on the fetus's own value (1/20 male, 1/10 female), not the mother's value, because it is compensation for the self, not a limb.

Compensation for a Fetus Struck in Slavery, Born Free, Then Dies
Hanafi ruling for fetus freed after assault, born alive then dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a fetus struck while a slave but freed before death, and explain why value is obligatory instead of diyah.

Core Idea
The cause (strike) in slavery determines compensation: value, not diyah, even if death occurs after freeing.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Imam Muhammad's Jami' al-Saghir: a pregnant slave is struck, her fetus is freed by the master, then born alive but dies from the strike. The Hanafi position is that the striker must pay the full market value of the fetus as a living slave (qimatan hayyan), not the diyah of a free person. The reasoning hinges on the time of the cause (sabab) being the strike, which occurred while the fetus was still a slave. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of giving weight to the state at the time of the causative act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key elements of the case
Pinpoint the four events in order: strike (darb), freeing (itq), birth alive, then death from injuries.
The order matter: strike precedes freeing.
2
Recognize the conflict in legal states
The cause (strike) occurred in slavery, but the death occurred in freedom. This creates tension: if we look only at death, diyah seems appropriate; if we look only at the cause, value (qimah) for a slave is due.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle on causation
Hanafi law gives priority to the time of the cause (sabab) for determining the type of compensation. Since the fatal blow was struck while the fetus was a slave, the obligation is value, not diyah.
This is based on the maxim 'al-ibrah li al-sabab' (consideration is given to the cause).
4
Combine cause and effect for the amount
Because the fetus died alive (not miscarried), the compensation is the full living value of a slave, not a lesser amount like ghurrah. This respects both the state of the cause (slavery) and the state of destruction (alive).
If the fetus had died before birth, only ghurrah (500 dirhams) would apply for a free fetus, or value for a slave.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The explicit text from Muhammad in Jami' al-Saghir is the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah): full living value due.
Intra-Hanafi variant exists but is not the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فإن ضربت فاعتق المولى ما فى بطنها ثم القته حيا ثم مات ففيه قيمته حيا ولا تجب الدية وان ماتت بعد العتق لانه قتله بالضرب السابق وقد كان فى حالة الرق فلهذا تجب القيمة دون الدية وتجب قيمته حيا لانه صار قاتلا اياه وهو حى فنظرنا إلى حالتي السبب والتلف ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا پس اگر باندی ماری گئی پس آقا نے جو اس کے پیٹ میں ہے اس کو آزاد کر دیا پھر اس نے اس کو زندہ گرایا پھر وہ مر گیا تو اس میں اس کی قیمت ہے اور دیت واجب نہ ہوگی اگر چہ وہ عتق کے بعد مرا ہے اس لئے کہ ضارب نے اس کو ضرب سے مارا ہے جو عتق پر مقدم ہے حالانکہ ضرب رقیت کی حالت میں تھی اسی وجہ سے قیمت واجب ہوگی نہ کہ دیت اور اس کی زندہ کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ ضارب اس کا قاتل ہوا ہے اس حال میں کہ وہ زندہ تھا تو ہم نے سبب اور تالف دونوں کی حالتوں کی طرف دیکھا۔ تشریح اگر زید نے خالد کی باندی کے پیٹ پر لات ماری اور ابھی تک کچھ نہیں ہوا تھا تو خالد نے اعلان کیا کہ جو اس باندی کے پیٹ میں ہے میں نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا اس کے بعد باندی نے زندہ جنین گرایا تو یہاں قاعدہ میں دیت واجب ہونی چاہئے کیونکہ وقت موت جنین آزاد ہے اور بعد خروج زندہ ہے۔ مگر دیت واجب نہیں کی گئی بلکہ قیمت واجب کی گئی ہے جو اس کے آقا کو ملے گی یعنی اگر وہ زندہ ہوتا تو اس کی جو قیمت ہوتی وہ قیمت ضارب پر واجب کر دی جائے گی اگر چہ یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ اس کی موت آزادی کی حالت میں واقع ہوئی ہے۔ لیکن ضرب جو اس کے لئے مہلک بنی ہے وہ بحالت رقیت واقع ہوئی ہے لہذا اس کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے قیمت واجب کی گئی ہے دیت نہیں اور چونکہ ضارب نے اسے زندہ کو مارا ہے اس لئے زندہ کی قیمت واجب کی گئی ہے۔ چونکہ یہاں سبب اور تکلف کی حالتوں میں تعارض ہے حالت سبب کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ قیمت واجب ہو کیونکہ وہ اس وقت غلام ہے اور حالت تلف کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ دیت واجب ہو کیونکہ وہ اس وقت زندہ ہے۔ تو ہم نے بر بناء احتیاط دونوں کو جمع کر دیا اور کہا کہ قیمت واجب ہے حالت سبب کی رعایت ہے اور زندہ کی قیمت واجب ہے حالت تلف کی رعایت سے ورنہ اگر حالت تلف کا اعتبار نہ ہوتا تو صرف غرہ واجب ہوتا۔ ایک قول کے مطابق مذکورہ تفصیل شیخین کے قول کے مطابق ہے وقيل هذا عندهما وعند مد تجب قيمته ما بين كونه مضروبا الى كونه غير مضروب لان الاعتاق قاطع
He (Muhammad) said in Jami' al-Saghir: If the slave woman is struck, then the master frees what is in her womb, then she delivers it alive, then it dies, then its value (as a living slave) is due, and the diyah is not obligatory even if it died after the freeing, because he killed it by the prior strike, and it was in the state of slavery. For this reason, the value is obligatory, not diyah. And its value when alive is obligatory because he became its killer while it was alive. So we looked at both the state of the cause and the state of the destruction. Translation: Muhammad said in Jami' al-Saghir: If a slave woman is struck, then the master frees what is in her womb, then she delivers it alive, then it dies, then for it is its value (as a living slave) and diyah is not obligatory, even if it died after the freeing, because the striker killed it by the prior strike, which preceded the freeing, and the strike occurred in the state of slavery. For this reason, the value is obligatory, not diyah. And its value when alive is obligatory because the striker became its killer while it was alive. So we considered both the states of the cause and the destruction. Explanation: If Zaid kicked the belly of Khalid's slave woman and nothing had happened yet, then Khalid declared that he freed what is in the belly of this slave woman. Thereafter, the slave woman delivered a live fetus. Then according to the rule, diyah should be obligatory because at the time of death the fetus is free and after birth it is alive. But diyah is not made obligatory; rather, the value is made obligatory, which will go to its master, i.e., if it had lived, its value would be what it would be; that value is made obligatory on the striker. Although it is apparent that its death occurred in a state of freedom. But the strike that was fatal occurred in a state of slavery, so considering that, the value is made obligatory, not diyah. And since the striker killed it while it was alive, the value when alive is made obligatory. Since here the states of cause and destruction conflict: the state of the cause requires that the value be obligatory because at that time it was a slave, and the state of destruction requires that diyah be obligatory because at that time it was alive. So we combined both by precaution and said value is obligatory, considering the state of cause, and the value when alive is obligatory considering the state of destruction. Otherwise, if the state of destruction were not considered, only the ghurrah would be obligatory. According to one saying, the mentioned detail is according to the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?), and it is said: according to them, its value between being struck and not being struck is obligatory because the freeing is a cut-off.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents a specific ruling from Muhammad al-Shaybani's Jami' al-Saghir, dealing with a conflict between the state of the cause (the strike) and the state of the destruction (death). The scenario: a slave woman is struck on the belly, causing injury. Before the fetus is born, the master frees the fetus. Later, the fetus is born alive but dies from the injury. The ruling: the striker must pay the value (qimah) of the fetus as if it were a living slave, not the diyah of a free person. The reasoning is that although the death occurred when the fetus was free, the fatal blow was struck while the fetus was still a slave. The cause (darb) is the determinant factor. However, because the fetus was alive at death, the compensation is the full value of a living slave, not just the ghurrah (the fixed compensation for a miscarried fetus). The commentary also notes a variant view (qil) attributed to the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) that the value should be the difference between the value before being struck and after, because the freeing interrupts the chain of causation. The passage illustrates the Hanafi principle of considering the time of the cause when determining whether diyah or value is due, and demonstrates a careful reconciliation of conflicting factors by combining considerations of both cause and effect to avoid injustice.

Key Terms
ضرب (darb): The act of striking, which is the cause (sabab) of the death.
عتق (itq): Freeing of the slave; here, it occurs after the strike but before death.
قيمة (qimah): The monetary value of the fetus as if it were a living slave.
غرہ (ghurrah): A fixed compensation of 500 dirhams for a miscarried fetus of a free woman. Here, it is mentioned as a lesser amount that would apply if the death had been before birth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a slave woman is struck, her fetus is freed by the master, then born alive and dies, what compensation is due?
A) Full diyah of a free person.
B) The value of the fetus as a living slave.
C) Only the ghurrah (500 dirhams).
D) One-tenth of the mother's value.

Key Takeaway
When a fetus is struck in slavery but dies after being freed, Hanafi law requires compensation of its full living value, not diyah, because the cause (strike) occurred in slavery.

Intra-Hanafi Difference: The Value as Difference Before and After Strike
Intra-Hanafi dispute on value calculation when freeing occurs after strike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the alternative Hanafi view that compensation is the difference in value due to the strike, and evaluate why the majority position takes the full living value.

Core Idea
Some Hanafis subtract the value after the strike, treating the freeing as a causal cut-off—a minority view.

This lesson explores a variant opinion within the Hanafi school regarding the same case from Jami' al-Saghir. While the majority ruling imposes the full living value, another position (attributed to the two shaykhs) holds that the compensation should be only the difference between the fetus's value immediately after the strike and its value before the strike. This disagreement turns on whether the freeing (itq) after the strike severs the causal chain, limiting liability to the direct consequence of the assault.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi ruling
As per Muhammad's explicit text: the striker pays the full living value of the fetus (qimatan hayyan).
This is the mufta bihi.
2
Identify the variant view
The passage mentions: 'qimatan ma baina kaunihi madruban ila kaunihi ghayr madrub' – the value between being struck and not being struck, i.e., the depreciation caused by the strike.
This is attributed to 'the two shaykhs' (possibly Abu Yusuf and Muhammad himself in another report?).
3
Understand the reasoning for the variant
The freeing (itq) is considered a cut-off (qati'). After the freeing, the fetus is no longer property of the master, so the striker's liability cannot extend to the full value that existed after the freeing. He is only liable for the injury he inflicted while it was still a slave.
This view treats the freeing as a novation that limits damages to pre-freeing loss.
4
Compare the two views: scope of liability
Majority: liability attaches to the cause (strike) for the full value as a living slave because the fatal blow was struck in slavery; the freeing is irrelevant. Variant: liability is limited to the injury actually caused before the freeing, i.e., the reduction in value.
The difference is in how to measure damages, not in the type (value vs diyah).
5
Identify the tarjih
The explicit text of Muhammad (Jami' al-Saghir) is relied upon. The variant is acknowledged but not operative in fatwa.
Some later works (e.g., al-Hidayah) may discuss this difference.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage presents a specific ruling from Muhammad al-Shaybani's Jami' al-Saghir, dealing with a conflict between the state of the cause (the strike) and the state of the destruction (death). The scenario: a slave woman is struck on the belly, causing injury. Before the fetus is born, the master frees the fetus. Later, the fetus is born alive but dies from the injury. Key Terms
ضرب (darb): The act of striking, which is the cause (sabab) of the death.
عتق (itq): Freeing of the slave; here, it occurs after the strike but before death.
قيمة (qimah): The monetary value of the fetus as if it were a living slave.
قاطع (qati'): A cut-off; here, the freeing is described as something that severs the causal chain of liability.

What is the key difference between the majority Hanafi view and the variant view on compensation for a fetus struck in slavery then freed?
A) Majority says diyah, variant says value.

C) Majority says no compensation, variant says ghurrah.
D) Majority says value of a dead slave, variant says value of a free person.

Key Takeaway

Compensation for a Fetus: Assaulted as Slave, Emancipated, then Dies Free
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for a fetus caused while a slave, then freed and dying free.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sahibayn's ruling on compensation when a fetus is struck before emancipation, freed, born alive, then dies, and distinguish it from Imam Muhammad's view by identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When cause (blow) in slavery but death in freedom, Hanafis combine: value of slave alive, not diyah.

This passage presents a nuanced case in Hanafi criminal law: a pregnant slave is struck, the master then frees the fetus, the fetus is born alive, but later dies from the injury. Should the striker pay full diyah (blood-money for a free person) or the value of a slave (qimah)? The Hanafi school is divided internally, with the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) holding one view and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holding a different view in his individual capacity. Understanding this dispute requires careful analysis of the temporal interplay between the cause of death (the blow) and the moment of death (post-emancipation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal scenario
State the sequence: pregnant slave struck, master frees fetus, live birth, death from injury. Recognize the two conflicting time points: blow (in slavery) and death (in freedom).
2
State the Sahibayn's ruling and its rationale
The Sahibayn rule that the striker owes the full value of the fetus as a living slave (qimatuhu hayyan). This combines the state of the cause (slavery → value) with the state of destruction (alive → value alive, not ghurrah). They consider the blow as the effective cause and treat emancipation as not cutting off sirayah.
3
State Imam Muhammad's dissenting view
Imam Muhammad holds that only the depreciation in value due to the blow is owed (the difference between its value before and after the strike). His reasoning: emancipation cuts off sirayah (ongoing lethal effect), so the striker is liable only for the injury, not the full value as if the death were caused after emancipation.
4
Contrast the two views and their proofs
The key point of dispute is the effect of emancipation on sirayah. The Sahibayn do not see emancipation as interrupting causation; Imam Muhammad does. This leads to a thamarah al-khilaf: the amount of compensation differs drastically.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
The passage indicates that the Sahibayn's view is the relied-upon position, as it is recorded in al-Jami' al-Saghir (Zahir al-Riwayah). Imam Muhammad's view is considered a nawadir (rare transmission) and is not the basis for fatwa.

Source Text

باند ماری گئی آقا نے اس کے پیٹ میں جو تھا اُسے آزاد کر دیا اس سے باندی نے زندہ بچہ ڈالا پھر وہ مرگئی، دیت واجب ہوگی یا نہیں
قال فإن ضربت فاعتق المولى ما فى بطنها ثم القته حيا ثم مات ففيه قيمته حيا ولا تجب الدية وان ماتت بعد العتق لانه قتله بالضرب السابق وقد كان فى حالة الرق فلهذا تجب القيمة دون الدية وتجب قيمته حيا لانه صار قاتلا اياه وهو حى فنظرنا إلى حالتي السبب والتلف ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا پس اگر باندی ماری گئی پس آقا نے جو اس کے پیٹ میں ہے اس کو آزاد کر دیا پھر اس نے اس کو زندہ گرایا پھر وہ مر گیا تو اس میں اس کی قیمت ہے اور دیت واجب نہ ہوگی اگر چہ وہ عشق کے بعد مرا ہے اس لئے کہ ضارب نے اس کو ضرب سے مارا ہے جو عشق پر مقدم ہے حالانکہ ضرب رقیت کی حالت میں تھی اسی وجہ سے قیمت واجب ہوگی نہ کہ دیت اور اس کی زندہ کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ ضارب اس کا قاتل ہوا ہے اس حال میں کہ وہ زندہ تھا تو ہم نے سبب اور تالف دونوں کی حالتوں کی طرف دیکھا۔ تشریح اگر زید نے خالد کی باندی کے پیٹ پر لات ماری اور ابھی تک کچھ نہیں ہوا تھا تو خالد نے اعلان کیا کہ جو اس باندی کے پیٹ میں ہے میں نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا اس کے بعد باندی نے زندہ جنین گرایا تو یہاں قاعدہ میں دیت واجب ہونی چاہئے کیونکہ وقت موت جنین آزاد ہے اور بعد خروج زندہ ہے۔ مگر دیت واجب نہیں کی گئی بلکہ قیمت واجب کی گئی ہے جو اس کے آقا کو ملے گی یعنی اگر وہ زندہ ہوتا تو اس کی جو قیمت ہوتی رہی قیمت ضارب پر واجب کر دی جائے گی اگر چہ یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ اس کی موت آزادی کی حالت میں واقع ہوئی ہے۔ لیکن ضرب جو اس کے لئے مہلک بنی ہے وہ بحالت رقیت واقع ہوئی ہے لہذا اس کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے قیمت واجب کی گئی ہے دیت نہیں اور چونکہ ضارب نے اسے زندہ کو مارا ہے اس لئے زندہ کی قیمت واجب کی گئی ہے۔ چونکہ یہاں سبب اور تکلف کی حالتوں میں تعارض ہے حالت سبب کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ قیمت واجب ہو کیونکہ وہ اس وقت غلام ہے اور حالت تلف کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ دیت واجب ہو کیونکہ وہ اس وقت زندہ ہے۔ تو ہم نے بر بناء احتیاط دونوں کو جمع کر دیا اور کہا کہ قیمت واجب ہے حالت سبب کی رعایت ہے اور زندہ کی قیمت واجب ہے حالت تلف کی رعایت سے ورنہ اگر حالت تلف کا اعتبار نہ ہوتا تو صرف غرہ واجب ہوتا۔
ایک قول کے مطابق مذکورہ تفصیل شیخین کے قول کے مطابق ہے
وقيل هذا عندهما وعند مد تجب قيمته ما بين كونه مضروبا الى كونه غير مضروب لان الاعتاق قاطع للسراية على ما يأتيك من بعد ان شاء الله تعالى.
ترجمہ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ شیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور محمدؐ کے نزدیک اس کی قیمت واجب ہو گی اس تفاوت کے مطابق جو اس کے مضروب اور غیر مضروب ہونے کے درمیان ہے اس لئے کہ اعتاق سرایت کو روکنے والا ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو بعد میں تیرے سامنے آئے گی انشاء اللہ تعالی۔
تشریح بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ تفصیل مذکور شیخین کے مسلک کے مطابق ہے اور امام محمد کا مسلک اور ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یہ جنین کی غیر مضروب ہوتا تو مثلاً اس کی قیمت ہزار روپے تھی اور مضروب ہونے کی صورت میں آٹھ سوروپے ہے تو ان دونوں کے درمیان دوسو روپے کا تفاوت ہے یہی تفاوت واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مضرب موت مانع سرایت ہے اسی طرح امام محمد کے نزدیک اعتاق بھی قاطع سرایت ہے لہذا بعد عتق ضرب سابق کی سرایت کا دروازہ بند ہو گیا۔ باب فى جناية المملوک والجنایۃ علیہ میں اس کی تفصیل آ رہی ہے۔
A slave woman was struck; her master freed what was in her womb; then she gave birth to a living child; then it died. Is diyah obligatory or not? He said: If she is struck and the master frees what is in her womb, then she delivers it alive, then it dies, then its value alive is due, and diyah is not obligatory, even if it died after emancipation, because he killed it by the prior blow and it was in a state of slavery; thus value is obligatory, not diyah, and its value alive is due because he became its killer while it was alive. So we looked at the states of the cause and the destruction. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: So if the slave woman is struck, then the master frees what is in her womb, then she delivers it alive, then it dies, then its value is due, and diyah is not obligatory, even if it died after emancipation, because the striker killed it by the blow that preceded the emancipation, while the blow was in a state of slavery; for that reason value is obligatory, not diyah, and its value alive is obligatory because the striker became its killer while it was alive. So we considered both the state of the cause and the state of destruction. Explanation: If Zayd kicked Khalid's slave woman in the belly and nothing had happened yet, then Khalid announced, 'I have freed what is in this slave woman's womb,' then the slave woman delivered the fetus alive, then by the rule diyah would be obligatory because at the time of death the fetus is free and after birth it is alive. But diyah was not made obligatory; rather value was made obligatory, which goes to its master: that is, if it had been alive its value would be such, so that value is imposed on the striker, even though it is apparent that its death occurred in a state of freedom. But the blow that was fatal occurred in a state of slavery, so considering that, value is obligatory, not diyah. And since the striker killed it alive, the value alive is obligatory. Since there is a conflict between the states of cause and destruction: the state of cause requires that value be obligatory because at that time it is a slave, and the state of destruction requires that diyah be obligatory because at that time it is free. So we combined both out of caution and said: value is obligatory in consideration of the state of cause, and the value alive is obligatory in consideration of the state of destruction; otherwise, if the state of destruction were not considered, only ghurrah would be obligatory. According to one opinion, the aforementioned detail accords with the saying of the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And it is said that this is according to them, and according to Muhammad (al-Shaybani) its value is obligatory between its being struck and not struck, because emancipation cuts off the continuing effect (sirayah), as will come after you, God willing. Translation: And it is said that this is according to the two shaykhs, and according to Muhammad its value is obligatory in the difference between its being struck and not struck, because emancipation prevents continuation (sirayah), according to the detail that will come before you later, God willing. Explanation: Some have said that the mentioned detail is according to the madhhab of the two shaykhs, and Imam Muhammad's madhhab is different: he says that if this fetus were not struck, for example its value would be a thousand rupees, and in the condition of being struck it is eight hundred rupees, then between them there is a difference of two hundred rupees; that difference is obligatory. Because the striking that caused death is a barrier to sirayah? Similarly, according to Imam Muhammad, emancipation also cuts off sirayah, so after emancipation the door of sirayah from the prior blow is closed. This detail comes in the chapter on injury to a slave and injury upon him.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a pregnant slave woman is struck in the abdomen by a third party, causing injury that later leads to the death of the fetus after it is born alive. Before the fetus is born, the master emancipates it. The question is whether the striker owes diyah (full blood money for a free person) or qimah (value of a slave). The Hanafi ruling, attributed to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), is that the striker owes the value of the fetus as if it were a living slave at the time of the blow, not diyah. The reasoning: the cause of death (the blow) occurred while the fetus was still a slave (since emancipation had not yet taken effect at the moment of the blow). The death itself occurred after emancipation, making it a free person at death. There is a conflict: the cause (blow) dictates slave compensation, the effect (death) dictates free compensation. The Hanafis combine both considerations: they impose the value of a free person? No, they impose the value of a slave (qimah) but calculated as if alive (since it was born alive), thus preserving the condition at the time of the cause. This is out of caution. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani has a different view: he holds that the striker owes only the difference in value between what the fetus would have been worth before the blow and after the blow (i.e., the depreciation due to injury), because the emancipation cuts off the ongoing effect (sirayah) of the blow. The passage then notes that this latter view is detailed in a later chapter.

Key Terms
قيمته حيا (qimatuhu hayyan): The market value of the fetus if it were alive at the time of the blow (as a slave)
سراية (sirayah): The ongoing lethal effect of a blow that causes death later
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave; here, the master frees the unborn fetus, which changes its legal status at the time of birth/death

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a slave woman is struck and her master later frees the fetus which is born alive then dies, what compensation is due according to the Sahibayn?
A) Full diyah for a free person
B) The value of the fetus as a slave (qimah) calculated alive
C) Only a ghurrah (one-tenth of diyah)
D) Nothing because the master freed it

Key Takeaway
When cause and effect span different legal statuses (slave vs. free), Hanafis (Sahibayn) combine: slave compensation (qimah) from the cause, and valuation as alive from the effect.

Expiation for Killing a Fetus: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on kaffarah for fetal death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on kaffarah for fetal death and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the nufus mutlaqah distinction.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is a punishment for absolute souls only; the fetus is not an absolute soul, so kaffarah is not wajib.

In this lesson, we examine a key ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a person who causes a miscarriage must expiate (kaffarah). The Hanafi school holds that kaffarah is not obligatory because it is a punishment reserved for fully born humans. The Shafi'i school argues that since the fetus has some soul, kaffarah is precautionarily required. We will explore the proofs and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and his school: kaffarah is not wajib for the fetus.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds kaffarah is wajib because the fetus is a soul in some respect (min wajh nafs).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Shafi'i reasoning: since the fetus has some soul, kaffarah is obligatory out of precaution (ihtiyatan).
Precaution is a valid principle in Shafi'i usul.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Present the Hanafi proof: kaffarah is a punishment (uqubah), and punishments are legislated only for absolute souls (nufus mutlaqah). The fetus is not an absolute soul, so kaffarah does not extend to it.
This is supported by the fact that full diyah is not due for a fetus; only ghurrah is wajib.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says no kaffarah; Shafi'i says it is wajib. The Hanafi school recommends voluntary kaffarah as an act of piety.
The mufta bihi (relied upon) position is the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا كفارة فى الجنين وعند الشافعي تجب لانه نفس من وجه فتجب الكفارة احتياطا ولنا ان الكفارة فيها معنى العقوبة وقد عرفت فى النفوس المطلقة فلا تتعداها ولهذا لم يجب كل البدل قالوا الا ان يشاء ذالك لانه ارتكب محظورا فاذا تقرب الى الله تعالى كان افضل له ويستغفر مما صنع .. ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جنین میں کفارہ نہیں ہے اور شافعی کے نزدیک کفارہ واجب ہے اس لئے کہ جنین من وجہ نفس ہے تو احتیاطاً کفارہ واجب ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفارہ میں عقوبت کے معنی ہیں اور عقوبت نفوس مطلقہ میں پہچانی گئی ہے پس ان سے متعدی نہ ہوگی ۔ اسی وجہ سے پورا بدل واجب نہ ہو گا مشائخ نے فرمایا مگر یہ کہ ضارب چاہے اس لئے کہ اس نے ایک منظور کا ارتکاب کیا ہے پس جب اس نے کفارہ کے ذریعہ اللہ کی جانب تقرب حاصل کیا تو یہ اس کے لئے افضل ہوگا اور اپنی حرکت سے استغفار کرے۔ تشریح جنین کا جو منمان ہوتا ہے وہ تو آپ کو معلوم ہو گیا اب بتاتے ہیں کہ جنین کی صورت میں کفارہ بھی واجب ہے یا نہیں؟ کیونکہ کفارہ عقوبت ہے اور یہ عقوبت نفوس مطلقہ کے بارے میں وارد ہوئی ہے اور یہ نفس مطلق نہیں ہے بلکہ من وجہ نفس ہے۔ لہذا عقوبت صرف نفوس مطلقہ ہی میں واجب ہوگی ۔ چونکہ نفس مطلق نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے تو بجائے پوری دیت کے غرہ واجب ہوا ہے۔ ہاں اگر احتیاطاً کفارہ دیدے تو بہتر ہے تا کہ باعث تقرب ہو سکے اور جنین کو ہلاک کرنے کا جو جرم اس نے کیا ہے اس سے استغفار کرے۔
He said: And there is no kaffarah (expiation) for the fetus. According to al-Shafi'i, it is obligatory because it is a soul in some respect, so kaffarah is obligatory out of precaution. Our proof is that kaffarah carries the meaning of punishment, and punishment is recognized for absolute souls (nufus mutlaqah), so it does not extend beyond them. For this reason, the full blood money (badal) is not obligatory. They (the scholars) said: unless he wishes, because he committed a prohibited act, so if he draws near to Allah through kaffarah, it is better for him and he seeks forgiveness for what he did. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And there is no kaffarah for the fetus. According to al-Shafi'i, it is obligatory because the fetus is a soul in some respect, so kaffarah becomes obligatory out of precaution. Our proof is that kaffarah has the meaning of punishment, and punishment is recognized for absolute souls (nufus mutlaqah), so it does not extend beyond them. For this reason, the full blood money (badal) is not obligatory. The mashayikh said: unless he wishes, because he committed a prohibited act, so if he seeks nearness to Allah through kaffarah, it is better for him and he seeks forgiveness for what he did. Explanation: You have learned what the ruling (hukm) of the fetus is. Now we inform you whether kaffarah is obligatory in the case of a fetus or not. Because kaffarah is a punishment, and this punishment is prescribed for absolute souls, and this is not an absolute soul but a soul in some respect. Therefore, punishment is obligatory only for absolute souls. Since it is not an absolute soul, instead of full diyah, ghurrah is obligatory. Yes, if he gives kaffarah out of precaution, it is better so that he may attain nearness and seek forgiveness for the crime of killing the fetus.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's Matn (via the commentary) presents the ruling on kaffarah (expiation) for causing a miscarriage or fetal death. The Hanafi position: kaffarah is not wajib (obligatory) for killing a fetus. The Shafi'i school holds it is wajib because the fetus is considered a human soul in some respects (min wajh nafs). The Hanafi proof: kaffarah is a punishment (uqubah); punishment for homicide is established only for absolute souls (nufus mutlaqah), i.e., a fully formed, born human. The fetus, while having the potential, is not a complete soul (nafs). Since the full diyah (blood money) is not due for a fetus (only ghurrah is due), kaffarah also is not due. However, it is recommended (mustahabb) for the perpetrator to voluntarily offer kaffarah as an act of piety and seeking forgiveness, because he has committed a prohibited act (irtikab mahzur).

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for killing a human being; normally wajib for accidental killing of a free Muslim
نفس مطلق (nafs mutlaq): An absolute soul, i.e., a fully formed and born human being with complete legal personhood

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi school rule regarding kaffarah (expiation) for causing the death of a fetus?
A) Kaffarah is wajib because the fetus is a human being
B) Kaffarah is not wajib because the fetus is not an absolute soul
C) Kaffarah is wajib only if the fetus was fully formed
D) Kaffarah is wajib if the mother was a free Muslim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that kaffarah is not wajib for fetal death because it is a punishment limited to absolute souls; voluntarily offering it is commendable.

Partially Formed Fetus Has Same Rulings
Ruling that a fetus with some formed parts equals a fully formed fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a partially formed fetus and explain the three proofs supporting its equivalence to a fully formed fetus for diyat and related laws.

Core Idea
A fetus with some visible creation is legally a soul – same diyat, ghurrah, and kaffarah as a complete fetus.

This passage concludes the section on fetal diyat by establishing the legal threshold for fetal personhood. The Hanafi school rules that once any part of the fetus's body has formed – such as a hand, foot, or head – it is considered a soul (nafs) and carries the same legal consequences as a fully formed fetus. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its three proofs: general hadith, analogy from other maternal rulings, and the distinction from pre-formational matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening phrase: 'And the fetus in which some of its formation has become apparent is like the complete fetus in all these rulings.' State the legal equivalence clearly.
The ruling covers all previously discussed rulings: diyat, ghurrah, kaffarah, etc.
2
Analyze the First Proof – General Hadith
The text says 'due to the general applicability of what we have narrated.' This refers to hadiths that speak of 'fetus' without qualification. Identify that the Hanafi school takes the unrestricted wording to include any fetus with some formation.
This is a dalil naqli from ahad hadith.
3
Analyze the Second Proof – Analogy from Other Rulings
The text argues that a partially formed fetus is already considered a child (walad) for matters like establishing motherhood, expiration of iddah, and postpartum period. Therefore, it should also be considered a child for diyat. Identify the far' (new case) and asl (analogous case).
This is a qiyas based on the common illa of being recognized as a child.
4
Analyze the Third Proof – Distinction from Clot and Blood
The text states that by this extent of formation, the fetus is distinguished from a clot ('alaqah) and blood (dam), so it is considered a soul. Recognize that before formation, no rulings apply; after formation, personhood is established.
This is a negative reasoning: if it weren't a soul, it would remain a clot, but it has features so it must be a soul.
5
Summarize and Note Practical Implications
Combine the three proofs to affirm that the threshold for fetal personhood in Hanafi law is when any part of the body is visible. Apply this to modern scenarios like miscarriage at 12 weeks with visible limbs.
This ruling is consistent across all Hanafi sources and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجنين الذي قد استبان بعض خلقه بمنزلة الجنين التام فى جميع هذه الاحكام لاطلاق ما رويناه ولانه ولد في حق امومية الولد وانقضاء العدة والنفاس وغير ذالك فكذا في حق هذا الحكم ولان بهذا القدر يتميز عن العلقة والدم فكان نفسا والله اعلم.
And the fetus in which some of its formation has become apparent is like the complete fetus in all these rulings, due to the general applicability of what we have narrated, and because it is a child (walad) in the matter of motherhood, expiration of iddah, postpartum period, and so forth; likewise in this ruling. And because by this extent it is distinguished from a clot and blood, so it is a soul (nafs). And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This concluding passage of the section establishes that a fetus that shows signs of some creation—such as limbs or features—is legally equivalent to a fully formed fetus in all the rulings discussed (diyah, ghurrah, kaffarah, etc.). The proof: 1) The general application of the hadith narrations that mention 'fetus' without condition. 2) Analogy: the partially formed fetus is already considered a 'child' (walad) for other rulings like establishing motherhood, completing iddah, and determining postpartum period (nifas). Therefore, it should also be considered a soul (nafs) for the purposes of diyat and related laws, distinguishing it from mere clots ('alaqah) or blood (dam) that have no rulings.

Key Terms
استبان بعض خلقه (istabana ba'du khalqihi): When some part of the fetus's creation has become apparent, e.g., hand, foot, or head
الجنين التام (al-janin al-tamm): The complete/fully formed fetus
العلقة (al-alaqah): A clot, the earliest stage of fetal development before formation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal status of a fetus that has some formed parts (like a limb) compared to a fully formed fetus?
A) It is considered like a clot and has no rulings
B) It is considered like a fully formed fetus in all rulings
C) It is considered a child only for inheritance but not for diyat
D) It is considered a free person if born alive

Key Takeaway
A fetus becomes a legal soul (nafs) for diyat and related rulings as soon as any part of its body is formed, based on general hadith, analogy, and distinction from pre-formational matter.

Kaffarah for a Fetus: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains the Hanafi vs Shafi'i ikhtilaf on kaffarah for fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kaffarah for a fetus, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and apply the Hanafi proof that kaffarah is restricted to absolute souls.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is not wajib for a fetus because it is not an absolute soul; punishment does not extend to incomplete souls.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether expiation (kaffarah) is obligatory for causing the death of a fetus. The Hanafi school argues that kaffarah is a punishment limited to complete human souls, while the Shafi'i school considers it obligatory as a precaution. Understanding this distinction clarifies the broader Hanafi principle that punishment follows the completeness of the soul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
The act is killing a fetus, and the dispute is whether kaffarah (expiation) is wajib.
Kaffarah is separate from diyat (monetary compensation).
2
State the Hanafi position
No kaffarah is obligatory. Only ghurrah (compensation) is wajib. Voluntary kaffarah is recommended.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Kaffarah contains punishment (uqubah), and punishment is established only for absolute souls (nufus mutlaqah). A fetus is a soul only from one aspect, not absolute.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
4
Analyze the Shafi'i counterargument
The Shafi'i school argues that since the fetus is a soul from one aspect, kaffarah is wajib as a precaution (ihtiyat).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Punishment cannot be extended beyond absolute souls; otherwise full diyah would be due, which is not the case. The text recommends voluntary kaffarah as an act of worship and repentance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جنین میں کفارہ ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
قال ولا كفارة فى الجنين وعند الشافعي تجب لانه نفس من وجه فتجب الكفارة احتياطا ولنا ان الكفارة فيها معنى العقوبة وقد عرفت فى النفوس المطلقة فلا تتعداها ولهذا لم يجب كل البدل قالوا الا ان يشاء ذالك لانه ارتكب محظورا فاذا تقرب الى الله تعالى كان افضل له ويستغفر مما صنع ..
والجنين الذي قد استبان بعض خلقه بمنزلة الجنين التام فى جميع هذه الاحكام لاطلاق ما رويناه ولانه ولد في حق امومية الولد وانقضاء العدة والنفاس وغير ذالك فكذا في حق هذا الحكم ولان بهذا القدر يتميز عن العلقة والدم فكان نفسا والله اعلم.
Is there kaffarah for the fetus or not? Statements of jurists. He said: And there is no kaffarah for the fetus, while according to al-Shafi'i it is obligatory because it is a soul from one aspect, so kaffarah is obligatory as a precaution. Our proof is that kaffarah contains the meaning of punishment, and punishment is known in absolute souls, so it does not extend beyond them; for this reason the full substitute (diyah) is not obligatory. They said: unless he wishes that, because he committed a forbidden act, so if he seeks nearness to Allah through it, it is better for him, and he should seek forgiveness for what he did. And the fetus whose some of its limbs have become apparent is in the status of a complete fetus in all these rulings due to the generality of what we narrated, and because it is a child regarding the right of being umm al-walad, completion of 'iddah, nifas, and other than that; similarly regarding this ruling, and because by this extent it is distinguished from the clot and the blood, so it is a soul. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: (1) whether kaffarah (expiation) is obligatory for killing a fetus, and (2) the legal status of a fetus whose limbs have begun to form. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position that no kaffarah is required for a fetus, contrasting with Imam al-Shafi'i who considers it obligatory. The Hanafi proof is that kaffarah is a punishment (uqubah) and punishment is established only for complete human souls (nufus mutlaqah). Since a fetus is not a complete soul but only a soul from one aspect (min wajh), punishment cannot extend to it. This is consistent with the rule that only the ghurrah (one-twentieth of full diyah) is due, not the full diyah. However, if the perpetrator voluntarily gives kaffarah as an act of worship and repentance, it is better. The passage then clarifies that a fetus whose limbs have formed (even partially) is treated as a complete fetus in all rulings. This is based on the generality of the hadith (which mentions 'fetus' absolutely) and on analogy with other rulings: such a fetus is considered a child for purposes of umm al-walad (mother of a child), completion of 'iddah, and nifas. Once limbs are apparent, it is no longer a clot (alaqah) or blood (dam), but a soul.

Key Terms
جنین (janeen): An unborn child, specifically one whose limbs have begun to form (after 120 days according to Hanafi fiqh).
کفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for unlawful killing; for Hanafis, it is a punishment tied to complete souls.
غرہ (ghurrah): Compensation for a fetus: one-twentieth of full diyah or a slave of specified value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on kaffarah for killing a fetus?
A) Kaffarah is wajib.
B) Kaffarah is not wajib; voluntary kaffarah is recommended.
C) Kaffarah is wajib only if the fetus had formed limbs.
D) Kaffarah is not wajib under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah is not wajib for killing a fetus because a fetus is not an absolute soul; voluntary kaffarah is recommended.

Legal Status of a Fetus with Formed Limbs
Explains the legal status of a partially formed fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a fetus with formed limbs is treated as a complete fetus in Hanafi fiqh, citing the hadith, analogy with umm al-walad/'iddah/nifas, and the distinction from a clot.

Core Idea
Once a fetus's limbs form, it is considered a soul and treated like a complete fetus in all legal rulings.

The second part of the passage addresses the legal status of a fetus whose limbs have become apparent. The Hanafi school equates such a fetus with a fully formed fetus in all rulings, based on the generality of the hadith, analogy with other areas of fiqh, and the fact that limb formation distinguishes it from a clot or blood. This lesson unpacks these proofs and their implications.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
A fetus with some formed limbs is treated as a complete fetus in all rulings.
This includes rulings on diyat, kaffarah, umm al-walad, 'iddah, nifas, etc.
2
Identify the first proof: generality of the hadith
The word 'janeen' in the hadith is general and includes any fetus, even if partially formed.
This is a dalil naqli.
3
Identify the second proof: analogy (qiyas)
Just as such a fetus is considered a child for umm al-walad, 'iddah, and nifas, so it is for this ruling (diyat/ghurrah and related).
The shared illa is that limb formation indicates the presence of a soul.
4
Identify the third proof: distinction from clot and blood
Once limbs form, it is no longer a mere clot (`alaqah) or blood, but a soul (nafs).
This is a rational proof based on physical development.
5
Connect to the earlier kaffarah discussion
Since it is treated as a complete fetus, the rulings on kaffarah and ghurrah are the same as for a fully formed fetus.
Thus, kaffarah remains not wajib, and ghurrah is wajib.

Legal Status of a Partially Formed Fetus
Explaining that a fetus with some limbs formed is legally treated as a complete fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a fetus with partially formed limbs is legally a complete human (nafs) and identify the proofs and implications.

Core Idea
A fetus with some formed limbs is legally a nafs for all rulings, not just a blood clot.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that a fetus whose limbs have begun to appear is not merely a clot of blood but has attained the status of a human soul. The ruling extends to matters of diyat, umm walad, iddah, and nifaas. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying the diyat rules in cases of fetal death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What is the ruling regarding a fetus that has some limbs formed but not fully developed?
The question arises in cases of miscarriage or abortion.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
Such a fetus is in the rank of a complete fetus (janeen tamam) and is considered a nafs (human soul).
This applies to all related rulings, not just diyat.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The hadith about 'janeen' uses absolute wording (mutlaq) which includes both fully and partially formed fetuses. The Hanafi principle: al-mutlaq yajri ala itlaqihi.
The hadith was previously narrated in the book; its general nature covers this case.
4
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
Actual formed limbs distinguish the fetus from congealed blood (mughalazah) and flowing blood (masfa), demonstrating it is a living soul.
This is why the fetus is treated as a nafs.
5
Apply to other rulings
The same ruling governs: woman becomes nafsa (postnatal bleeding), slave girl becomes umm walad, iddah is completed, and diyat is due for killing.
These are practical consequences listed in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور وہ جنین جس کے بعض اعضاء ظاہر ہو گئے ہیں وہ جنین نام کے درجہ میں ہے ان تمام احکام کے اندر اس حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں اور اس لئے کہ وہ بچہ ہے ام ولد ہونے کے حق میں اور عدت گزرنے کے حق میں اور نفاس وغیرہ کے حق میں پس ایسے ہی اس حکم میں اور اس لئے کہ اتنی مقدار سے وہ منجمد خون اور دم سے ممتاز ہو جائے گا تو یہ نفس ( آدمی ) ہوگا، واللہ اعلم۔ تشریح جب کچھ اعضاء جنین کے تیار ہو گئے تو وہ جنین نام کے درجہ میں ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں مطلق جنین کا ذکر ہے جو ان دونوں کو شامل ہے پھر وہ جنین جس کے کچھ اعضاء بن گئے ہوں باقی تمام احکام میں جنین تام کے حکم میں ہے تو یہاں بھی اس کو جنین تام کے حکم میں رکھا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جب کچھ اعضاء بن گئے تو اب وہ خون سیال اور خون منجمد نہیں رہا تو نفس کا درجہ اس کو دیا جائے گا۔ جس بچہ کے کچھ اعضاء مثلاً ہاتھ یا پیر یا ناخن وغیرہ بن گئے وہ بچہ کے حکم میں ہے اس کی وجہ سے عورت نفساء ہو جائے گی اور باندی ام ولد ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اس کی وجہ سے عدت گذر جائے گی۔ اور استقرار کے ایک سو بیس دن کے بعد اعضاء بن جاتے ہیں تفصیل کے لئے دیکھئے۔ شامی ص ۲۰۱ ج ۱
Translation: And the fetus whose some limbs have appeared is in the rank of a fetus (janeen) in all these rulings due to the generality of the hadith that we have narrated, and because it is a child, in the matter of becoming umm walad, and in the matter of completing the iddah, and in the matter of nifaas etc., so similarly in this ruling, and because to this extent it will be distinguished from congealed blood and blood, so it will be a soul (person). And Allah knows best. Explanation: When some limbs of the fetus are formed, then it is in the rank of a fetus, because in the hadith the absolute fetus is mentioned which includes both. Then the fetus whose some limbs have been formed, in all remaining rulings it is in the ruling of a complete fetus, so here too it will be placed in the ruling of a complete fetus. Because when some limbs are formed, then it is no longer flowing blood or congealed blood, so it will be given the rank of a soul. The child whose some limbs, for example hand or foot or nail etc., are formed is in the ruling of a child; because of it the woman becomes nafsa (postpartum bleeding) and the slave girl becomes umm walad, and because of it the iddah will pass. And limbs form after one hundred and twenty days of settlement. For details see Shami p. 201 vol. 1.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that a fetus whose limbs have partially formed is legally considered a complete fetus (janeen tamam) for all purposes. The proof is the general wording of the hadith about 'janeen' which applies to both fully formed and partially formed fetuses. The author explains that such a fetus is distinguished from congealed blood and therefore has the status of a living soul (nafs). This affects rulings on nifaas (postnatal bleeding), umm walad (the slave girl becoming the mother of her master's child), and completion of iddah. The passage also notes that limbs form after 120 days of pregnancy, referencing the Shami commentary.

Key Terms
جنين (janeen): An unborn child; specifically in this context, a fetus that has begun to form limbs.
نفس (nafs): A living human soul, giving full legal status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is considered a complete human being (nafs) for all rulings.
C) It is considered a complete human only for diyat.
D) It is not considered a human until full term.

Key Takeaway
A fetus with partially formed limbs is legally a complete human being (nafs) by Hanafi fiqh, based on the absolute wording of the hadith, and this status affects diyat, nifaas, umm walad, and iddah.
