Right to Remove Harmful Structures from Public Roads
Ruling with proof: the right to remove harmful public road structures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that any individual may remove harmful structures from a public road and explain the qiyas to common property that underlies this right.

Core Idea
Any person can remove a harmful structure from a public road because the right of passage is a common right, like co-ownership.

This lesson examines a ruling from Imam Muhammad in the Zahir al-Riwayah: if someone builds a privy, water spout, or bench on a public road causing harm, any member of the public has the right to remove it. The proof is analogized to common property where co-owners can remove unauthorized additions. Understanding this ruling clarifies the legal concept of common rights (huquq mushtaraka) and the permissibility of self-help in upholding them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What structures are being built? A privy (kaneef), water spout (mizab), water outlet (jarsham), or bench (dukkan). Ruling: it is permissible (mubah) for any person from the general public to remove them.
The ruling applies only to structures that cause inconvenience to passers-by.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is analogical reasoning (qiyas). The author compares the common right of passage to common property (milk mushtarak).
The qiyas is explicit in the text: 'as in common property'.
3
Analyze the qiyas structure
Break down: asl (common property) has the ruling that each co-owner can remove unauthorized additions; far' (public road) has the common right of passage; the illa (effective cause) is the shared right (haqq mushtarak); thus the same ruling applies.
The illa is jaliyyah (clear) because both involve a shared entitlement.
4
Note the scope and key terminology
The right applies to any structure that obstructs or harms the common passage. Understand the non-Arabic terms (kaneef, jarsham) that appear in the text.
The tanbeeh (note) clarifies that these words are borrowed (dakheel).

باب ما يحدثه الرجل في الطريق ترجمہ یہ باب ان چیزوں کے بیان میں ہے جن کو مر در استہ بنائے تشریح قتل کبھی مباشرت کے طریقہ پر ہوتا ہےاور کبھی بطریق سبب ہوتا ہے مباشرت کے احکام سے فراغت کے بعد قتل سبب کو بیان کر رہے ہیں اول کو اس لئے مقدم کیا کہ وہ بلا واسطہ ہے یا اس کا وقوع بکثرت ہے۔ کسی نے عام راستہ پر پاکخانہ، پر نالہ، چبوترہ بنایا جس سے گذرنے والوں کو تکلیف ہوتی ہوا سے ہٹانے کا کیا حکم ہے قال ومن أخرج إلى الطريق الأعظم كنيفا أو ميزابا أو جرصنا أو بنى دكانا فلرجل من عرض الناس أن ينزعه لأن كل واحد صاحب حق بالمرور بنفسه وبدوا به فكان له حق النقض كما فى الملك المشترك فإن لكل واحد حق النقض لـو أحـدث غيرهم فيه شيئا فكذا في الحق المشترك ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے بڑے راستہ کی طرف بیت الخلاء نکالا یا پر نالہ یا جرمن یا چبوترہ بنایا پس عوام الناس میں سے کسی بھی شخص کو یہ حق ہے کہ اس کو دور کر دے اس لئے کہ ہر ایک صاحب حق ہے بذات خود گذرنے میں اور اپنے چوپاؤں کے ساتھ تو ہر ایک کو توڑنے کا حق ہو گا جیسے ملک مشترک میں اس لئے کہ ہر ایک کو توڑنے کا حق ہوتا ہے اگر ان کے غیر نے اس میں کوئی چیز ایجاد کر دی پس ایسے ہی حق مشترک کے اندر۔ تشریح عام گذرگاہ میں تمام لوگوں کا حق ہے لہذا اگر کوئی عام گذرگاہ میں کوئی ایسی چیز بنا دے جس سے لوگوں کو تکلیف ہو اور ان کو نقصان پہنچے تو تمام لوگوں کو یہ حق حاصل ہو گا کہ مضرت کو دور کرنے کے لئے اس کو ہٹا دیں۔ جیسے ملک مشترک میں اگر کوئی ایسا تصرف کر دے تو اس کو دور کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح حق مشترک میں بھی کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور اس میں تمام لوگوں کا حق ہے کہ اس میں خود گذریں اور اپنے جانوروں کو لے جائیں لہذا اگر عام گذرگاہ پر بیت الخلاء یا چبوترہ پا پر نالہ وغیرہ لگا دیا تو تمام لوگوں کو حق ہوگا کہ اس کو الگ کر دیں۔ تنبیه کنیف ، بیت الخلاء، جرمن یہ لفظ اصل عربی نہیں ہے بلکہ دخیل ہے جس کی مختلف تغیر کی گئی ہے۔ -۲ وہ پانی کی نالی جو دیوار میں فٹ ہو جیسے ہمارے یہاں کھتی کہتے ہیں۔ ا برج کڑیوں کا وہ حصہ جس کو دیوار سے باہر نکال دیا گیا ہو۔ -۴- زیند -۵ راستہ کے دونوں طرف دیوار ہوں اور درمیان کو چھاپ دینا تا کہ ادھر سے ادھر جانے میں کوئی پریشانی نہ ہو بہر حال جو بھی معنی مراد لئے جائیں اس کو عام راستہ میں بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ( کمامر )
Chapter on what a man builds on the road. Translation: This chapter is about the things that are built on the road. Explanation: Killing sometimes occurs directly and sometimes indirectly. After finishing the rulings of direct killing, they are explaining indirect killing. The first is given precedence because it is immediate or more frequent. If someone builds a privy, spout, or bench on the public road that causes inconvenience to passers-by, what is the ruling for removing it? He (Muhammad) said: And whoever puts out towards the main road a privy, a spout, a water outlet, or builds a shop, then any person from the general public has the right to remove it, because every individual has a right of passage for themselves and their animals, so they have the right of removal, just as in common property: if someone other than the owners creates something, each co-owner has the right of removal. Similarly in this common right. Explanation: The general public has a right in the public thoroughfare. Therefore, if someone builds something that causes difficulty and harm, all people have the right to remove it to eliminate the harm. Just as in common property, if someone makes such a disposition, it is removed, so similarly in a common right it will be permissible. And all people have the right to pass through with themselves and their animals. So if on a public road a privy, bench, or spout is installed, all people have the right to remove it. Note: "Kaneef" means privy, "Jarsham" is not originally Arabic but a borrowed word with variant forms. 2) A water channel fitted in a wall, like we call "khati". 3) "Uruj": the part of a beam protruding from a wall. 4) "Zaynid"? 5) A roof covering between two walls to facilitate crossing. In any case, whatever meaning is intended, building it on a public road is not permissible.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof, establishing that any individual from the general public has the right to remove harmful structures built on a public road. The proof is analogical (qiyas) to common property (milk mushtarak): just as co-owners can remove unauthorized additions, so too can any person with the common right of passage remove obstructions. The passage defines key terms like kaneef (privy), mizab (spout), and jarsham (water outlet), noting that the latter is a borrowed word. The tanbeeh clarifies that building such structures on public roads is inherently impermissible if it causes harm.

Key Terms
كنيف (kaneef): A privy or toilet built on or protruding into a public road.
ميزاب (mizab): A spout or water gutter that drains water onto the road.
جرمن (jarsham or jarsun): A water outlet or channel fitted into a wall, resembling a modern downspout.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, who has the right to remove a harmful structure built on a public road?
A) Only the owner of the structure
B) The ruler or his representative
C) Any person from the general public
D) Only neighbours of the structure

Key Takeaway
Any individual can remove a harmful structure from a public road because the right of passage is a common right, analogous to co-ownership of property.

Permissibility of Using Structures on Public Roads if No Harm
Ruling with proof on permissibility of using public road structures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a structure built on a public road, identify the condition of no harm, and apply the hadith 'La darara wa la dirar' to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
Using a structure on a public road is permissible if harmless; harm makes it makruh tahrimi.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common urban issue: building structures like benches or shops that encroach on public roads. The Hanafi school balances private benefit with public interest. The key is whether the structure causes any harm to Muslims. The ruling relies on the famous hadith prohibiting harm and reciprocal harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
What is the ruling for the builder? What condition is attached? The text says it is permissible 'as long as it does not harm the Muslims.'
2
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
Why is passage analogous to using the structure? The builder has a right of passage, and passage is harmless. Anything similar in meaning (like sitting) is also permissible if harmless.
3
Apply the dalil
How does the hadith 'la darara wa la dirar' govern this case? The hadith prohibits causing any harm, so if the structure harms Muslims, it becomes prohibited.
4
Note the change in ruling when harm occurs
When does it become makruh tahrimi? If it causes harm, both building and benefiting become makruh tahrimi due to the explicit prohibition.
5
Recognize the three-part structure
The tanbeeh mentions three parts: (1) whether construction itself is permissible, (2) whether benefiting is permissible, (3) something else. Identify what is covered in this passage.
The text cuts off mid-sentence; only the first two parts are fully discussed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويسع للذى عمله أن ينتفع به ما لم يضر بالمسلمين لأن له حق المرور ولا ضرر فيه فيلحق ما في معناه به إذ المانع متعنت فإذا أضر بالمسلمين كره له ذالك لقوله عليه السلام لا ضرر و لاضرر في الإسلام ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے اس کو بنایا اس کے لئے گنجائش ہے کہ اس سے اتفاع کرے جب تک کہ مسلمانوں کے لئے مضر نہ ہو اس لئے کہ اس کے لئے مرور کا حق ہے اور مرور میں کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے تو جو چیز مرور کے معنی میں ہوگی مرور کے ساتھ لاحق ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ مانع ( روکنے والا ) متعنت ہے پس جب وہ مسلمانوں کے لئے نقصان دہ ہو تو یہ عمل ونفع ) اس کے لئے مکروہ ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے اسلام میں نہ ضرر ہے اور نہ ضرار ۔ تشریح عام گذرگاہ کی طرف کسی نے جو چیز بنائی اگر وہ عوام الناس کے لئے مضر نہیں ہے تو بنانے والے کو حق ہے کہ اس سے فائدہ اٹھائے کیونکہ بنانے والے کو اس میں گذرنے گذرنے کا حق ہے اس لئے کہ اس کے گذرنے سے کسی کا نقصان نہیں ہے تو جس چیز کے بنانے سے لوگوں کو نقصان نہ ہو وہ ضرور کے درجہ میں ہے اور مرور جائز ہے تو اب ایجاد ند کور بھی جائز ہوگی۔ اگر مضر نہ ہونے کے باوجود بھی کوئی اس کو روکتا ہے تو وہ محعت شمار کیا جائے گا ( مرسرکش ) ہاں اگر اس سے مسلمانوں کو نقصان پہنچے تو پھر اس کو بنانا بھی اور اس سے انتقاء بھی مکروہ تحریمی ہے کیونکہ ارشاد نبوی ہے "لاضرر ولا ضرار فی الاسلام" اسلام میں نہ ضرر ہے اور نہ ضرار، یعنی یہ جائز نہیں کہ کوئی کسی کو ابتداء نقصان پہنچائے اور نہ یہ جائز ہے کہ جزاء نقصان پہنچائے ضر را یک جانب سے ہوتا ہے اور ضرار دو جانب سے یعنی ضرار مضارة کے معنی میں جس نے آپ کو نقصان پہنچایا اس کو نقصان پہنچانا یہ بھی ضرار ہے اور قصاص وغیرہ میں اپنے حق سے زیادہ وصول کرنا بھی ضرار ہے۔ تنبیہ اس مسئلے کے تین جز ، ہیں۔ 1- احداث جائز ہے یا نہیں۔
He (Muhammad) said: And it is permissible for the one who made it to benefit from it as long as it does not harm the Muslims, because he has the right of passage and there is no harm in it; so anything that is in its meaning will be attached to it, because the one who prevents is obstinate. So when it harms the Muslims, this action (and benefit) is disliked for him due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'No harm and no reciprocating harm in Islam.' Translation: Muhammad said: And the one who built it has leeway to benefit from it as long as it is not harmful to Muslims, because he has the right of passage and there is no harm in passage; so whatever is in the meaning of passage will be annexed to it, because the preventer is obstinate. So when it becomes harmful to Muslims, this action (and benefit) is makruh for him due to the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'No harm and no reciprocating harm in Islam.' Explanation: If someone builds something towards the public road and it is not harmful to the general public, the builder has the right to benefit from it, because he has the right to pass through, and his passing causes no loss. So anything built that does not harm people is in the position of (right of) passage, and passage is permissible, so creating such a thing will also be permissible. If despite no harm someone stops him, that person will be considered obstinate. Yes, if it causes harm to Muslims, then building it and benefiting from it is makruh tahrimi, because of the prophetic saying: 'No harm and no reciprocating harm in Islam' meaning that it is not permissible for anyone to initially cause harm, nor to cause harm as reprisal. 'Darar' is from one side, and 'dirar' is from two sides, i.e. dirar is in the sense of mudarrah: harming the one who harmed you is also dirar, and in qisas etc. taking more than one's right is also dirar. Note: This issue has three parts: 1) Is construction permissible or not? ...
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage provides the second ruling of the chapter: the builder may use his structure (e.g., a bench or spout) as long as it does not harm Muslims. The proof is the hadith 'la darara wa la dirar' which prohibits both initial harm and retaliatory harm. The author explains that since the builder has a right of passage, and passage is harmless, anything analogous to passage (like sitting on a bench) is also permissible if harmless. If it causes harm, it becomes makruh tahrimi. The tanbeeh begins to enumerate three parts of the issue: (1) whether construction itself is permissible, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
ضرر (darar): Harm inflicted unilaterally by one person on another.
ضرار (dirar): Retaliatory harm or reciprocating harm, considered doubly wrong.
متعنت (muta'anniit): One who is obstinate or unnecessarily difficult; here, a person who prevents a harmless action without reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person who builds a bench on a public road that does not inconvenience anyone?
A) It is absolutely prohibited.
B) It is permissible to build and use it.
C) It is only permissible if the builder gets permission from the ruler.
D) It is makruh tanzih.

Key Takeaway
A structure on a public road is permissible as long as it causes no harm; if it causes harm, it becomes makruh tahrimi.

Building in a Non-Through Alley: Permission Required and Internal Hanafi Dispute
States ruling on constructing latrines/spouts in private alleys and the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on prevention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on constructing in a non-through alley and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the right to prevent or remove such construction.

Core Idea
In a non-through alley, even harmless construction requires unanimous permission because the alley is jointly owned.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines the ruling on building structures like latrines and spouts in a private alley (darb ghayr nafidh). It presents the general rule requiring permission from all residents, then delves into an internal Hanafi dispute on whether residents can prevent or remove such construction. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how joint ownership rights operate in Hanafi property law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property type
Recognize that a non-through alley is jointly owned by its residents, unlike a public road where individual ownership is legally presumed for ease of use.
The key distinction is the ability to obtain unanimous consent.
2
State the general ruling
According to the matn, no construction (spout, latrine, etc.) is permissible without permission from all residents, regardless of whether it causes harm.
Harmlessness is not a defense; permission is the sole criterion.
3
Follow the intra-Hanafi dispute
The three positions differ on the right to prevent or remove after construction: Abu Hanifa allows prevention and removal always; Abu Yusuf allows prevention only before construction and removal only if harmful; Muhammad denies any right if the construction is harmless.
The dispute centers on whether the right of co-owners is absolute or conditional on harm.
4
Understand the legal basis
The ruling is based on joint ownership, evidenced by the right of shuf'a (pre-emption). Since obtaining consent is possible, the property remains in shared ownership and any unilateral disposition is invalid without agreement.
This contrasts with public roads where obtaining all consents is impractical.

بنانے سے روکنا اور بنانے کے بعد اٹھانے کا حکم دینا۔
-۴- بنانے سے روکنا اور بنانے کے بعد اٹھانے کا حکم دینا۔
۔ اس کی ایجاد سے اگر کوئی مر جائے یا کوئی چیز ضائع ہو جائے اس کا ضمان ۔ تو اگر احداث سے لوگوں کا ضرر ہو تو اس کو بنانا جائز نہیں ہے لیکن اگر راستہ کی وسعت کی وجہ سے گذر نیوالوں کا کوئی نقصان نہ ہو تو بنانا جائز ہے۔ دوسرا مسئلہ ... بقول امام ابوحنیفہ اگر اس نے بادشاہ کی اجازت کے بغیر یہ بنایا ہے تو تمام لوگوں کو حق ہے کہ اس کو منع کریں اور اگر بنا چکا ہے تو اس کو ہٹوا د میں خواہ اس میں ضر ر ہو یا نہ ہو۔
اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ بنانے سے پہلے سب کو حق تھا کہ روکیں مگر بنانے کے بعد نہیں ( جب کہ مضر نہ ہو ) تو مانع معنت ہو گا۔ اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر وہ مضر نہ ہو تو بنانے سے پہلے اور بعد میں کسی کو انکار کا حق نہ ہوگا اور مانع متعنت نہ ہوگا۔ یعنی آخری مسئلہ یہاں مذکور ہے۔ اور تیسرے جزء کی تفصیلات آگے آرہی ہیں۔
مخصوص گلی میں پر نالہ ، بیت الخلاء بنانے کے لئے سب گلی والوں سے اجازت ضروری ہے
قال وليس لأحد من أهل الدرب الذى ليس بنافذ أن يشرع كنيفا ولا ميزابا إلا بإذنهم لأنها مملوكة لهم ولهذا وجبت الشفعة لهم على كل حال فلايجوز التصرف أضر بهم أو لم يضر بهم إلا بإذنهم وفي الطريق النافذ له التصرف إلا إذا أضر لأنه يتعذر الوصول إلى إذن الكل فجعل في حق كل واحد كأنه هو المالك وحده حكما كيلا يتعطل عليه طريق الانتفاع ولا كذالك غير النافذ لأن الوصول إلى إرضائهم ممكن فبقى على الشركة حقيقة وحكما
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور وہ گلی جو عام نہیں ہے اس کے اہل میں سے کسی کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ بیت الخلاء اور پر نالہ نکالے مگران سب کی اجازت سے اس لئے کہ یہ گلی ان کی مملوک ہے اسی وجہ سے ان کے لئے ہر حال میں شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے تو تصرف جائز نہ ہوگا خواہ وہ مضر ہو یا مضر نہ ہو مگر ان کی اجازت سے اور عام راستہ میں اس کو حق تصرف ہے مگر جب کہ وہ مضر ہو اس لئے کہ تمام کی اجازت کی جانب وصول مستعد رہے تو ہر ایک کے حق میں یوں قرار دیا جائے گا گویا کہ حکما وہی تنہا مالک ہے تا کہ اس پر انتفاع کا طریقہ معطل نہ ہو جائے اور غیر نافذ ایسا نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ان کے راضی کرنے تک رسائی ممکن ہے تو یہ ( غیر نافذ ) حقیقہ اور حکما شرکت پر باقی رہے گا۔ تشریح پہلی گفتگو عام راستہ میں تھی اور یہ اس راستہ میں ہے جو عام نہ ہو تو اس میں کوئی چیز بنانا جائز نہیں ہے خواہ وہ مضر ہو یا نہ ہو ہاں اگر وہ سب لوگ اجازت دے دیں جن کا وہ راستہ ہے تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ان تمام شرکا کا مملوک ہے اور دلیل ملک یہ ہے کہ تمام لوگوں کو اگر یہاں کوئی مکان بیچا جائے شفعہ پہنچتا ہے جس کی تفصیل کتا الشفعہ میں گذر چکی ہے۔ تو ان دونوں راستوں میں فرق یہ ہوا کہ یہاں سب کی اجازت ضروری ہے۔ اور اول میں عدم مضرت ضروری ہے وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ یہاں سب کو راضی کرنا ممکن ہے تو اسی پر مدار رکھا گیا اور اس راستہ میں حقیقہ اور حکماً سب کو برابر کا شریک مان کر رسته و مملوک مشترک شمار کیا گیا۔
The ruling on preventing construction and ordering removal after construction. Issue 4: Preventing construction and ordering removal after construction. If someone dies or something is lost due to its creation, the liability is on the creator. If the construction harms people, it is not permissible to build. But if the road is wide and passersby suffer no loss, construction is permissible. Second issue: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if he built without the king's permission, all people have the right to prevent him. If he already built, they can have it removed, whether harmful or not. Imam Abu Yusuf says: Before building, everyone had the right to prevent, but after building (if not harmful) they cannot, and anyone preventing would be stubborn. Imam Muhammad says: If not harmful, no one has the right to object before or after, and the objector would be stubborn. This is the last issue mentioned here. Details of the third part come later. For a private alley, permission from all residents is necessary to build a spout or latrine. He (Muhammad) said: No one from the residents of a non-through alley has the right to place a latrine or spout except with their permission, because it is owned by them. Hence shuf'a is established for them in all cases. So such disposition is not permissible, whether harmful or not, except with their permission. In a public road, he has the right to dispose except when harmful, because obtaining permission of all is difficult, so each is considered legally as if he is the sole owner, so that his way of benefiting is not obstructed. Not so for a non-through alley, because obtaining their consent is possible, so it remains in shared ownership actually and legally. Commentary: The first discussion was about a public road; this is about a road that is not public. In it, building anything is not permissible, whether harmful or not. Yes, if all those who own the road give permission, it is permissible. Because it is owned by all partners. The proof of ownership is that if a house is sold there, shuf'a is due to all partners, whose details passed in the Book of Shuf'a. So the difference between the two roads is that here everyone's permission is necessary, while in the first, non-harmfulness is necessary. The reason for the difference is that here it is possible to satisfy everyone, so the ruling is made on that. In this road, actually and legally, all are considered equal partners, and the road is considered shared property.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the ruling on constructing structures like latrines and spouts in a non-through alley (darb ghayr nafidh). It begins by presenting an internal Hanafi dispute on whether residents have the right to prevent construction or have it removed after construction. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if built without general permission, all residents have the right to prevent it, and if built, they can have it removed whether it causes harm or not. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that prevention is allowed only before construction; after construction, if harmless, removal cannot be demanded. Imam Muhammad holds that if harmless, no resident can prevent it at any stage. The text then quotes the matn from al-Hidayah: 'No one from the residents of a non-through alley has the right to place a latrine or spout except with their permission.' The reason given is that the alley is owned jointly by the residents, evidenced by the right of shuf'a (pre-emption) when a house is sold there. Therefore, any disposition requires unanimous permission, unlike a public road where only harmlessness is required because obtaining everyone's consent is impossible. The commentary clarifies the distinction: in a private alley, actual and legal shared ownership persists; in a public road, each is legally considered sole owner to avoid disruption of benefit. The proof of ownership is the shuf'a right mentioned in the Book of Shuf'a.

Key Terms
درب غير نافذ (darb ghayr nafidh): A dead-end alley or private road that does not lead to a public thoroughfare; owned jointly by its residents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a non-through alley (darb ghayr nafidh), what is the ruling on constructing a spout (mizab) without permission from all residents?
A) Permissible if it causes no harm.
B) Not permissible, even if harmless, because it is jointly owned.
C) Permissible only if the builder is a resident.
D) Permissible only after government permission.

Key Takeaway
In a non-through alley, construction requires consent of all co-owners, and under the relied-upon Hanafi position, violations can be reversed even if harmless.

Liability for Death from Falling Structure: Diyah on 'Aqilah
Ruling with proof: diyah on 'aqilah for death by falling structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for death caused by a falling structure on a public road and explain why the diyah is on the builder's 'aqilah.

Core Idea
The diyah for death caused by a protruding structure is on the builder's 'aqilah because the builder is a transgressive cause.

This lesson addresses a common urban scenario: a structure projecting over a public road collapses and kills a passerby. Who bears the blood money? The Hanafi ruling is clear: the diyah falls on the builder's 'aqilah (agnatic relatives). The reasoning rests on causation (tasabbub) and transgression (ta'addi) in occupying public airspace. We will unpack the proof and the general principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act: building a roshan (skylight/balcony) or mizab (spout) over a public road. The ruling: if it falls on a person and kills him, diyah is wajib on the builder's 'aqilah.
The ruling is not on the builder individually but on his 'aqilah.
2
Locate the cause and its basis
The builder is a cause (musabbib) of the death. The cause is transgressive (muta'addi) because he occupied airspace that does not belong to him – the public road's airspace.
This distinguishes it from an act where the cause is not transgressive (e.g., a natural collapse without negligence).
3
Derive the general principle (qa'idah kulliyyah)
Whoever is a transgressive cause of death owes diyah on his 'aqilah. This is the general rule from the text: 'wa huwa al-asl'.
This principle applies to similar cases (e.g., other structures mentioned 'aw nahwahu').
4
Apply the principle to the case
Here, the builder is the transgressive cause, so diyah is on his 'aqilah. The commentary emphasises this is the general rule, not an exception.
The ruling is consistent with other cases of indirect causation in diyat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راستے میں روشندان یا پر نالہ بنایا کسی انسان پر گرا اور وہ ہلاک ہو گیا دیت کس پر ہوگی
قال وإذا أشرع في الطريق روشنا أو ميزابا أو نحوه فسقط على إنسان فعطب فالدية على عاقلته لأنه مسبب لتلفه متعد بشغله هواء الطريق وهذا من أسباب الضمان وهو الأصل وكذالك إذا سقط شيء مما ذكرنا في أول الباب.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب کہ نکالا راستہ میں روشن یا پر نالہ یا اس کے مثل پس وہ کسی انسان پر گر گیا پس وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے تلف ہونے کا سبب متعدی ہے اس کے مشغول کرنے کی وجہ سے راستہ کی فضا کو اور یہ ضمان کے اسباب میں سے ہے اور یہی قاعدہ کلیہ ہے اور ایسے ہی جب ان چیزوں میں سے کوئی چیز گر گئی جن کو ہم اول باب میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ جو کسی کے قتل و ہلاک کا سبب ہوتا ہے تو اس کے عاقلہ پر اگر ہالک کی دیت واجب ہوتی ہے لہذا اگر کسی نے راستہ میں مذکورہ چیزوں میں سے کوئی چیز بنائی وہ کسی شخص کے اوپر گر جائے جس سے وہ مر جائے تو بنانے والے کے عاقلہ پر اس کی دیت واجب ہوگی اتنی بات سے مسئلہ صاف ہو گیا۔
تنبیه روشن کی تفسیر صاحب عین الہدایہ نے روشندان سے کی ہے اور بعض نے زمینہ سے اور بعض نے اس لینٹر سے جو راستہ پر ڈال دیا جائے تاکہ اس مکان سے دوسرے مکان میں جاسکے، بہر حال جو بھی تفسیر ہو حکم ایک ہی ہے۔
If a roshan or spout is built in the road, falls on a person, and he dies, who bears the diyah? He said: And if he places in the road a roshan or a spout or the like, and it falls on a person, and he dies, then the diyah is on his 'aqilah, because he is the cause of his destruction, being a transgressor by occupying the airspace of the road. This is among the causes of liability, and it is the general principle. Similarly, if something mentioned at the beginning of the chapter falls. Translation by Quduri: And when he places in the road a roshan or spout or the like, and it falls on a person, and he dies, then the diyah is on his 'aqilah, because he is the transgressive cause of his destruction by occupying the airspace of the road. This is among the causes of liability, and it is the general rule. Similarly, when something from what we mentioned at the beginning of the chapter falls. Commentary: The general rule is that whoever is the cause of the killing or destruction of another, the diyah of the deceased is obligatory on his 'aqilah. Therefore, if someone builds any of the mentioned things in the road and it falls on a person causing his death, the diyah is obligatory on the builder's 'aqilah. This clarifies the issue. Note: The interpretation of 'roshan' – the author of 'Ayn al-Hidayah' interprets it as a skylight, some as a balcony, and some as a lantern placed over the road to move from one house to another. Whatever the interpretation, the ruling is the same.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability when a structure (roshan/skylight or mizab/spout) constructed over a public road falls and kills a person. The matn from al-Hidayah states that the diyah (blood money) is due on the 'aqilah (agnatic heirs) of the builder. The reason given is that the builder is the cause (musabbib) of the death and is a transgressor (muta'addi) by occupying the public airspace, which is not his property to use. This transgression makes him liable for damages. The commentary explains the general principle (qa'idah kulliyyah): whoever causes the death of another, even indirectly, the diyah falls on his 'aqilah. Thus, in this case, since the builder placed an object that caused death, the 'aqilah must pay the diyah. A note clarifies that the term 'roshan' has different interpretations (skylight, balcony, or connecting lantern), but all share the same legal ruling.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('aqilah): The agnatic relatives of the perpetrator (usually male paternal relatives) who are liable to pay diyah in cases of unintended killing or injury caused by their kinsman.
مسبب (musabbib): A person who is an indirect cause of an event, as opposed to a direct actor (mubashir).
متعاد (muta'addi): Transgressor; one who commits an act without right, exceeding the bounds of permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi ruling, what is the reason that diyah is on the 'aqilah rather than on the builder individually?
A) The builder is a direct killer (mubashir) and thus his 'aqilah is liable.
B) The builder is a transgressive cause (musabbib muta'addi) of the death, and liability for indirect killing is on the 'aqilah.
C) The builder acted with intent to kill, so his 'aqilah must pay.
D) The state is always liable for accidents on public roads.

Key Takeaway
If a structure over a public road falls and kills a person, the diyah is wajib on the builder's 'aqilah because he is a transgressive cause.

Liability for Multiple Deaths from a Single Transgression: The Analogy of Pushing
Ruling with analogy on causal chain liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a transgressor is liable for all deaths in a causal chain arising from his transgression, using the qiyas jali approach.

Core Idea
A builder whose debris causes a chain of deaths is liable for all, just as a pusher is liable for both deaths.

This passage from al-Hidayah extends liability from direct causation to causation through a chain of events. It uses an analogy to clarify that the builder's initial transgression makes him responsible for all subsequent deaths, even if multiple occur in a sequence. Understanding this principle is crucial for determining diyah in complex accident scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transgression
Recognize that the builder placed the structure (e.g., spout) in a way that caused it to fall and create debris. This is the initial transgression (ta'addi).
Without transgression, there is no liability.
2
Trace the chain of events
The debris causes a person to trip. That person then falls on another, and both die. Identify each link in the causal chain.
The chain is uninterrupted: debris → trip → fall → death of both.
3
Apply the analogy to pushing
The builder's action is analogous to directly pushing the first person onto the second. In direct pushing, the pusher is liable for both deaths. By qiyas, the builder is also liable for both.
This is a clear analogy (qiyas jali).
4
State the ruling
The builder must pay diyah for both deaths. There is no reduction because the chain flows from his single act.
The ruling covers both human and animal deaths (as noted for beasts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا إذا تعثر بنقضه إنسان أو عطبت به دابة وإن عثر بذالک رجل فوقع علی آخر فماتا فالضمان على الذي أحدثه فيهما لأنه يصير كالدافع إياه عليه.
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جب کہ اس کی ٹوٹن سے کوئی انسان پھسل گیا یا اس کی وجہ سے کوئی چوپایہ ہلاک ہو گیا اور اگر اس سے کوئی آدمی پھسل گیا پس وہ دوسرے پر گر گیا پس وہ دونوں مر گئے تو ان دونوں کے اندر ضمان اس شخص پر ہو گا جس نے اس کو بنایا تھا اس لئے کہ بنانے والا ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اس کو دوسرے پر گرانے والا ۔ تشریح یعنی پرنالہ یا چھجہ وغیرہ جوگر گیا تھا اب جو اس کی ٹوٹن پڑی ہے اگر اس میں کوئی پھسل کر مر جائے تو مالک پر دیت واجب ہوگی اور اگر ایک پھسلا اور پھسل کر دوسرے پر گرا جس سے وہ دونوں مرگئے تو مالک پر دونوں کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو ایسا ہو گیا گویا کہ مالک نے ایک کو پکڑ کر دوسرے پر دھکا دید یا ہو تو ہاں دھکا دینے والے پر دونوں کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہوگا۔
And similarly, if a person trips over its debris, or an animal perishes because of it. And if a man trips over that, falls on another, and both die, then liability is on the one who made it for both, because he becomes like one who pushed him onto the other. Translation: And similarly, if a person slips on its debris, or an animal perishes due to it. And if a man slips on it, falls on another, and both die, then liability is on the one who built it for both, because the builder becomes like one who pushed him onto the other. Commentary: Meaning if a spout or cornice etc. had fallen and its debris remains, if someone slips on it and dies, the owner is liable for diyah. And if one slips and falls on another, and both die, then the owner is liable for both. Because this is as if the owner grabbed one and pushed him onto the other. Indeed, the pusher is liable for both. Similarly here.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage extends the ruling of liability for falling structures to cases where the debris itself causes harm. The matn from al-Hidayah states that if a person trips over debris (from a fallen structure) and dies, or an animal perishes, the builder is liable. Furthermore, if one person trips, falls on another, and both die, the builder is liable for both deaths. The analogy (qiyas jaliy) is made: the builder is like someone who pushed the first person onto the second, because the builder's action (placing the structure) set the chain of causation. Just as a direct pusher is liable for both deaths, so is the builder here. The commentary in Urdu explains: the debris from a fallen spout or cornice: if someone slips on it and dies, the owner pays diyah; if two die in the chain, the owner pays for both. The principle is that the builder's transgression (placing the structure unlawfully over the road) makes him responsible for all consequences flowing from it, even if multiple deaths occur in a causal chain.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Legal liability, here for payment of diyah due to causing death through transgressive action.
تعثر (ta'aththur): Tripping or stumbling over debris.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the victim's heirs for wrongful death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If debris from a fallen spout causes a person to trip and fall onto another, killing both, who is liable for the diyah?
A) The first victim's 'aqilah pays for the second.
B) No one, as it is a chain of accidents.
C) The builder is liable for both deaths.
D) The state is liable.

Key Takeaway
A single transgression that sets off an unbroken chain of deaths renders the transgressor liable for all those deaths, by analogy to direct pushing.

Liability for a Projecting Spout: Causation and Transgression in Diyah
Ruling on diyah when a projecting structure falls and kills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah when a projecting structure falls on a person and explain why the builder's 'āqilah is liable.

Core Idea
Indirect causation (sabab) plus transgression (ta‘addī) triggers diyah on the ‘āqilah.

This lesson examines a ruling from al-Quduri on liability for blood-money when a projecting structure falls and kills a person. The ruling establishes that the builder’s ‘āqilah (agnatic relatives) must pay diyah because the builder is both a cause (sabab) and a transgressor (muta‘addī) by occupying public airspace. Understanding this principle is essential for distinguishing between direct and indirect causation in Hanafi tort law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. Here, the act is building a projecting structure (like a window or spout) that falls and kills someone. The ruling: diyah is obligatory upon the builder's 'āqilah.
Note: The ruling applies to any projection into a public road.
2
Identify the legal basis: causation (sabab) and transgression (ta‘addī)
The passage explicitly states two reasons for liability: (1) the builder is a cause (sabab) of the death, and (2) he is a transgressor (muta‘addī) by occupying the airspace of the road. Distinguish between direct act (mubasharah) and indirect cause (sabab); here it is the latter.
Transgression (ta'addi) is key: building without permission in public space makes the act unlawful.
3
Understand the role of the ‘āqilah
The diyah is not paid by the builder personally, but by his 'āqilah (agnatic relatives). This is because the killing is considered a form of manslaughter by causation, not intentional murder. The 'āqilah collectively bears the blood-money as a social responsibility.
This is a unique feature of Hanafi fiqh; other schools may differ.
4
Recognize the generality of the principle
The author emphasizes that this is a general principle (qā'idah kulliyyah) applicable to any similar case. Anything built in the road that falls and kills triggers the same ruling. The specific type of structure (window, spout, lantern) does not change the ruling.
The tanbīh clarifies that different interpretations of 'roshan' do not affect the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإذا أشرع في الطريق روشنا أو ميزابا أو نحوه فسقط على إنسان فعطب فالدية على عاقلته لأنه مسبب لتلفه متعد بشغله هواء الطريق وهذا من أسباب الضمان وهو الأصل وكذالك إذا سقط شيء مما ذكرنا في أول الباب.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب کہ نکالا راستہ میں روشن یا پر نالہ یا اس کے مثل پس وہ کسی انسان پر گر گیا پس وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے تلف ہونے کا سبب متعدی ہے اس کے مشغول کرنے کی وجہ سے راستہ کی فضا کو اور یہ ضمان کے اسباب میں سے ہے اور یہی قاعدہ کلیہ ہے اور ایسے ہی جب ان چیزوں میں سے کوئی چیز گر گئی جن کو ہم اول باب میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ جو کسی کے قتل و ہلاک کا سبب ہوتا ہے تو اس کے عاقلہ پر اگر ہالک کی دیت واجب ہوتی ہے لہذا اگر کسی نے راستہ میں مذکورہ چیزوں میں سے کوئی چیز بنائی وہ کسی شخص کے اوپر گر جائے جس سے وہ مر جائے تو بنانے والے کے عاقلہ پر اس کی دیت واجب ہوگی اتنی بات سے مسئلہ صاف ہو گیا۔
تنبیه روشن کی تفسیر صاحب عین الہدایہ نے روشندان سے کی ہے اور بعض نے زمینہ سے اور بعض نے اس لینٹر سے جو راستہ پر ڈال دیا جائے تاکہ اس مکان سے دوسرے مکان میں جاسکے، بہر حال جو بھی تفسیر ہو حکم ایک ہی ہے۔
(Imam al-Quduri) said: And when one projects into the road a window or a water-spout or the like, and it falls upon a person and he dies, then the blood-money is upon his 'aqilah because he is a cause of his destruction, being a transgressor by occupying the airspace of the road, and this is among the causes of liability, and that is the principle. And similarly if something from what we mentioned in the beginning of the chapter falls. Commentary: The principle is that whoever is a cause of someone's death, the blood-money is upon his 'aqilah. So if someone builds any of these things in the road and it falls on a person and kills him, the builder's 'aqilah is liable for the blood-money. Clarification: The interpretation of 'roshan' - some say it is a window projecting outward, others say it is a lantern placed on the road to go from one house to another; in any case, the ruling is the same.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from al-Quduri regarding liability when a projecting structure falls on someone in a public road. The author begins by identifying the passage type as a rule of causation (sabab) with the authority of the matn. The ruling holds the builder liable because he is both a cause of the death and a transgressor by occupying the public airspace without permission. The reasoning is that occupying the airspace is a form of transgression (ta'addi), and therefore the builder's 'aqilah (the tribe or group responsible for paying blood-money) must pay the diyah. The author emphasizes that this is a general principle (qā'idah kulliyyah) extending to anything built in the road that causes death. A clarification (tanbīh) notes that the term 'roshan' may refer to a projecting window or a lantern, but the ruling is consistent regardless of the specific structure.

Key Terms
روشن (roshan): A structure projecting from a house into a public road, such as a window or lantern.
عاقلہ ('aqilah): The male agnatic relatives of the perpetrator who are collectively responsible for paying diyah.
سبب (sabab): A cause that indirectly leads to harm, as opposed to direct action (mubasharah).
متعدی (muta'addi): One who acts unlawfully by exceeding proper bounds, here by occupying public space.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the builder of a projecting spout liable for the blood-money when it falls and kills someone?
A) Because he directly pushed the person
B) Because he is a cause and a transgressor by occupying public airspace
C) Because he intended to kill
D) Because the spout was not properly constructed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, diyah is wajib upon the 'āqilah when death results from an indirect cause (sabab) combined with transgression (ta'addī) in public space.

Liability for Deaths Caused by Fallen Debris
Ruling on diyah via analogy to a pusher

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a builder is liable for all deaths resulting from his hazardous structure, using qiyas to the case of a pusher.

Core Idea
A builder is liable for deaths caused by debris, even via a chain, by analogy to direct pushing.

This passage from al-Hidayah expands liability for a fallen structure beyond direct impact. The builder is held responsible not only if a person is killed by the falling object, but also if someone trips on the debris and dies, or trips and falls onto another person, killing both. The reasoning uses a clear qiyas (analogy) to the case of a person who pushes another onto a third, establishing that the builder is like a pusher. Understanding this analogy helps us grasp how Hanafi fiqh treats indirect causation in torts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling
Recall the basic case: if a structure falls and directly kills someone, the builder is liable. This passage extends that liability.
2
Identify the new cases
The passage adds three scenarios: a person trips on debris and dies; an animal dies; and a person trips and falls onto another, killing both. Focus on the last as the most complex.
3
Understand the qiyas (analogy)
The asl (original case) is: a person pushes another onto a third, killing both. The pusher is liable for both deaths. This is well established (Ijma or qiyas on direct killing).
4
Extract the illa (effective cause)
The illa is that the pusher's action is the cause of both deaths. Similarly, the builder's action of creating a hazardous debris is the cause of the chain of deaths.
The illa is jaliyyah (evident) because causation is clear.
5
Apply the hukm to the far' (new case)
Since the builder's debris is the cause of the trip and subsequent fall, he is liable for both deaths, just as the pusher is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا إذا تعثر بنقضه إنسان أو عطبت به دابة وإن عثر بذالک رجل فوقع علی آخر فماتا فالضمان على الذي أحدثه فيهما لأنه يصير كالدافع إياه عليه.
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جب کہ اس کی ٹوٹن سے کوئی انسان پھسل گیا یا اس کی وجہ سے کوئی چوپایہ ہلاک ہو گیا اور اگر اس سے کوئی آدمی پھسل گیا پس وہ دوسرے پر گر گیا پس وہ دونوں مر گئے تو ان دونوں کے اندر ضمان اس شخص پر ہو گا جس نے اس کو بنایا تھا اس لئے کہ بنانے والا ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اس کو دوسرے پر گرانے والا ۔ تشریح یعنی پرنالہ یا چھجہ وغیرہ جوگر گیا تھا اب جو اس کی ٹوٹن پڑی ہے اگر اس میں کوئی پھسل کر مر جائے تو مالک پر دیت واجب ہوگی اور اگر ایک پھسلا اور پھسل کر دوسرے پر گرا جس سے وہ دونوں مرگئے تو مالک پر دونوں کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو ایسا ہو گیا گویا کہ مالک نے ایک کو پکڑ کر دوسرے پر دھکا دید یا ہو تو ہاں دھکا دینے والے پر دونوں کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہوگا۔
And similarly when a person trips on its broken piece, or an animal is killed by it. And if a person trips on that and falls on another and both die, then the liability for both is upon the one who made it, because he becomes like one who pushed the first onto the second. Commentary: If a water-spout or balcony falls, and someone slips on its broken piece and dies, the owner is liable for the blood-money. And if one slips and falls on another and both die, the owner is liable for both, because it is as if the owner grabbed the first and pushed him onto the second; just as the pusher is liable for both, so is the builder.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage expands the earlier ruling to cases where the debris of the fallen structure causes death indirectly. The passage type is a ruling with analogy: if someone trips on the broken piece and dies, the builder is liable because he is the cause of the debris being there. If an animal dies, the same applies. The most extensive case is when one person trips and falls onto another, killing both. The builder is liable for both deaths because his action is analogous to pushing the first person onto the second: in both cases, the death is caused by the builder's transgression. The commentary clarifies that the analogy is direct: just as a person who physically pushes another is liable for both deaths, so too is the builder who creates a dangerous condition leading to the same result.

Key Terms
نقض (nuqad): The broken piece or debris of a fallen structure.
دافع (dafi'): One who pushes, used as an analogy for the builder's liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the first victim's estate
B) The person who tripped
C) The builder of the spout
D) No one, as it was an accident

Key Takeaway
The builder is liable for all deaths caused by his hazardous debris, even through an intermediate chain, because he is the effective cause (sabab) analogous to a direct actor (dafi').

Liability Depends on Which Part of Spout Strikes
Fiqh ruling with condition on spout fall

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a spout falls and kills someone, and explain how transgression (ta'addi) determines liability between the part inside the wall and the projecting part.

Core Idea
Liability for a fallen spout hinges on transgression: inside the wall no fault, outside the wall liable.

When a building structure like a spout falls and causes death, not every instance leads to liability. The Hanafi school draws a critical distinction based on whether the fatal part was within the owner's property or projected into public space. This lesson examines that distinction and its underlying principle of transgression (ta'addi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage considers two cases: the spout's part that was inside the wall strikes, versus the part outside the wall strikes. Recognize that the ruling differs for each.
2
Apply the principle of ta'addi
Liability hinges on transgression. The owner is not a transgressor for the part inside his own wall but is a transgressor for the part projecting into public space without necessity.
Transgression (ta'addi) means exceeding one's lawful right.
3
Determine liability for each part
For the part inside the wall: no liability (no diyah). For the projecting part: liability is wajib (diyah must be paid).
4
Note the absence of kaffarah and hirman
In neither case is expiation (kaffarah) required, nor is the killer barred from inheritance (hirman 'an al-mirath) because the killing is not direct or intentional.
The bar from inheritance only applies when qisas or kaffarah is obligated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن سقط الميزاب نظر فإن أصاب ما كان منه فى الحائط رجلا فقتله فلاضمان عليه لأنه غير متعد فيه لما أنه وضعه في ملكه، وإن أصابه ما كان خارجا من الحائط فالضمان على الذى وضعه لكونه متعديا فيه ولا ضرورة لأنه يمكنه أن يركبه فى الحائط ولا كفارة عليه ولا يحرم عن الميراث لأنه ليس بقاتل حقيقة ترجمہ اور اگر پر نالہ گر جائے تو دیکھا جائے پس اگر وہ حصہ لگا ہے جو کہ پر نالہ کا دیوار میں ہے کسی شخص کو پس اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر ضمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں مستعدی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے اس کو اپنی ملک میں رکھا ہے اور اگر وہ حصہ لگا ہے جو دیوار سے باہر ہے تو رکھنے والے پر ضمان ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں متعدی ہے اور کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کو دیوار میں لگا نا ممکن تھا اور اس پر کفارہ نہیں ہے اور نہ یہ میراث سے محروم ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ حقیقۂ قاتل نہیں ہے۔
تشریح اگر پر نالہ گر گیا اور اس سے کوئی ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس کا جو حصہ دیوار میں فیٹ تھا اگر وہ لگا ہو تو مالک پر ضمان نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اپنی دیوار میں لگانے کا اس کو اختیار تھا تو تعدی نہیں پائی گئی اور اگر وہ حصہ لگا ہو جو دیوار سے باہر ہے تو ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ اس کی تعدی ہے اور اس کی ضرورت اس کو تھی بھی نہیں کیونکہ یہ صرف اپنی دیوار میں لگا تا باہر نہ نکالتا یا کسی بناتا۔ بہر حال قتل میں کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا اور نہ یہ قاتل میراث سے محروم ہوتاہے کیونکہ حرمان کا باعث وہ قتل ہے جو بطریق مانعتہ المخلو قصاص یا کفارہ واجب کرے اور یہاں کوئی بھی واجب نہیں ہے (وبیناہ فی درس السراجی)۔
And if the spout falls, then it is considered: If the part that was in the wall strikes a person and kills him, there is no liability because he is not a transgressor in that, since he placed it in his own property. And if the part that was outside the wall strikes him, then liability is upon the one who placed it because he is a transgressor in that, and there is no necessity because he could have fixed it in the wall. And there is no expiation upon him, nor is he barred from inheritance because he is not a true killer. Commentary: If the spout falls and kills, the part that was within the wall: if it strikes, the owner is not liable because he had the right to place it in his own wall, so no transgression. If the part outside the wall strikes, liability is wajib because of transgression, and there was no necessity to project it. In either case, expiation is not wajib, and the killer is not barred from inheritance because the bar comes from a killing that requires retaliation or expiation; here neither is required.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage refines the ruling by distinguishing between the part of the spout that was embedded in the wall and the part that projected outward. The passage type is a ruling with a condition: the liability hinges on whether the fatal part was within the builder's property (the wall) or in public space. Since the builder owns the wall, he is not a transgressor for the part inside it; therefore no liability. However, for the projecting part, he is a transgressor because he occupied public airspace without necessity (he could have kept it within the wall). Thus he is liable. The passage further clarifies that in neither case is kaffarah required, nor is the killer barred from inheritance, because the killing is not intentional or direct. The commentary explains that the bar from inheritance (hirman) only applies to a killing that obligates qisas or kaffarah, and here neither is obligatory.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for accidental killing, which is not wajib here because the killing is not direct.
حرمان عن الميراث (hirman 'an al-mirath): Bar from inheritance, which applies only to a killer who is liable for qisas or kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a spout falls and the part that was inside the wall kills someone, what is the ruling?
A) Full diyah is wajib
B) Half diyah is wajib
C) No liability
D) The builder is barred from inheritance

Key Takeaway
Liability for damage from a fallen structure depends on whether the builder had the right to place that part in that location; transgression is the decisive factor.

Diyah When Both Parts of a Spout Strike
Ruling on diyah when both spout parts strike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on diyah when a person is killed by two combined causes, and explain the reasoning (illa) using the principle of i'tibar al-ahwal.

Core Idea
When a liable and non-liable cause combine, liability is halved to account for both possibilities.

This lesson examines a specific case in Hanafi diyah law: when a spout falls and both its inside (non-liable) and projecting (liable) parts strike a person, causing death. The passage rules that half diyah is wajib in both known and unknown scenarios, using an analogy with a wound from a wild beast and a human. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the legal principle of considering all possible states (i'tibar al-ahwal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
The case: a person is struck and killed by both parts of a spout (inside and projecting). If it is known that both struck, half diyah is wajib and half is waived. If unknown which part struck, half diyah is still wajib.
The ruling applies regardless of knowledge of which part struck.
2
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The text analogizes to a case where a wild beast and a human wound a person: the human is liable for half diyah. This establishes that when a liable and non-liable cause combine, the liable party pays half.
The wild beast represents the non-liable (inside part), the human the liable (projecting part).
3
Analyze the reasoning (talil)
The principle 'i'tibar al-ahwal' (considering all states) justifies the half: if only the projecting part struck, full diyah; if only the inside part, no diyah. The middle ground (half) accounts for both possibilities.
This is a form of compromise (tawassut) between full liability and no liability.
4
Note the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi school holds that half diyah is wajib in both known and unknown cases. Some schools may hold full liability in the unknown case, but Hanafi relies on i'tibar al-ahwal.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أصابه الطرفان جميعا وعلم ذالك وجب النصف وهدر النصف كما إذا جرحه سبع وإنسان ولو لم يعلم أى طرف أصابه يضمن النصف اعتبارا للأحوال.
ترجمہ اور اگر اس کو دونوں کنارے لگے ہوں اور یہ بات معلوم ہو چکی ہو تو نصف واجب ہوگا اور نصف رائیگاں ہو گا جیسے جب کہ اس کو کسی درندہ اور انسان نے زخمی کیا ہو۔ اور اگر یہ معلوم نہ ہو سکے کہ کونسا کفارہ اس کو لگا ہے۔ تو وہ نصف کا ضامن ہوگا جملہ احوال کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے ۔
تشریح ۔ اور اگر دونوں کنارے لگے ہوں اور یہ معلوم بھی ہو کہ دونوں کنارے لگے ہیں تو اس صورت میں نصف دیت واجب ہوگی اور نصف کو ہدر قرار دیا جائے گا ، جیسے اگر کسی شخص کو شیر نے اور انسان نے زخمی کیا ہو جس سے وہ مر جائے تو انسان پر نصف دیت واجب ہو گی ۔ اور اگر یہ معلوم نہ ہو سکے کہ کون سا کنارہ لگا ہے تو کبھی نصف کا ضامن ہو گا۔ کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ اس میں دونوں حالتوں کی رعایت ہے یعنی ایک جانب سے لگنے کی صورت میں پورا ضمان واجب ہے اور ایک طرف سے کچھ بھی واجب نہیں تو ہم نے درمیان میں کر دیا کہ نصف واجب ہے تو دونوں کی رعایت ہوگئی۔
And if both edges strike him and that is known, then half is obligatory and half is waived, as when a wild beast and a human wound him. And if it is not known which edge struck him, he is liable for half, considering all states. Commentary: If both edges strike and it is known that both struck, half diyah is wajib and half is waived, like the case where a lion and a human wound a person and he dies: the human is liable for half diyah. And if it is not known which edge struck, then he is liable for half because consideration is given to both states: if one edge struck, full liability; if the other, none; so we take the middle: half is wajib, thus both states are taken into account.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage addresses the case when both the part inside the wall and the projecting part strike the victim. The passage type is a ruling with a conditional: if it is known that both parts struck, then half diyah is obligatory (for the projecting part) and half is waived (for the part inside the wall). The analogy given is with a wound from both a wild animal and a human: the human is liable for half. If it is unknown which part struck, then the builder is still liable for half because we consider both possibilities: full liability if the projecting part struck, no liability if the inside part struck; the middle ground is half. The commentary explains that this is a compromise to account for both possible states.

Key Terms
هدر (hadar): Waived or nullified; here, half the diyah is not payable.
اعتبارا للأحوال (i'tibaran li'l-ahwal): Considering all possible states or circumstances to arrive at a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Half diyah
C) No diyah
D) Quarter diyah

Key Takeaway
When a liable and non-liable cause combine, Hanafi law imposes half diyah, using the principle of considering all states (i'tibar al-ahwal) as a compromise between full and no liability.

Liability for a Water Spout: Inside vs Outside the Wall
Ruling on liability for a falling water spout distinguishing inside vs outside.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a water spout falls and kills, and identify the element of transgression (ta'di) that determines liability.

Core Idea
No liability for harm caused by the part of a spout inside your wall; liability arises only for the projecting part due to transgression.

When a water spout falls and kills someone, is the owner liable? The Hanafi school draws a precise line: liability depends on whether the fatal part was inside or outside the owner's wall. This ruling turns on the concept of ta'di (transgression). The passage from al-Hidayah explains the reasoning and its consequences for expiation and inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? The owner places a water spout that falls and kills. The ruling: if the part inside the wall kills, no liability (daman); if the part outside kills, liability is wajib.
The ruling is not about the spout itself but about the location of the fatal part.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the reasoning: absence or presence of transgression (ta'di). The owner is not transgressing when placing something on his own property; he is transgressing when extending it into public space without necessity.
Ta'di is the key legal cause (illa) for liability.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does ta'di lead to liability? Placing the spout outside is a transgression because it invades public right-of-way. There was no necessity (darurah) because the owner could have kept it within the wall. Therefore, he is responsible for the harm.
The absence of necessity is also part of the proof.
4
Note the subsidiary rulings
The passage adds: no expiation (kaffarah) is due, and the owner is not deprived of inheritance. This is because the killing is not considered direct murder (qatl haqiqi) that would trigger those consequences.
These follow from the fact that liability is not criminal but civil.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (like al-Shafi'i) may hold the owner liable regardless of location if the spout was defective or negligent. The Hanafi position relies on the distinction of ta'di.
This ikhtilaf is noted in the later tradition (mukhtalaf fih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن سقط الميزاب نظر فإن أصاب ما كان منه فى الحائط رجلا فقتله فلاضمان عليه لأنه غير متعد فيه لما أنه وضعه في ملكه، وإن أصابه ما كان خارجا من الحائط فالضمان على الذى وضعه لكونه متعديا فيه ولا ضرورة لأنه يمكنه أن يركبه فى الحائط ولا كفارة عليه ولا يحرم عن الميراث لأنه ليس بقاتل حقيقة ترجمہ اور اگر پر نالہ گر جائے تو دیکھا جائے پس اگر وہ حصہ لگا ہے جو کہ پر نالہ کا دیوار میں ہے کسی شخص کو پس اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر ضمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں متعدی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے اس کو اپنی ملک میں رکھا ہے اور اگر وہ حصہ لگا ہے جو دیوار سے باہر ہے تو رکھنے والے پر ضمان ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں متعدی ہے اور کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کو دیوار میں لگا نا ممکن تھا اور اس پر کفارہ نہیں ہے اور نہ یہ میراث سے محروم ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ حقیقۂ قاتل نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اگر پر نالہ گر گیا اور اس سے کوئی ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس کا جو حصہ دیوار میں فٹ تھا اگر وہ لگا ہو تو مالک پر ضمان نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اپنی دیوار میں لگانے کا اس کو اختیار تھا تو تعدی نہیں پائی گئی اور اگر وہ حصہ لگا ہو جو دیوار سے باہر ہے تو ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ اس کی تعدی ہے اور اس کی ضرورت اس کو تھی بھی نہیں کیونکہ یہ صرف اپنی دیوار میں لگا تا باہر نہ نکالتا یا کسی بناتا۔ بہر حال قتل میں کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا اور نہ یہ قاتل میراث سے محروم ہوتا ہے کیونکہ حرمان کا باعث وہ قتل ہے جو بطریق مانعتہ المخلو قصاص یا کفارہ واجب کرے اور یہاں کوئی بھی واجب نہیں ہے (وبیناہ فی درس السراجی)۔
And if a water spout falls, it is considered: if it hits a person with the part that was in the wall and kills him, there is no liability, because he is not transgressing since he placed it in his property. And if it hits him with the part outside the wall, the liability is on the one who placed it, because he is transgressing and there is no necessity since he could have mounted it within the wall. And there is no expiation on him, and he is not deprived of inheritance because he is not a killer in reality. Translation: And if a water spout falls, it is considered: if the part that was inside the wall hits someone and kills him, there is no liability because he is not transgressing, because he placed it in his own property. And if the part outside the wall hits him, the liability is on the one who placed it because he is transgressing and there is no necessity since he could have fixed it inside the wall. And there is no expiation on him, and he is not deprived of inheritance because he is not a killer in reality. Explanation: If a water spout falls and someone dies from it, if the part that was fixed in the wall hits him, the owner is not liable because he had the right to fix it in his own wall, so no transgression occurred. And if the part outside the wall hits him, liability is wajib because of his transgression, and he had no necessity for it, because he could have fixed it within his wall without extending it outward or made something else. In any case, expiation is not wajib for the killing, and the killer is not deprived of inheritance because the cause of deprivation is a killing that necessitates retaliation or expiation, and here nothing is wajib (and it is explained in Dars al-Siraji).
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on liability when a water spout (mizab) falls and kills someone. The ruling distinguishes between the part of the spout embedded in the wall and the part projecting outside. If the part inside the wall causes death, there is no liability (dhaman) because the owner placed it on his own property and was not transgressing (mut'addi). If the projecting part causes death, the owner is liable because he transgressed by placing it over the public path, and there was no genuine necessity to do so; he could have confined it to his wall. Additionally, no expiation (kaffarah) is wajib, and the owner is not barred from inheritance because the killing is not considered direct (qatl haqiqi) that would require retaliation or expiation. The Urdu commentary paraphrases and explains the reasoning, emphasizing the lack of necessity and the owner's authority over his wall.

Key Terms
ميزاب (mizab): A water spout or drain projecting from a wall to carry rainwater off the roof.
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay compensation (blood money or damages) for harm caused.
تعدي (ta'di): Transgression or exceeding proper limits, here placing an object where it causes harm to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Whether the killing was intentional or accidental
C) Whether the spout hit the victim with its part inside the wall or outside the wall
D) Whether the owner had a permit from the authorities

Key Takeaway
Liability for a falling water spout hinges on transgression: no daman for the part inside the wall, wajib for the part outside.

Both Ends of Water Spout Hit: Known and Unknown
Ruling on liability when both parts of spout hit or when uncertain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diya when both ends of a water spout hit a victim, distinguish between known and unknown cases, and apply the qiyas analogy to similar joint liability scenarios.

Core Idea
When both parts of a spout strike, half diya is payable; uncertainty also yields half, balancing full liability and no liability.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario from diyat (blood money): a water spout projecting from a wall, where both the inside (within property) and outside (over public path) ends strike a person. The ruling uses qiyas with a case where a wild animal and a human jointly cause death. Understanding this ruling helps clarify how Hanafi fiqh apportions liability when a liable and a non-liable cause combine, and how uncertainty is resolved by giving weight to both possibilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage to identify the two cases discussed: (1) both ends hit and it is known, (2) it is unknown which end hit. Note the ruling for each.
The known case uses the beast-and-human analogy; the unknown case uses a balancing principle.
2
Analyze the known case qiyas
The known case is analogized to a joint wound by a beast and a human. Identify the asl (original case), far (new case), and illa (effective cause). The illa is that death results from combined acts of a liable party (human/outside part) and a non-liable cause (beast/inside part).
The inside part is akin to the beast because it is within the owner's property and thus not liable.
3
Understand the unknown case reasoning
When it is unknown which end hit, the text states: 'consideration is given to both situations.' There are two possibilities: full diya if only the outside part hit, no diya if only the inside part hit. The middle course is half diya, giving weight to both possibilities.
This is a principle of caution and fairness, not pure qiyas.
4
Extract the ruling and its limitation
The ruling: half diya is wajib in both cases. Note that this applies only when the spout is installed such that the outside part extends into a public area where liability attaches. The inside part is treated as non-liable.
The scope is limited to diyat cases involving combined liable and non-liable causes.
5
Apply to analogous modern scenarios
Think of modern building features like awnings, window boxes, or signage that project into public space. If both the part on private property and the part over public space cause injury, the same ruling applies. Also consider cases of joint tortfeasors with one non-liable party.
The core principle is apportionment when liability is mixed with non-liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أصابه الطرفان جميعا وعلم ذالك وجب النصف وهدر النصف كما إذا جرحه سبع وإنسان ولو لم يعلم أى طرف أصابه يضمن النصف اعتبارا للأحوال. ترجمہ اور اگر اس کو دونوں کنارے لگے ہوں اور یہ بات معلوم ہو چکی ہو تو نصف واجب ہوگا اور نصف رائیگاں ہو گا جیسے جب کہ اس کو کسی درندہ اور انسان نے زخمی کیا ہو۔ اور اگر یہ معلوم نہ ہو سکے کہ کونسا کفارہ اس کو لگا ہے۔ تو وہ نصف کا ضامن ہوگا جملہ احوال کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے ۔ تشریح ۔ اور اگر دونوں کنارے لگے ہوں اور یہ معلوم بھی ہو کہ دونوں کنارے لگے ہیں تو اس صورت میں نصف دیت واجب ہوگی اور نصف کو ہدر قرار دیا جائے گا ، جیسے اگر کسی شخص کو شیر نے اور انسان نے زخمی کیا ہو جس سے وہ مر جائے تو انسان پر نصف دیت واجب ہو گی ۔ اور اگر یہ معلوم نہ ہو سکے کہ کون سا کنارہ لگا ہے تو کبھی نصف کا ضامن ہو گا۔ کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ اس میں دونوں حالتوں کی رعایت ہے یعنی ایک جانب سے لگنے کی صورت میں پورا ضمان واجب ہے اور ایک طرف سے کچھ بھی واجب نہیں تو ہم نے درمیان میں کر دیا کہ نصف واجب ہے تو دونوں کی رعایت ہوگئی۔
And if both ends hit him together and that is known, half is wajib and half is waived, just as if a beast and a human wounded him. And if it is not known which end hit him, he guarantees half, considering the circumstances. Translation: And if both ends hit him and this is known, then half is wajib and half is waived, as when a wild animal and a human wound him. And if it is not known which end hit him, then he is liable for half, taking all situations into account. Explanation: And if both ends hit him and it is known that both ends hit, then half of the diya is wajib and the other half is disregarded, just as if a lion and a human wounded him and he died, then the human is liable for half the diya. And if it is not known which end hit him, then he is liable for half. Why? Because consideration is given to both situations: if one end hits, full liability is wajib; if the other end hits, nothing is wajib. So we adopt a middle course: half is wajib, thus both situations are considered.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where both the inside and outside parts of a water spout hit a victim, and also the case of uncertainty. If it is certain that both ends struck, the diya (blood money) is halved: half is payable (for the part outside the wall) and half is waived (for the part inside). This is analogous to a case where a wild animal and a human both wound a person, and the death results; the human pays half diya because the animal's act is uncompensated. If it is unknown which part hit (i.e., whether it was the inside or outside end), the owner pays half diya. The reasoning: because there are two possibilities: full liability if only the outside part hit, and no liability if only the inside part hit. The rule applies half to balance both possibilities. This is based on the principle of caution and fairness, giving weight to each possible situation.

Key Terms
ھدر (hadar): Waived, disregarded; the portion of diya not payable because the act was not attributable to a liable person.
دیت (diya): Blood money, compensation paid to the heirs of a victim in cases of homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full diya
B) Half diya
C) No diya
D) Quarter diya

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diyat, when a liable and a non-liable cause combine, half diya is imposed; uncertainty is resolved by halving to balance both possibilities.

Liability for a Projecting Eave or Beam Sold Before Harm
Ruling on liability when a projecting eave or beam is sold and later causes death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a harmful projection is sold after placement and identify the causal principle that keeps liability on the original actor.

Core Idea
The harmful act of placing an obstruction remains the cause of liability even after ownership transfers.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario where a person creates a hazard (a projecting eave or a beam) on public property, then sells the property or the object. If the hazard later causes death, who bears the blood money? The Hanafi ruling hinges on the principle that the original harmful act is the effective cause (sabab) and is not nullified by the sale. Understanding this principle clarifies many cases of transferred liability in tort.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage describes two cases: (1) a projecting eave built and then the house sold, (2) a beam placed and then sold with a stipulation freeing the seller from liability. In both, the object later kills someone.
Both scenarios involve an original act of placing a harmful object.
2
State the ruling and the liable party
In both cases, the ruling is that liability (diya) is on the seller (the person who originally placed the object), not the buyer.
Even if the seller stipulated freedom from liability, it does not help.
3
Extract the causal reasoning (ta'lil)
The reason given is 'finnahu wa huwa al-wad'u lam yanfakh bi-zawal milkihi' – the act of placing is not annulled by the removal of his ownership. The act itself is the cause of liability, and it remains attributable to the actor.
This is a principle of causation: the effect (the placement) does not retroactively become void when ownership changes.
4
Apply to a new case
Consider if a person digs a pit on his land, then sells the land. If someone falls into the pit, the seller is liable because the digging was his act. The buyer's ownership does not erase the initial harmful act.
This illustrates the same principle applied to a different hazard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أشرع جناحا إلى الطريق ثم باع الدار فأصاب الجناح رجلا فقتله أو وضع خشبة في الطريق ثم باع الخشبة وبرىء إليه منها فتركها المشترى حتى عطب بها إنسان فالضمان على البائع لأن فعله وهو الوضع لم ينفسخ بزوال ملكه وهو الموجب. ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے راستہ میں روشندان نکالا پھر گھر کو بیچ دیا پس وہ روشندان کسی شخص کو لگا پس اس کو مار دیا یا اس نے راستہ میں لکڑی رکھی پھر لکڑی کو فروخت کر دیا اور مشتری سے لکڑی سے بری ہونے کی شرط لگالی پس مشتری نے لکڑی کو چھوڑ دیا یہاں تک کہ اس کی وجہ سے کوئی انسان ہلاک ہو گیا تو ضمان بائع پر ہو گا اس لئے کہ بائع کا فعل (رکھنا) اس کی ملک کے زوال سے فسخ نہیں ہوا اور موجب ضمان وہی ہے (یعنی بائع کا فعل )۔ تشریح اگر زید نے مکان کے باہر راستہ میں چھجہ بنایا، زید نے راستہ میں لکڑی ڈال دی پھر زید نے یہ مکان یا یہ لکڑیاں خالد کو فروخت کر دیں اور زید نے خالد سے یہ بھی شرط کر لی تھی کہ میں ہر اس ضمان سے بری ہوں جو لکڑی سے یا چھجہ وغیرہ سے وجود میں آئے پھر لکڑی کی وجہ سے یا روشندان اور چھجہ کی وجہ سے کوئی آدمی مر گیا تو ضمان زید پر ہی واجب ہوگا خالد پر نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اصل موجب ضمان وہ زید کا فعل ہے کہ اس نے ایسی حرکت کیوں کی اور اب اگر چہ اس کی ملکیت نہیں ہے لیکن عدم ملک سے فعل کا زوال ثابت نہ ہو گا۔
And if he fixed a projecting eave into the road, then sold the house, and the eave hit a person and killed him; or if he placed a beam in the road, then sold the beam and was freed from liability for it, and the buyer left it until a person was harmed by it, then the liability is on the seller because his action, i.e., the placing, was not annulled by the removal of his ownership, and it is what causes liability. Translation: And if he extended a window projection into the road, then sold the house, and the projection hit a person and killed him; or if he placed a beam in the road, then sold the beam and stipulated with the buyer that he is free from liability, and the buyer left the beam until a person died from it, then liability is on the seller because the seller's act (placing) is not annulled by the removal of his ownership, and the cause of liability is that act. Explanation: If Zayd built a canopy (chajja) projecting into the road, or placed a beam in the road, then sold the house or the beam to Khalid, and Zayd also stipulated with Khalid that he is free from any liability arising from the beam or canopy, and then a person dies due to the beam or canopy, liability is wajib on Zayd, not Khalid. Because the actual cause of liability is Zayd's act of placing the harmful object. Even though ownership has transferred, the act is not nullified by loss of ownership.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a person creates a harmful obstruction (e.g., a projecting eave or a beam) on public property, then sells the property or the object itself, and later the obstruction causes death. The ruling is that the original seller (the one who placed it) remains liable for the blood money (diya), not the buyer. This is because the act that caused the liability—the placement—was done by the seller, and that act does not become void simply because ownership changed hands. Even if the seller stipulated that he is free from liability, his original wrongful act remains the effective cause (sabab). The buyer's mere inaction (leaving it as is) does not transfer the liability because the buyer did not perform the initial harmful act. The commentary clarifies through an example: Zayd builds a canopy over the road or places wood, sells to Khalid with a condition of disclaiming liability, but if someone dies, Zayd is still liable because his action is the root cause.

Key Terms
جناح (janah): A projecting part of a building, such as an eave or a room extending over the street.
بریء (bari'): Free from liability; a stipulation that the seller is not responsible for future harm from the sold object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The buyer, because he now owns the property
B) The seller, because the harmful act of building was his
C) Neither, because it was an accident
D) The state, because the canopy was in public space

Key Takeaway
The original harmful act remains the basis for liability even after the property is sold, and a stipulation disclaiming liability does not change this.
