Liability for Object Placed in Road After Property Sold
Ruling on damages from balcony or wood placed in road after sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that liability for harm caused by an object placed in a public road remains on the seller even after selling the property, and explain the legal reasoning based on the act of placement.

Core Idea
The act of placing a harmful object in the road creates liability that is not annulled by selling the property.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the Book of Diyat on liability when an object placed in a public road causes death after the property is sold. The text presents two scenarios: a balcony and a piece of wood. The key question is whether the seller or buyer bears responsibility. The Hanafi position, supported by rational reasoning, is that the seller remains liable because his act of placement is the direct cause, and ownership transfer does not dissolve that act. This principle reinforces that liability is based on one's own actions, not on current ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Note the two cases: a balcony (جناح) extended into the road and a piece of wood (خشبة) placed in the road. In both, the item is sold after placement.
The ruling applies to any object placed in a public road that later causes harm.
2
Determine the ruling
The ruling (ضمان) is on the seller, not the buyer. Even if the seller stipulates immunity (البراءة), liability remains on him.
Stipulating immunity does not negate liability because the cause is the seller's own act.
3
Understand the legal proof
The proof is rational: the act of placement (الوضع) is the cause (موجب) of harm. This act is not annulled by the removal of ownership (زوال ملكه).
The cause of liability is the act, not ownership.
4
Apply the principle
Consider a modern parallel: a homeowner installs a balcony overhanging a public path, sells the house, and the balcony collapses. The original owner is liable because his installation is the direct cause.
The same principle applies to any object placed by the seller that remains after sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أشرع جناحا إلى الطريق ثم باع الدار فأصاب الجناح رجلا فقتله أو وضع خشبة في الطريق ثم باع الخشبة وبرىء إليه منها فتركها المشترى حتى عطب بها إنسان فالضمان على البائع لأن فعله وهو الوضع لم ينفسخ بزوال ملكه وهو الموجب.
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے راستہ میں روشندان نکالا پھر گھر کو بیچ دیا پس وہ روشندان کسی شخص کو لگا پس اس کو مار دیا یا اس نے راستہ میں لکڑی رکھی پھر لکڑی کو فروخت کر دیا اور مشتری سے لکڑی سے بری کی شرط لگالی پس مشتری نے لکڑی کو چھوڑ دیا یہاں تک کہ اس کی وجہ سے کوئی انسان ہلاک ہو گیا تو ضمان بائع پر ہو گا اس لئے کہ بائع کا فعل (رکھنا) اس کی ملک کے زوال سے فسخ نہیں ہوا اور موجب ضمان وہی ہے (یعنی بائع کا فعل)۔
تشریح: اگر زید نے مکان کے باہر راستہ میں چھجہ بنایا، زید نے راستہ میں لکڑی ڈال دی پھر زید نے یہ مکان یا یہ لکڑیاں خالد کو فروخت کر دیں اور زید نے خالد سے یہ بھی شرط کر لی تھی کہ میں ہر اس ضمان سے بری ہوں جو لکڑی سے یا چھجہ وغیرہ سے وجود میں آئے پھر لکڑی کی وجہ سے یا روشندان اور چھجہ کی وجہ سے کوئی آدمی مر گیا تو ضمان زید پر ہی واجب ہوگا خالد پر نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اصل موجب ضمان وہ زید کا فعل ہے کہ اس نے ایسی حرکت کیوں کی اور اب اگر چہ اس کی ملکیت نہیں ہے لیکن عدم ملک سے فعل کا زوال ثابت نہ ہو گا۔
And if he extended a balcony into the road then sold the house, and the balcony struck a man and killed him, or he placed a piece of wood in the road then sold the wood and stipulated immunity from it, and the buyer left it until a person was harmed by it, then the liability is upon the seller because his act (the placement) is not annulled by the removal of his ownership, and it is that which necessitates liability. Translation: If he took out a balcony in the road then sold the house, and the balcony hit someone and killed him, or he placed a piece of wood in the road then sold the wood and stipulated immunity from the buyer, and the buyer left the wood until a person died due to it, then liability is upon the seller, because the seller's act (the placement) is not annulled by the loss of his ownership, and the cause of liability is that (the act of the seller). Explanation: If Zayd built a canopy outside the house in the road, or placed wood in the road, then sold the house or wood to Khalid, and stipulated immunity from any liability arising from the wood or canopy, then a person dies due to the wood or canopy, the liability is upon Zayd, not Khalid, because the cause of liability is Zayd's act of placing it, and even though he no longer owns it, loss of ownership does not annul the act.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Book of Diyat regarding liability when an object placed in the public road causes death after the property (house or object) has been sold. The text presents two cases: (1) a balcony (جناح) extended into the road, and (2) a piece of wood placed in the road. In both, the property is sold, but the harmful object remains. The ruling places liability (ضمان) on the seller (بائع), not the buyer (مشتری). The reason is that the act of placing the object (الوضع) is the direct cause of harm, and this act is not annulled by the transfer of ownership. Even if the seller stipulates immunity (البراءة) from liability, that condition does not remove the obligation because it is the seller's own act that created the harm. The commentary in Urdu uses the example of Zayd and Khalid to illustrate: Zayd's act of placing the canopy or wood is the cause of loss, and ownership transfer does not nullify his responsibility. Therefore, the seller must pay diyat (blood money) for the death.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Financial liability or responsibility to compensate for harm caused.
موجب (mujib): The cause or legal basis that necessitates liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the two cases presented (balcony extended into road then sold, wood placed in road then sold), who bears liability if the object causes death?
A) The buyer, because he now owns the property.
B) The seller, because his act of placement is not annulled by the sale.
C) Both the seller and buyer jointly.
D) Neither, if the seller stipulated immunity.

Key Takeaway
Liability for harm caused by an object placed in a public road remains on the person who placed it, even after selling the property, because the act of placement is the legal cause that is not annulled by a change in ownership.

Liability for Placing a Burning Coal in the Road
Ruling on liability for fire placed in road, including wind scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for a hazard placed in a public road and apply the exception for foreseeable wind.

Core Idea
A transgressor is liable for direct harm; intervening nature may break causation unless foreseeability reconnects it.

This passage from the Book of Diyat examines a classic tort scenario: someone places a burning coal in a public road, and it causes damage. The ruling distinguishes between direct and indirect causation, with a crucial exception when the actor knew or should have known of a strong wind. Understanding this distinction is key to Hanafi causation theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing a burning coal in the road. The initial ruling: if it burns something directly where placed, the person is liable (daman). Note the basis: being a transgressor (muta'addī) by placing a hazard in the public way.
Transgression (ta'addī) is the foundation of liability in Hanafi torts.
2
Analyze the effect of wind as an intervening cause
If the wind moves the coal to another place before it burns, the general rule is no liability — the wind 'annuls' the act. The actor's causal contribution is severed.
This illustrates the principle of intervening cause (al-sabab al-munqati').
3
Apply the exception: foreseeable wind
The text adds a qualification (qīla): if it was a windy day (or season, e.g., wheat harvest), the person remains liable. Reason: he knew the likely consequence, so his act is treated as if he directly caused the harm.
Foreseeability reconnects the causal chain.
4
Derive the underlying principle
The principle: a transgressor is liable for all foreseeable consequences of his wrongful act, even if an external force (wind) intervenes. This is a case of 'tasabbub' (indirect causation) akin to 'mubāsharah' when knowledge exists.
The Hanafi view balances strict liability with natural causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وضع في الطريق جمرا فأحرق شيئا يضمنه لأنه متعد فيه ولو حركته الريح إلى موضع آخر ثم احرق شيئا لم يضمنه لفسخ الريح فعله وقيل إذا كان اليوم ريحا يضمنه لأنه فعله مع علمه بعاقبته وقد أفضى إليها فجعل كمباشرته.
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے راستہ میں انگارا رکھا پس انگارے نے کسی چیز کو جلا دیا تو وہ ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں متعدی ہے اور اگر انگارے کو ہوا نے حرکت دی دوسری جگہ کی جانب پھر انگارے نے کسی چیز کو جلا دیا تو وہ ضامن نہ ہوگا ہوا کے فسخ کر دینے کی وجہ سے اس کے فعل کو اور کہا گیا ہے کہ جب وہ دن سخت ہوا والا ہو تو وہ اس کا ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس نے یہ کام کیا ہے اس کے انجام کو جاننے کے باوجود اور اس کا فعل اس انجام کی جانب پہنچ چکا ہے تو افضاء کو اس کی مباشرت کے مثل شمار کیا جائے گا۔
تشریح: اگر زید نے راستہ میں آگ رکھ دی اور اس سے کوئی جل کر مر گیا تو زید ضامن ہوگا کیونکہ یہ اس کی زیادتی ہے کہ اس نے راستہ میں آگ رکھی ہے اور اگر ہوا کی وجہ سے وہ انگارہ وہاں سے اڑ کر دوسری جگہ پہنچ گیا اور اس سے کوئی جل کر مر گیا تو اب زید ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اب یہ زید کا فعل نہیں رہا بلکہ ہوا کا فعل ہو گیا بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اگر ان دنوں میں جب کہ ہوا سخت چلتی ہے جیسے گیہوں کاٹنے کے زمانہ میں کسی نے آگ راستہ میں رکھ دی اور وہ ہوا کی وجہ سے کہیں اڑ جائے اور کسی چیز کو جلا دے تو اب آگ رکھنے والا ضامن ہو گا۔
And if he placed a coal in the road and it burned something, he is liable because he is a transgressor in that. And if the wind moved it to another place and then it burned something, he is not liable because the wind annulled his act. And it is said: if the day is windy, he is liable because he did his act knowing its consequence, and it has reached it, so it is made like his direct act. Translation: If he placed a burning coal in the road and it burned something, he is liable because he is a transgressor. And if the wind moved it to another place and then it burned something, he is not liable because the wind annulled his act. And it is said that if it is a day of strong wind, he is liable because he did the act knowing its end, and his act has led to that end, so it is considered like his direct act. Explanation: If Zayd placed a fire in the road and someone died by burning, Zayd is liable because it is his transgression of placing fire in the road. And if due to wind the coal flew to another place and someone died by burning, then Zayd is not liable because it is no longer his act but the act of the wind. Some scholars said that if during days when strong wind blows, like the wheat harvesting season, someone placed fire in the road and it flew due to wind and burned something, then the one who placed the fire is liable.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Diyat deals with liability for placing a burning coal (انگارہ) in a public road. The initial ruling: if the coal burns something directly where it was placed, the person who placed it is liable because he is a transgressor (متعدی) by putting a hazard in the public way. The second scenario: if the wind moves the coal to another location and then it causes damage, the general rule is no liability because the wind has 'annulled' (فسخ) the original act. However, there is a qualification (قيل): if it was a notably windy day, such that the person could foresee the coal being blown away, then he is liable. The reasoning is that his act of placing the coal in a windy environment, knowing the likely consequence, is treated as if he directly brought about the harm (بمباشرته). The Urdu commentary explains this with the example of wheat harvesting season when strong winds are typical. This is a refinement of causation (سببیہ): the act must be the proximate cause; an intervening natural event may break the chain unless the actor's knowledge of the risk makes him responsible.

Key Terms
متعدي (muta'addī): A transgressor; one who exceeds proper bounds by placing a hazard in a public space.
مباشرة (mubāsharah): Direct causation; performing an act that directly causes harm.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment; in this context, the wind 'annuls' the original act, severing legal causation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, when is a person who placed a burning coal in a road NOT liable for damage caused after the coal is moved by wind?
A) If the coal was placed during a windy day.
B) If the wind moved the coal on a calm day without foreseeable strong winds.
C) If the damage occurs at night.
D) If the person did not intend to cause harm.

Key Takeaway
A transgressor is liable for direct harm from a placed hazard; wind severs liability unless the wind was foreseeable, in which case his indirect act is treated as direct.

Liability When Hired Workers Cause a Deadly Fall
Ruling on damages from falling balcony when workers are hired

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule of liability for a fatal falling object caused by hired workers, distinguishing before and after handover, and explain the Hanafi use of istihsan in shifting liability.

Core Idea
A hired worker's act causing death stays with them until the work is handed over.

This passage from Kitab al-Diyat addresses a common scenario: hired workers removing a balcony cause it to fall and kill someone. The ruling pivots on whether the work has been completed and handed over. Before handover, the workers are liable because the killing is a direct consequence of their act and not covered by the hire contract. After handover, the owner becomes liable by istihsan, because the act is attributed to the owner as if he performed it himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two time periods
Note the distinction: before the workers finish and hand over the work, and after they finish and hand over. This determines liability.
2
Analyze the before-handover ruling
Liability is on the workers because their act directly caused death; the killing is not part of the hire contract, so the act does not transfer to the owner.
Kaffarah also due on workers because direct killing.
3
Analyze the after-handover ruling
Liability shifts to the owner by istihsan. The contract is valid, workers earned wage, and their act (construction/repair) is transferred to the owner as if he did it.
This departs from qiyas which would keep liability on workers.
4
Understand the istihsan rationale
Qiyas would keep liability on workers always. Istihsan considers the completion and handover as transferring responsibility because the owner benefits from the work.
Istihsan is a stronger equitable principle here.
5
Apply the principle to similar hire scenarios
For any hired task (e.g., repairing a roof, removing a structure), liability follows the same rule: workers liable before handover, owner after handover.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استأجررب الدار العملة لإخراج الجناح أو الظلة فوقع فقتل إنسانا قبل أن يفرغوا من العمل فالضمان عليهم لأن التلف بفعلهم وما لم يفرغوا لم يكن العمل مسلما إلى رب الدار وهذا لأنه انقلب فعلهم قتلا حتى وجبت عليهم الكفارة والقتل غير داخل في عقده فلم ينتقل فعلهم إليه فاقتصر عليهم.
ترجمہ: اور اگر گھر والے نے معماروں کو اجرت پر رکھا روشندان یا چھجہ نکالنے کے لئے پس وہ گر گیا پس اس نے کسی انسان کو قتل کر دیا ان کے کام سے فارغ ہونے سے پہلے تو ضمان معماروں پر ہو گا اور جب تک وہ فارغ نہ ہوں تو کام گھر والے کی طرف سپر د کیا ہوا نہ ہوگا اور یہ اس لئے کہ ان کا فعل قتل سے بدل گیا یہاں تک کہ ان کے اوپر کفارہ واجب ہے اور قتل مستاجر کے عقد میں داخل نہیں ہے تو معماروں کا فعل مستاجر کی جانب منتقل نہ ہوگا تو یہ فعل معماروں پر منحصر رہے گا۔
تشریح: زید نے کچھ معمار اجر رکھے تاکہ وہ روشندان یا چھجہ وغیرہ نکال دیں تو جب تک معمار کام سے نبٹ کر اجرت وغیرہ لے کر یہ زید کے حوالہ نہیں کریں گے جب تک یہ انہیں کی ذمہ داری میں شمار کیا جائے گا اور جب فارغ ہو کر اس کے حوالہ کر دیں تو اب وہ ذمہ دار نہ ہوں گے بلکہ زید خود ذمہ دار ہوگا، لہذا پہلی صورت میں اگر کوئی شخص اس میں دب کر مر جائے تو معماروں پر ضمان ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں زید پر ضمان ہوگا۔
وإن سقط بعد فراغهم فالضمان على رب الدار استحسانا لأنه صح الاستيجار حتى استحقوا الأجر ووقع فعلهم عمارة وإصلاحا فانتقل فعلهم إليه فكأنه فعل بنفسه فلهذا يضمنه.
ترجمہ: اور اگر وہ ان کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد گرا ہے تو بر بناء استحسان رب الدار پر ضمان واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ استیجار صحیح ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ اجرت کے مستحق ہو چکے ہیں اور ان کا فعل تعمیر و اصلاح ہو چکا ہے تو ان کا فعل رب الدار کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے گا گویا کہ رب الدار نے خود یہ کام کیا ہے اسی وجہ سے وہ اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔
And if the owner of the house hired workers to remove the balcony or the awning, and it fell and killed a person before they finished the work, then the liability is upon them because the destruction was by their act, and as long as they have not finished, the work has not been handed over to the owner of the house. And this is because their act turned into killing, such that expiation (kaffarah) is obligatory upon them, and killing is not included in the contract of hire, so their act is not transferred to the hirer, so it remains upon them. Translation: If the house owner hired workers to remove the balcony or awning, and it fell and killed a person before they finished the work, then liability is on the workers. And until they finish, the work is not handed over to the owner. This is because their act turned into killing, so kaffarah is due on them, and killing is not part of the hire contract, so their act is not transferred to the hirer, so it remains upon them. Explanation: Zayd hired some workers to remove the balcony or awning. As long as the workers have not finished and handed over the work to Zayd, they are responsible. When they finish and hand over, they are not responsible; Zayd becomes responsible. So in the first case, if someone dies under it, the workers pay diyat; in the second, Zayd pays. And if it falls after they have finished, then the liability is upon the owner of the house by istihsan, because the hire is valid such that they are entitled to the wage, and their act was construction and repair, so their act is transferred to the owner, as if he did it himself, therefore he is liable. Translation: And if it fell after they finished, then by istihsan liability is on the owner of the house because the hire is valid such that they have become entitled to the wage, and their act was building and repair, so their act is transferred to the owner, as if he did it himself, for that reason he is liable.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Diyat deals with liability when a balcony or awning falls and kills someone while being removed by hired workers. Two stages are distinguished: (1) If the object falls before the workers have finished and handed over the work, liability is on the workers. The reason is that their act is directly causative (turned into killing), and the contract of hire does not cover killing, so their act does not transfer to the hirer (owner). They must also pay kaffarah (expiation) for unlawful killing. (2) If the object falls after the workers have finished and handed over, liability shifts to the owner (رب الدار) by istihsan. This is because the hire contract was valid; the workers have done their job (building/repair) and are entitled to wages. Their act is then attributed to the owner, as if he did it himself. Therefore, the owner must pay diyat. The Urdu commentary illustrates with Zayd and workers, confirming the two scenarios.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference; a departure from analogical reasoning (qiyas) for a more equitable ruling.
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation for unlawful killing; obligatory in addition to diyat when death is caused by a direct act (mubasharah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hired worker's removal of a balcony causes it to fall and kill someone after the work is completed and handed over, who pays diyat?
A) The worker, because he performed the act.
B) The owner of the house, because the act is transferred to him by istihsan.
C) Both the worker and the owner equally.
D) Neither, because it was an accident.

Key Takeaway
Liability for a fatal accident caused by hired workers' acts transfers to the owner only after the work is completed and handed over, due to istihsan.

Liability of Hired Workers for Death Before Completion
Ruling on liability when hired workers cause death before finishing work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when hired workers cause death before completing their work, and identify the proof (dalil) that their act constitutes direct killing (qatl).

Core Idea
Workers bear liability and kaffarah because their act is direct killing, not transferred to the owner under ijarah.

This lesson examines a specific case from Hanafi fiqh: when hired workers cause a person's death before finishing their assigned task, who is liable? The text from Al-Hidayah (via Ashraf ul Hadaya) rules that the workers themselves are liable, not the owner. The reasoning revolves around the nature of the act — it becomes a killing, and killing is not part of the hire contract. We will explore the ruling, its proof via qiyas, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The owner hires workers to remove a skylight or balcony. Before completion, a worker falls and kills someone. Identify the parties: owner (musta'jir) and workers (ujara').
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling is that liability (daman) and expiation (kaffarah) are on the workers, not the owner. The workers must pay blood money (diyah) and perform kaffarah.
This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The work has not been handed over, so the workers' act is still theirs. The act caused death, so it is classified as qatl (killing). Killing is not part of the ijarah contract, so the act does not transfer to the owner.
The key condition is that the work is not yet handed over (taslim).
4
Identify the proof (dalil)
The obligation of kaffarah on the workers proves that their act is direct killing. This is an instance of qiyas: after the event, the act is analogous to intentional killing regarding liability.
The dalil is the wajib nature of kaffarah, which is only due on the direct perpetrator.
5
Contrast with the completed scenario
Once the work is finished and handed over to the owner, any subsequent death caused by the structure is the owner's responsibility. The act transfers to the owner upon handover.
This contrast reinforces the conditionality of the ruling on completion.

Source Text

ولو استأجررب الدار العملة لإخراج الجناح أو الظلة فوقع فقتل إنسانا قبل أن يفرغوا من العمل فالضمان عليهم لأن التلف بفعلهم وما لم يفرغوا لم يكن العمل مسلما إلى رب الدار وهذا لأنه انقلب فعلهم قتلا حتى وجبـت عـلـيـهـم الـكفارة والقتل غير داخل في عقده فلم ينتقل فعلهم إليه فاقتصر عليهم ترجمہ اور اگر گھر والے نے معماروں کو اجرت پر رکھا روشندان یا چھجہ نکالنے کے لئے پس وہ گر گیا پس اس نے کسی انسان کو قتل کر دیا ان کے کام سے فارغ ہونے سے پہلے تو ضمان معماروں پر ہو گا اور جب تک وہ فارغ نہ ہوں تو کام گھر والے کی طرف سپر د کیا ہوا نہ ہوگا اور یہ اس لئے کہ ان کا فعل قتل سے بدل گیا یہاں تک کہ ان کے اوپر کفارہ واجب ہے اور قتل مستاجر کے عقد میں داخل نہیں ہے تو معماروں کا فعل مستاجر کی جانب منتقل نہ ہوگا تو یہ فعل معماروں پر منحصر رہے گا۔ تشریح زید نے کچھ معمارا جیر رکھے تاکہ وہ روشندان یا چھجہ وغیرہ نکال دیں تو جب تک معمار کام سے نبٹ کر اجرت وغیرہ لے کر یہ زید کے حوالہ نہیں کریں گے جب تک یہ انہیں کی ذمہ داری میں شمار کیا جائے گا اور جب فارغ ہو کر اس کے حوالہ کر دیں تو اب وہ ذمہ دارنہ ہوں گے بلکہ زید خود ذمہ دار ہوگا، لہذا پہلی صورت میں اگر کوئی شخص اس میں دب کر مر جائے تو معماروں پر ضمان ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں زید پر منہان ہوگا۔ کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں معماروں کا فعل ہی قتل شمار کیا جائے گا جس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفارہ بھی معماروں پر واجب ہوتا ہے حالانکہ زید نے عقد اجارہ کیا عقد قتل نہیں کیا تھا اس لئے ان کا فعل انہیں پر منحصر رہے گا آگے دوسری صورت کا بیان ہے۔
And if the owner of the house hires workers to remove a skylight or a balcony, and (one of them) falls and kills a person before they finish the work, then the liability is upon them because the destruction is by their act, and as long as they have not finished, the work has not been handed over to the owner of the house. And this is because their act turned into killing such that expiation is obligatory upon them, and killing is not included in his contract, so their act does not transfer to him; thus it remains confined to them.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling on liability (daman) when hired workers (e.g., builders) cause a death before completing their assigned task. The owner hired them to remove a skylight or balcony. If they fall and kill someone, the liability is on the workers, not the owner. The reasoning: the workers' act has become a killing (qatl), evidenced by the fact that kaffarah (expiation) is obligatory on them. Since killing is not part of the hiring contract (ijarah), their act does not transfer to the owner. Thus, they bear full responsibility. The Urdu commentary further explains using the example of Zaid hiring workers: until they finish and hand over the work, any harm is on them; after handover, it's on Zaid. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, found in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Legal liability to compensate for harm or death; here it implies payment of blood money (diyah) or kaffarah.
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hire where one party pays another for service or use of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kaffarah (expiation) wajib on the workers in this case?
A) Because the owner forced them to work
B) Because their act turned into killing and they are directly responsible
C) Because the contract includes killing
D) Because they were paid for the work

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, hired workers bear liability for death caused before completing and handing over work, because their act remains their own direct killing until transfer.

Liability for Death After Work Completion
Ruling on liability after work completion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability after work completion and explain the istihsan reasoning that transfers liability to the owner.

Core Idea
After handover, the owner is liable because the workers' constructive act transfers to him by istihsan.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the chapter of diyat (blood money): after hired workers finish their job and hand over the work, if a subsequent death occurs (e.g., a wall falls), who bears the liability? The Hanafi ruling, based on istihsan, places liability on the owner. Understanding this ruling requires grasping how the nature of the act (constructive vs. destructive) and the completion of the contract affect legal responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the passage carefully: workers are hired to demolish or repair a structure. After they finish and leave, the structure falls and kills someone. The ruling states liability is on the owner (rabb al-dar) by istihsan.
This contrasts with the scenario where death occurs during work, where the workers themselves may be liable.
2
Understand the istihsan reasoning
The key reasoning: the hire contract was valid (workers earned wages), and their act was 'building and repair' (constructive), not killing. Therefore, the act is attributed to the owner as if he did it himself. This overrides qiyas that would keep liability on the workers.
Istihsan here is used to achieve a more equitable outcome: the owner benefits from the work and should bear the risk after handover.
3
Trace the transfer of act
The passage explicitly states 'their act transfers to him, as if he did it himself.' This transfer (naql) is the legal mechanism: once the workers finish, their constructive action becomes legally the owner's action.
This transfer is not physical but legal (hukmi), based on the owner's ownership of the premises and benefit from the work.
4
Compare with strict qiyas
If strict qiyas were applied, the workers would be liable since they physically performed the act that led to death. But istihsan sets aside qiyas because the act's classification as 'building' (constructive) and the completion of the contract shift liability.
This is an example of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy): the act is analogized to the owner's own act once the workers are no longer in control.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن سقط بعد فراغهم فالضمان على رب الدار استحسانا لأنه صح الاستيجار حتى استحقوا الأجر ووقع فعلهم عمارة وإصلاحا فانتقل فعلهم إليه فكأنه فعل بنفسه فلهذا يضمنه. ترجمہ اور اگر وہ انکے فارغ ہونے کے بعد گرا ہے تو بر بناء استحسان رب الدار پر ضمان واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ استیجار صیح ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ اجرت کے مستحق ہو چکے ہیں اور ان کا فعل تعمیر و اصلاح ہو چکا ہے تو ان کا فعل رب الدار کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے گا گویا کہ رب ابدار نے خود یہ کام کیا ہے اسی وجہ سے وہ اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ تشریح اس صورت میں معماروں کا فعل زید کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ فعل تعمیر ومرمت ہے قتل نہیں ہے تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا نے خود یہ کام کیا ہے جس سے کوئی مر گیا تو ضمان اسی پر واجب ہوگا۔
And if it falls after they have finished, then the liability is upon the owner of the house by istihsan, because the hire was valid such that they became entitled to the wage, and their act was building and repair, so their act transfers to him, as if he did it himself; therefore he is liable for it.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage presents the second scenario: after the workers finish their job and hand over the work (e.g., the balcony is removed), if the structure later falls and kills someone, the liability shifts to the owner (rabb al-dar). The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The reasoning: the hire contract was valid, the workers earned their wage, and their act was one of building and repair, not killing. Therefore, their act is attributed to the owner, as if he did it himself. The Urdu commentary paraphrases this, noting that once work is complete, the workers' act is no longer theirs but belongs to the owner. This is from Kitab al-Diyat in Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that sets aside strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason for shifting liability from workers to owner after completion in the Hanafi ruling?
A) The workers have no money
B) The owner ordered the killing
C) The workers' act is considered building, which transfers to the owner
D) The workers are no longer present

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, after workers complete and hand over constructive work, the owner becomes liable for subsequent death by istihsan, overriding the qiyas that would keep liability on the workers.

Liability for Spilling Water in Public Path
Ruling on liability for water harm in public path

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for death caused by water in a public path and explain the basis of ta'addi.

Core Idea
Spilling water in a public path constitutes ta'addi, making one liable for any harm caused.

In this short passage from the chapter on diyat, the Hanafi school establishes a clear principle: causing harm through wrongful action in a public thoroughfare incurs liability. The text expands the ruling from pouring water to sprinkling and performing wudu, all of which can create a hazard for passersby.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? The passage mentions pouring, sprinkling, or performing wudu in a public path. The ruling is that if a person or animal dies as a result, the doer is liable (daman wajib).
The hukm level is wajib, meaning liability is obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the underlying reason: the act constitutes ta'addi (transgression) because it causes harm to passersby. This is a form of qiyas based on the general principle that wrongful harm must be compensated.
No specific Quran or hadith is cited; the reasoning is talil (causal explanation).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does ta'addi establish liability? The act of placing water in a public way without necessity is inherently harmful to passersby, making it wrongful. Harm caused by a wrongful act triggers liability (daman).
The key is that the act is not merely the cause but is done without justification, i.e., ta'addi.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
The ruling is not limited to deliberate pouring; it includes sprinkling and washing (wudu) because they also create a hazard. The common element is causing harm to passersby.
This expansion shows the principle's flexibility: any act that wrongfully endangers the public incurs liability.
5
Evaluate the authority
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah (the core transmitted texts) and is agreed upon across the Hanafi school and even other schools (muttafaq alayh). It is a well-established principle.
No ikhtilaf is reported, strengthening its reliability for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا إذا صب الماء فى الطريق فعطب به إنسان أو دابة وكذا إذا رش الماء أو توضأ لأنه متعد فيه بإلحاق الضرر بالمارة ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی (ضمان واجب ہو گا ) جب کہ راستہ میں پانی ڈالا پس اس سے کوئی انسان یا چوپایہ ہلاک ہو گیا اور ایسے ہی جب کہ راستہ میں پانی چھڑ کا یا وضو کیا اس لئے کہ اس میں متعدی ہے گزرنے والوں کے ساتھ ضرر کو لاحق کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر زید نے راستہ میں پانی ڈال دیا ، یا وضو کیا یا چھڑکاؤ کیا اور اس میں کوئی پھسل کر مر گیا تو ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ زید کی جانب سے تعدی پائی گئی ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے گذرنے والوں کو ضرر پہنچایا ہے۔
And likewise if one pours water in the road and a person or animal is harmed by it, and likewise if one sprinkles water or performs ablution, because he is a transgressor by causing harm to passersby.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage deals with liability for death caused by water on a public road. If someone pours, sprinkles, or performs wudu in a public path, and a person or animal slips and dies, the person is liable (daman wajib). The reason: it constitutes transgression (ta'addi) by causing harm to passersby. The Urdu commentary gives the example of Zaid who pours water or does wudu in the road, and someone slips and dies — Zaid is liable because of his transgression. This ruling is from Kitab al-Diyat, and is based on the general principle that causing harm wrongfully incurs liability.

Key Terms
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or wrongful action that causes harm; here, it is the legal basis for liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because water is dangerous
B) Because they acted wrongfully (ta'addi) by harming passersby
C) Because they owned the water
D) Because they were walking

Key Takeaway
Spilling water in a public path that causes death makes one liable for diyah because the act is wrongful (ta'addi) and harms others.

No Liability for Residents in Non-Through Streets
Exception: no liability for resident's water in a private street

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a resident's liability in a non-through street and explain the Hanafi basis for the exception.

Core Idea
In a private cul-de-sac, residents may pour water without liability – necessity of residence overrides general tort.

The previous lesson established that pouring water in a public thoroughfare causing death incurs liability. This lesson presents a critical exception: when the same act occurs in a non-through street by a resident, there is no liability. We explore the rationale, which hinges on the rights of residents and the concept of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Location
The act is pouring water, sitting, or placing belongings. The location is a non-through street (sikkah ghayr nafidhah).
This is the key distinguishing factor from the public street ruling.
2
Determine the Ruling
The ruling is that there is no liability (daman) even if the act causes death.
The text says 'بخلاف' (contrary to) indicating an exception.
3
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is based on custom and necessity: residents have the right to perform such acts because they are among the necessities of residence (darurat al-sukna).
The analogy is to a shared courtyard where each partner may do necessary things.
4
Understand the Talil (Rationale)
The rationale is that the act is within the permissible use of the private street. There is no transgression because the resident is using the street for legitimate domestic needs.
This is a form of istihsan or urf-based reasoning.
5
Distinguish from Public Street
In a public thoroughfare, liability applies regardless of residency. The exception only applies to residents in a non-through street.
This distinction is crucial for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف ما إذا فعل ذالك في سكة غير نافذة وهو من أهلها أو قعد أو وضع متاعه لأن لكل واحد أن يفعل ذالك فيها لكونه من ضرورات السكنى كما في الدار المشتركة ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ اس نے گلی میں کیا ہو جو عام نہ ہو اور وہ اس کے باشندوں میں سے ہو یا وہ بٹھایا اس نے اپنے سامان کو رکھا اس لئے کہ ہر ایک کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ وہ اس میں یہ کام کرے اس کے سکنی کی ضروریات میں سے ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسے مشترک حویلی میں۔ تشریح یہ گفتگو عام راستہ کی ہے اور اگر عام راستہ نہ ہو بلکہ سکہ غیر نافذ ہ ہو تو اس گلی میں رہنے والوں میں سے اگر کسی نے راستہ میں پانی ڈالا یا وہاں بیٹھا یا وہاں اپنا سامان رکھا جس سے پھسل کر کوئی مر گیا تو اس پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ کام یہاں ان کی ضروریات میں داخل ہے جیسے مشترک حویلی میں ہر شریک کو یہ حق ہوتا ہے کہ وہاں اپنی ضروریات کو پورا کرے، اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہوگا۔
Contrary to if he does that in a non-through street and he is one of its residents, or sits, or places his belongings, because everyone has the right to do that in it, as it is among the necessities of residence, just like in a shared courtyard.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage provides an exception to the previous ruling. If the action (pouring water, sitting, placing goods) is done in a non-through street (sikkah ghayr nafidhah) by a resident, there is no liability even if it causes death. The reason: such actions are considered necessities of residence (darurat al-sukna), and each resident has the right to use the street for these purposes. The Urdu commentary compares it to a shared courtyard (dar mushtarakah) where each partner may do necessary things. Thus, if a resident pours water in a cul-de-sac and someone slips and dies, the resident is not liable because it falls under permissible use. This is from Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
سكة غير نافذة (sikkah ghayr nafidhah): A non-through street or cul-de-sac; a private way used only by residents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a resident not liable for death caused by water in a non-through street?
A) Because the street is not public
B) Because residents have the right to use the street for necessities of residence
C) Because water is not dangerous
D) Because the resident owns the street

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, residents of a non-through street are not liable for damages from ordinary domestic use, as it is a necessity of residence.

Liability for Death Caused by Construction Workers
Commentary: Construction worker's act transferred to employer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah liability when a hired worker causes death during construction, and explain the legal basis for transferring the act to the employer.

Core Idea
The act of a hired builder is attributed to the employer because it is construction, not murder.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary explains a key principle in diyat: when a person hires workers for construction or repair, and that work accidentally causes someone's death, the liability shifts to the employer. This is because the workers' act is not direct killing but an indirect act of construction. Understanding this transfer of liability is crucial for determining who owes blood money.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
Recognize that Zaid hires builders for construction/repair; the builders' act (e.g., dropping a brick) causes death.
The act must be classified as construction or repair, not an intentional killing.
2
Understand the legal transfer
The act is transferred to Zaid because construction/repair is not classified as killing; it is an ordinary act attributed to the commissioner.
This transfer is based on the principle that the worker is an instrument (aalah) for the employer.
3
Distinguish direct vs. indirect causation
Unlike direct homicide where the killer bears liability, here the causation is indirect through authorized work.
If the worker had intentionally killed, the act would be his own, not transferred.
4
Apply the ruling
Conclude that Zaid must pay diyah (blood money) to the heirs of the deceased as the liable party.
The ruling is specific to accidental deaths during lawful construction/repair.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح اس صورت میں معماروں کا فعل زید کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ فعل تعمیر ومرمت ہے قتل نہیں ہے تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا نے خود یہ کام کیا ہے جس سے کوئی مر گیا تو ضمان اسی پر واجب ہوگا۔
Commentary: In this case, the act of the builders is transferred to Zaid, because the act is construction and repair, not killing. So it becomes as if he himself did this work. If someone died due to it, the blood money is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining a ruling about liability for death caused by construction workers. The principle is that if Zaid hires builders to do construction or repair work, and that work leads to someone's death, the liability transfers to Zaid. This is because the workers' act is not direct killing but an act of construction, which is attributed to the person who commissioned it. Therefore, Zaid must pay the blood money (diyah).

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay compensation (blood money) for harm caused.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a victim of accidental killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In the Hanafi ruling, if a builder hired by Zaid accidentally causes a death during construction, who is liable for blood money?

B) Zaid (the employer)
C) Both equally
D) No one

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diyat, the act of a hired constructor is attributed to the employer, making the employer liable for accidental death caused by the work.

No Liability for Water Spill in Private Alley by Resident
Ruling: Resident of a dead-end alley not liable for water spill

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for water spill in a private non-thoroughfare alley and explain why the resident is not liable based on necessity of residence.

Core Idea
In a private alley, residents' necessary actions like spilling water incur no liability.

You learned that spilling water on a public road causing harm makes one liable. But what if the alley is a dead-end shared by residents? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the nature of the space: a private alley is akin to a shared courtyard where residents have rights. This lesson explores that exception and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general rule
First, recognize that the general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that if you cause harm by spilling water on a public road, you are liable for damages. This passage presents an exception.
The general rule is not explicitly given here but is understood from the context (the passage says 'contrary to if...').
2
Spot the exception condition
The exception applies when the act occurs in a sikkah ghayr nafidhah (a non-thoroughfare alley) and the doer is a resident of that alley. Even sitting or placing belongings is included.
The key is that the alley is not a public through-street.
3
Understand the rationale: necessity of residence
The reason for no liability is that these actions are considered from the necessities of residence. Residents have the right to use the alley for normal living activities.
This is analogized to partners in a shared courtyard (dar mushtarakah) where each may use the space for his needs.
4
Apply the ruling
If a resident pours water, sits, or places goods in a private alley, and someone slips and dies, there is no liability because the act is not transgression.
The principle is that what is necessary for habitation is permitted even if incidental harm occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف ما إذا فعل ذالك في سكة غير نافذة وهو من أهلها أو قعد أو وضع متاعه لأن لكل واحد أن يفعل ذالك فيها لكونه من ضرورات السكنى كما في الدار المشتركة ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ اس نے گلی میں کیا ہو جو عام نہ ہو اور وہ اس کے باشندوں میں سے ہو یا وہ بٹھایا اس نے اپنے سامان کو رکھا اس لئے کہ ہر ایک کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ وہ اس میں یہ کام کرے اس کے سکنی کی ضروریات میں سے ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسے مشترک حویلی میں۔ تشریح یہ گفتگو عام راستہ کی ہے اور اگر عام راستہ نہ ہو بلکہ سکہ غیر نافذ ہ ہو تو اس گلی میں رہنے والوں میں سے اگر کسی نے راستہ میں پانی ڈالا یا وہاں بیٹھا یا وہاں اپنا سامان رکھا جس سے پھسل کر کوئی مر گیا تو اس پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ کام یہاں ان کی ضروریات میں داخل ہے جیسے مشترک حویلی میں ہر شریک کو یہ حق ہوتا ہے کہ وہاں اپنی ضروریات کو پورا کرے، اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہوگا۔
Contrary to if he did that in a non-thoroughfare alley and he is from its residents, or he sat or placed his belongings, because each one has the right to do that in it since it is from the necessities of residence, like in a shared courtyard. Translation: Contrary to the case when he did this in an alley that is not public and he is from its residents, or he sat or placed his belongings, because each person has the right to do this in it due to it being from the necessities of residence, like in a shared courtyard. Commentary: This discussion is about a public road. If it is not a public road but a non-thoroughfare alley, and one of the residents poured water, sat, or placed belongings there, and someone slipped and died, then there is no liability. Because these actions are within their necessities, just as in a shared courtyard each partner has the right to fulfill his needs there, similarly here.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage introduces an exception to the general liability rule. The matn states that the ruling of liability for water spilling is different if it occurs in a sikkah ghayr nafidhah (a dead-end alley that is not a public thoroughfare) and the one who spills is a resident. In such a case, there is no liability even if someone dies from slipping. The reason is that these actions (pouring water, sitting, placing goods) are considered necessities of residence. Every resident has the right to do them, just as partners in a shared courtyard (dar mushtarakah) have the right to use the common space for their needs. Therefore, these actions are not considered transgression (ta'addi) and thus do not create liability. This is based on the principle that what is necessary for habitation is permitted even if it causes incidental harm.

Key Terms
سکه غیر نافذہ (sikkah ghayr nafidhah): A dead-end alley that is not a public through-street, shared by residents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a resident of a private dead-end alley pours water and a passerby slips and dies, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The resident must pay blood money
B) The resident is not liable
C) The resident is partially liable
D) The passerby's family files a complaint

Key Takeaway
Residents of private alleys are not liable for water spills and similar necessary acts because they are exercising their right of residence, not committing transgression.

Liability for Water Sprinkling: The Role of Custom (Adah)
Ruling: No liability for small water splash unless customarily slippery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that liability for water sprinkling depends on whether the amount customarily causes slipping, and distinguish between large and small amounts.

Core Idea
No liability for a small water splash unless it customarily causes slipping.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the mashayikh (senior Hanafi scholars) that refines liability for water sprinkling on a public road. The ruling hinges on custom (adah): if the amount sprinkled is so small that it does not customarily cause slipping, there is no liability even if someone slips. This illustrates how 'urf (custom) can condition obligations in Hanafi fiqh. We will explore the reasoning and see how this ruling applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling on water sprinkling
The passage refines a broader rule. Implicitly, sprinkling water that causes slipping leads to liability. Identify the baseline before the refinement.
2
Identify the condition for liability
The passage conditions liability on the amount of water being large enough to customarily cause slipping. Note the key term 'adah (custom) as a condition.
3
Apply the condition to small amounts
For small amounts (as is customary for settling dust), there is no liability. The custom determines the threshold.
4
Recognize the authority level
This ruling comes from the mashayikh (later scholars), not the earliest texts. This shows how the school develops over time.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin
5
Connect to usul: 'adah (custom) as a source
Understand that 'urf (custom) is a recognized source of law in the Hanafi school. It can define conditions and affect substantive rulings like liability.
Customary practice (adah) is akin to 'urf in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا هذا إذارش ماء كثيرا بحيث يزلق به عادة أما إذا رش ماء قليلا كما هو المعتاد والظاهر أنه لايزلق به عادة لا يضمن ترجمہ مشائخ نے فرمایا یہ (ضمان ) جب ہے جب کہ اس نے زیادہ پانی چھڑ کا ہو جس سے عادہ پھسلن پیدا ہو جائے بہر حال جبکہ تھوڑا پانی چھڑ کا جیسا کہ یہ معتاد ہے اور ظاہر یہ ہو کہ اس سے عادہ پھسلن نہیں ہوئی تو وہ ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح صرف اسی وقت ضمان ہو گا جب کہ زیادہ پانی چھڑک دے جس سے ریٹن پیدا ہو جائے ورنہ اگر اتنا تھوڑا پانی چھڑ کا جس سے ریٹن نہ ہو تو پھر چھڑکنے والے پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
They (the mashayikh) said: This (liability) is when he sprinkles a lot of water such that it customarily causes slipping. But if he sprinkles a little water, as is customary, and it appears that it does not customarily cause slipping, then he is not liable. Translation: The mashayikh said: This (liability) is when he sprinkled a lot of water such that slipping customarily results. However, if he sprinkled little water, as is customary, and it is apparent that it does not customarily cause slipping, then he is not liable. Commentary: Liability occurs only when he sprinkles a lot of water such that it creates slipperiness. Otherwise, if he sprinkles so little water that there is no slipperiness, then the one who sprinkled is not liable.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage refines the general ruling about liability for water sprinkling. The mashayikh (senior scholars) state that the ruling regarding liability applies only when a large amount of water is sprinkled such that it customarily causes people to slip. If only a small amount is sprinkled, as is normal for settling dust (a common practice), and it is apparent that it does not ordinarily cause slipping, then the person is not liable even if someone slips and dies. The key factor is the customary (adah) occurrence of slipping. The commentary clarifies that liability hinges on whether the amount of water is sufficient to create a slippery condition (ratan). This shows that the Hanafi school considers 'urf (custom) in determining liability.

Key Terms
عادہ (adah): Customary practice; what is usual and normative in a given context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always
B) Only if the water causes impurity
C) Only if the amount is large enough to customarily cause slipping
D) Only if done intentionally

Key Takeaway
Liability for water sprinkling hinges on whether the amount customarily causes slipping; small customary amounts incur no liability.

Intentional Crossing by Victim: Liability of Spiller
Ruling: Victim's intentional crossing removes spiller's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of liability when a victim deliberately exposes themselves to harm, distinguishing between the presence of an alternative path and compulsion.

Core Idea
A victim's deliberate act breaks the causal chain; the spiller is only liable when the victim has no alternative.

In Hanafi tort law, not every harmful outcome leads to liability. This lesson explores a key principle: when the victim's own deliberate act is the direct cause of the harm, the person who created the hazardous condition may be absolved. We examine the ruling from Al-Hidayah where a person sprinkles water on part of a road and the victim intentionally walks on it, slips, and dies. The ruling turns on whether the victim had a choice and the nature of the cause (illah) versus a mere means (sabab).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify the act: the spiller pours water on part of a road; the victim intentionally walks on that spot and dies. The ruling in the matn is that the spiller is not liable.
2
Determine the condition for the ruling
The commentary clarifies that this ruling applies only when the wet area is partial (part of the road). If the entire road is wet, the spiller is liable. Note the key condition: whether the victim had a practical alternative.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The Hanafi principle is that when a valid cause (illatun salihah) is present—here, the victim's deliberate act as a free agent—it bears the ruling. The spiller's act is merely a means (sabab) and does not attract liability. This principle is derived from rational reasoning (aqli).
The cause must be sahihah (valid) meaning the agent is fully capable and aware.
4
Apply the analogy to wood
The same rule applies if someone places wood blocking part of the road. If the victim deliberately walks into it, no liability; if the whole road is blocked, the placer is liable because the victim is compelled.
This demonstrates that the rule is not limited to water but applies to any object placed on a road.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling: no liability on the spiller if the victim deliberately crosses a partial wet spot with knowledge and an alternative exists. Liability only if the entire road is wet (or similarly blocked), making the victim compelled.
This is from the zahir al-riwayah and is relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تعمد المرور في موضع صب الماء فسقط لا يضمن الراش لأنه صاحب علة وقيل هذا إذا رش بعض الطريق لأنه يجد موضعا للمرور ولا أثر للماء فيه فإذا تعمد المرور على موضع صب الماء مع علمه بذالك لم يكن على الراش شيء وإن رش جميع الطريق يضمن لأنه مضطر في المرور وكذا الحكم في الخشبة الموضوعة فى الطريق فى أخذها جميعه أو بعضه ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے پانی گرنے کی جگہ گزرنے کا تعمد کیا ہے پس وہ گر گیا تو چھڑکنے والا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ گذرنے والا صاحب علت ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ ( عدم وجوب ضمان ) اس وقت ہے جب کہ وہ راستہ کے کچھ حصہ پر چھڑ کے اس لئے کہ ( گذرنے والا ) گذرنے کی جگہ پائے گا حالانکہ اس جگہ میں پانی کا اثر نہیں ہے پس جب اس نے ( گذرنے والے نے ) پانی گرنے کی جگہ پر سے گذرنے کا ارادہ کیا اس کے جانے کے باوجود اس کو (پانی گرنے کو) تو چھڑکاؤ کرنے والے پر کچھ نہ ہوگا اور اگر اس نے پورے راستہ پر چھڑکاؤ کیا تو وہ ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ ( گذرنے والا ) مرور میں مجبور ہے اور یہی حکم ہے راستہ میں رکھی ہوئی لکڑی میں لکڑی کے کھیرنے میں پورے راستہ کو یا بعض راستہ کو ۔ تشریح زید نے جہاں پانی چھڑ کا ہے وہ پورے راستہ پر نہیں ہے بلکہ کچھ راستہ پر ہے جہاں کو خالد گذ رسکتا ہے لیکن وہ قصد امونچھوں کو تاؤ دیتے ہوئے اس جگہ کو گذر رہا ہے جہاں پانی ہے تو زید پر منمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں گذر نیوالے کا فعل علت ہے اور چھٹر کئے والے مافعل سبب ہے۔ اور اصول یہ ہے کہ جب علت کے اندر یہ صلاحیت ہو کہ حکم کی اضافت اس کی طرف ہو سکے تو پھر سبب اور شرط پر ضمان نہیں ہوا کرتا اور یہاں مار کا فعل علت صالحہ ہے کیونکہ یہ فائل مختار کا فعل ہے (و فصلناه في درس الحسامی) ہاں اگر زید نے پورے راستہ میں پانی چھڑک رکھا ہے تو زید ضامن ہوگا کیونکہ اپنی ضرورت میں جانے کے لئے خالد مجبور تھا اور وہ زید کے فعل کی وجہ سے گر گیا اور مر گیا تو زید پر ضمان ہوگا۔ اسی طرح اگر زید نے راستہ میں لکڑیاں ڈال رکھی ہیں تو بھی یہی تفصیل اور حکم ہے۔
And if he intentionally passed through the place where water was poured and fell, the sprinkler is not liable, because the passerby is the one with the cause (illah). And it was said: This (no liability) is when he sprinkled part of the road, because the passerby finds a place to pass where there is no effect of water. So when he intends to pass over the place of water with knowledge, then nothing on the sprinkler. But if he sprinkled the entire road, then he is liable, because the passerby is compelled in passing. Similar is the ruling for a piece of wood placed in the road, whether it takes up the whole road or part of it. Commentary: Where Zaid sprinkled water is not the entire road but part, and Khalid could pass elsewhere but deliberately goes over the wet spot. Then no liability on Zaid, because the passerby's act is the cause (illah) and the sprinkler's act is only a means (sabab). The principle: when the cause can bear attribution of the ruling, then liability does not fall on the means or condition. And here the passerby's act is a valid cause because it is the act of a free agent. (We have detailed this in the lesson of Al-Husami). However, if Zaid sprinkled the entire road, then Zaid is liable because Khalid is compelled to pass there. Similarly, if Zaid placed wood in the road, the same detail applies.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where the victim deliberately walks into the wet area. The matn states that if a person intentionally passes through the exact spot where water is spilled knowing it is wet, and then slips and dies, the sprinkler is not liable. The reason given is that the victim's deliberate act makes him the 'owner of the cause' (sahib al-illah). The commentary elaborates that this applies only if part of the road is wet and the victim could have avoided it; then the victim's choice is the direct cause (illatun salihah). If the entire road is wet, the victim is compelled (mudtarr) to walk on it, so the sprinkler is liable. The same rule applies if wood is placed across part or all of the road. The Hanafi principle is that if the direct cause (illah) is an act of a free agent, liability does not fall on the mere means (sabab) or condition. Thus, the victim's intentional crossing breaks the causal chain, unless there is no alternative.

Key Terms
علت صالحہ (illatun salihah): A valid cause that can bear attribution of the legal ruling; here, the victim's deliberate act.
سبب (sabab): A means or instrument that contributes to the outcome but is not the direct cause.
مضطر (mudtarr): One who is compelled, having no reasonable alternative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The victim (no one liable)

D) The municipality

Key Takeaway
If a victim deliberately exposes themselves to a hazard when an alternative exists, their own act is the legal cause; the person who created the hazard is not liable.

Liability for Spilling on Shop Forecourt with Permission
Ruling: commander liable by istihsan for spill on forecourt with permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when water is spilled on a forecourt with the owner's permission and apply the principle that the commander is liable by istihsan.

Core Idea
Liability follows the commander, not the doer, by istihsan when the act is done with permission.

In Hanafi law, the liability for harm caused by an act can shift from the actual doer to the one who commanded the act, especially when the doer is merely an instrument. This lesson examines a specific case: if a person sprinkles water on a shop's forecourt with the owner's permission, and someone slips and dies, the commander (aamir) bears the liability. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), which overrides the general qiyas that would place liability on the doer. Let's unpack the details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
First, identify the action (sprinkling water on a forecourt), the doer (Qah), the commander (Zaid), and the location (shop forecourt with owner's permission).
The location is 'fina'' – the area immediately in front of the shop, distinct from the public road.
2
Determine the default ruling (qiyas)
Under qiyas, the doer (Qah) would normally be liable for any harm directly caused by his act. Consider why that is the default rule.
Qiyas: whoever directly causes harm is liable.
3
Apply istihsan to override qiyas
Istihsan is applied here to transfer liability to the commander (Zaid) because he gave the order and the doer was merely following instructions.
The commander is considered the principal; the doer is an instrument (mujarrad fi'l).
4
State the ruling
By istihsan, the liability (daman) is wajib upon the commander alone, not on the doer.
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولورش فناء حانوت بإذن صاحبه فضمان ما عطب على الآمر استحسانا ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے دکان کی فناء میں مالک دکان کی اجازت سے پانی چھڑ کا تو جو چیز وہاں ہلاک ہوگی استحسانا اس کا ضمان آمر پر ہوگا۔ تشریح زید نے قہ کو حکم دیا کہ اس کی دکان کے سامنے سڑک پر نہیں بلکہ اس کی فناء میں پانی چھڑک دے اس نے چھڑک دیا تو اگر کوئی شخص یا جانور پھس کر مر گیا تو قہ پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا بلکہ زید پر ضمان ہوگا کیونکہ زید نے اس کام کا حکم دیا تھا اور قہ تو مجرد فعل ہے اس لئے آمر ضامن ہے۔
And if he sprinkles water in the forecourt (fina') of a shop with the owner's permission, then the liability for what perishes is upon the commander (aamir) by istihsan. Translation: And if he sprinkles water in the forecourt of a shop with the permission of the shop owner, then the liability for what perishes there is upon the commander by istihsan. Commentary: Zaid ordered Qah (someone) to sprinkle water in his shop's forecourt (fina'), not on the road. Qah did so. If a person or animal slips and dies, liability is not on Qah but on Zaid, because Zaid gave the command, and Qah is merely the agent (mujarrad fi'l). Therefore, the commander (aamir) is liable.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: someone sprinkles water on the forecourt (fina') of a shop with the owner's permission. If someone or something perishes as a result, the liability is upon the one who commanded the sprinkling (al-aamir), not the actual doer. This is established by istihsan (juristic preference). The commentary clarifies: Zaid commands Qah to sprinkle water on Zaid's shop's forecourt. Qah does so. If a person or animal slips and dies, Qah is not liable because he was following orders; instead, Zaid is liable because he gave the command and the act is attributed to him. This is based on the principle that the commander (aamir) is the principal, and the doer is merely an instrument, so liability follows the one who initiated the action.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The forecourt or area immediately in front of a shop, not part of the public road.
آمر (aamir): The person who commands or orders an action; the principal.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departure from qiyas for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qah, the doer
B) Zaid, the commander
C) Both equally
D) No one

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when an act is done on a forecourt with permission, the commander (aamir) is liable by istihsan, not the doer.
